<!-- policy: When closing a task, remove its entire block. History lives in git log per the tasks.md spec. -->
<!-- policy: Optional `**Status**:` field with allowed values `shipped`, `in-progress`, `blocked`. Consumed by `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion` (P0 watchdog filed in #346): explicit `shipped` + at least one merged PR named after the task ID is the operator-controlled fast path for auto-removal; `in-progress` or `blocked` vetoes auto-removal regardless of merged PRs. Absent field falls back to heuristics (acceptance-checkboxes + merged-PR title match). Format-agnostic — works identically for single-file `TASKS.md` and per-task `tasks/<id>.md` once that migration ships (filed as P2 follow-up of `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion`). -->
<!-- policy: Investor / product-manager / growth-analyst personas only run when **Tags** contains business, growth, revenue, customer, or pricing. -->
<!-- policy: Every term used here must appear in vision.md § Glossary or be sourced from a cited paper. New jargon → glossary entry in the same commit. -->
<!-- policy: Per constitutional rule #9 (pre-registered hypothesis-driven development — iron rule), every new task entry MUST include — in addition to the existing Details / Files / Verification / Acceptance / Risk fields — a runnable Measurement command (shell / OTEL query / CI script that produces the metric) and an explicit Pivot threshold (the value below which the *approach* is abandoned, not just the change reverted). The rule is iron: no exemption for bugfixes, refactors, or "small" fixes — a bugfix declares the stability metric (error rate, recurrence count, MTTR, etc.) it expects to move and by how much. If the metric source doesn't exist yet, ship a preparation PR first that lands the instrumentation. Vanity metrics (counts that always go up — LOC, commits, hours, tasks-in-flight) and post-hoc metrics (chosen after the result) are forbidden. Existing tasks predating rule #9 are retrofitted under task `rule-9-backfill-existing-tasks`. -->

<!-- policy: Per constitutional rule #7 (chaos engineering), every new novel package's README and every new user-story includes a "Failure modes & chaos verification" section with steady-state hypothesis, blast radius, operator escape hatch, and a failure-mode table (failure mode | trigger / fault axis | expected behavior — loud-crash-supervisor-restart / circuit-break-and-notify / graceful-degrade | chaos test). -->

## P0

<!-- Operator directive 2026-05-08: shift Minsky's product identity from "repo-rooted stack" to "global, context-aware CLI". The two blocks immediately below capture the remaining shift: (1) make `minsky` self-bootstrap on a fresh machine — auto-detect Claude exhaustion and install the local-LLM stack with one confirm prompt; (2) polish the `minsky` (no-args) UX so it reads context, suggests actions, and asks for confirmation. README's "Not a global CLI" disclaimer is retired in the same PR that lands (2). The original (0) — clean up the WIP merge backlog so the other-machine `git pull` produces a coherent main — shipped: PRs #324 / #331 / #339 / #341 / #344 / #353 / #365 / #366 merged, #361 closed (substrate shipped elsewhere). -->
- [ ] `minsky-cli-auto-bootstrap-local-llm` — `minsky` (no args) on a fresh machine auto-detects Claude exhaustion + auto-installs the local-LLM stack with a single confirm prompt
  - **ID**: minsky-cli-auto-bootstrap-local-llm
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, local-llm, auto-bootstrap, multi-machine-sync
  - **Progress**: Slices 1-44 shipped (PRs #382–#450). Core bootstrap + arch detection + PID-alive gates + skip-earlier optimizations + doctor rows + `minsky setup-opencode` + auto-wire + `minsky stop-local-llm` complete. **Slice 45 (current)**: auto-start `mlx_lm.server` in the bootstrap pre-flight when `probeLocalLlmServer()` returns unreachable — spawn `mlx_lm.server --model <model-path>` in the background, write PID to `.minsky/local-llm.pid`, poll until server is ready (up to 60s). Files: `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (add `startLocalLlmServer()` called from `executePlanWithProductionIo` when server probe fails).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I expect it to automatically understand that claude is out of tokens and to switch to local modal + install+set it up first if needed".
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: Today, getting Minsky to use the local-LLM fallback on a fresh machine requires the operator to (a) `pipx install mlx-lm`, (b) `pipx install --python python3.12 aider-chat`, (c) `huggingface-cli download <model>`, (d) start `mlx_lm.server` in another terminal, (e) export `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1 MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` before running the daemon. Five manual steps; on a machine with no Claude tokens this is the only path forward, but the friction means the operator avoids the other machine entirely. Pre-registration: post-fix, the `minsky` command (no args) on a fresh checkout with no Claude credits remaining: (1) detects "Claude exhausted" via `claude --print --version` + a synthetic 1-token probe that classifies stderr against `HARD_LIMIT_PATTERNS`; (2) detects each missing piece of the local stack (pipx, mlx-lm, aider, model weights, mlx-lm.server reachable); (3) prints a single multi-line summary with one `[Y/n]` confirm prompt (default Y on TTY, default N on non-TTY) listing what it would install, the disk envelope (~30 GB Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B), and the wall-clock estimate; (4) on confirm, installs everything sequentially with progress output; (5) starts `mlx_lm.server` in the background and writes its PID to `.minsky/local-llm.pid` so subsequent `minsky` invocations can detect liveness; (6) sets `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1 MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` and forwards to the existing `runStartOrAttach` path. Idempotent: re-running `minsky` on an already-set-up machine adds zero seconds — every detection is `which` + `pgrep` + a single `GET` against `/v1/models`. The 5-min UX target: from `git pull` on a never-set-up machine to a worker iterating against the local model, ≤45 min wall-clock (model download dominates).
  - **Details**: (a) New module `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts` exporting `detectLocalLlmStack(): Promise<LocalLlmStackState>` that returns a discriminated union over `{ pipx, mlx, aider, model, server }` each carrying `present` / `absent` / `error`. (b) Pure helper `planLocalLlmBootstrap(state, claudeProbe): BootstrapPlan` that decides which steps to run; the plan is a `readonly InstallStep[]` where each step is one of `install-pipx | install-mlx-lm | install-aider | download-model | start-mlx-server`. (c) I/O helper `executeBootstrapPlan(plan, opts: { confirm: () => Promise<boolean>, log: (s: string) => void })` that prompts once, then sequences the steps with `child_process.spawn` and streams progress. (d) `bin/minsky.mjs` gains a pre-flight: when the daemon is about to start AND `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM` is unset AND a synthetic claude probe classifies as `hard-limit`, run `detectLocalLlmStack()` and `planLocalLlmBootstrap`; if the plan is non-empty, print + confirm + execute; then export `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1 MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` for the spawned daemon. (e) Failure modes: pipx install fails → loud-crash with the exact `pipx` error + a recovery hint (`brew install pipx`); model download fails (network drop) → resume on next invocation (huggingface-cli is itself idempotent); mlx-lm.server fails to start → log the error, fall back to `hold` mode (existing behaviour from `decideProvider`). (f) Tests: `local-llm-bootstrap.test.ts` covers all 6 detection states + 5 install plans + the confirm-prompt seam (DI'd via opts.confirm).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.test.ts` (new, paired tests), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (pre-flight wiring), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (replace the manual install runbook with `minsky` auto-bootstrap; keep the manual recipe as fallback in a collapsed section), `setup.sh` (no changes — `minsky` itself owns the bootstrap on first run; setup.sh stays focused on the constitutional prereqs).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each detection state; integration test on a clean `/tmp/<scratch>` HOME with `pipx`/`mlx`/`aider`/`model` selectively missing — assert the plan covers exactly the missing pieces. Live-run on the other machine: `git pull && minsky` from a never-set-up state, assert the daemon picks the next P0 task and dispatches an aider invocation against the local server inside 45 min wall-clock. Re-run `minsky` immediately after — the bootstrap detection adds <500 ms per `minsky` invocation (target the budget for the no-op fast path).
  - **Measurement**: live-run wall-clock from `git pull` to first daemon iteration on the local model: target ≤45 min on a 1 Gbps link (the model download dominates; the dependency installs are <60 s combined). Idempotent fast-path: re-running `minsky` on a set-up machine adds ≤500 ms (measured via `time minsky --doctor` over 10 invocations).
  - **Pivot**: if the auto-detect produces false positives (treats a transient Claude rate-limit as hard-limit and triggers a 30 GB download), tighten the classifier — require the same hard-limit signal across 2 consecutive 1-token probes 60 s apart before installing. If the install path is too brittle to ship reliably (homebrew variations, Apple Silicon vs Intel, Python version drift), retire the auto-install and degrade to "print recipe + exit" — the fallback plan from the operator's original question. Don't retire the auto-detect; the detect-only path is itself useful (operator gets a one-line "claude exhausted, run `minsky bootstrap-local-llm` to install").
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I expect it to automatically understand that claude is out of tokens and to switch to local modal + install+set it up first if needed"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — pipx, mlx-lm, aider, huggingface-cli are all industry-standard); rule #2 (Strategy boundary — `detectLocalLlmStack` + `planLocalLlmBootstrap` are pure, the executor is the I/O); rule #6 (stay-alive — local-LLM fallback is the substrate that lets the daemon iterate on a budget-paused machine); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD). Composes with `local-llm-fallback-on-budget-pause` (already shipped slices 1-6 via PRs #370/#371) and `daemon-aider-brief-shrinker` (P0, queued).
  - **Risk**: medium. The auto-install touches a 30 GB download and starts a long-lived background process. Mitigation: single confirm prompt before any mutation; `--dry-run` flag prints the plan without executing; `MINSKY_NO_AUTO_BOOTSTRAP=1` env var disables the pre-flight entirely; the detection layer is read-only.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator request 2026-05-08 — "I have minsky on another machine in outdated stage with no claude tokens left. … I expect it to automatically understand that claude is out of tokens and to switch to local modal + install+set it up first if needed".


- [ ] `minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap` — `git clone && pnpm install && minsky` works on a fresh checkout without a manual `pnpm build` step
  - **ID**: minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, bootstrap, fresh-clone, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I've cloned minsky from scratch, ran pnpm install, then ran minsky and got module not found about tick-loop".
  - **Estimate**: 0.25d
  - **Hypothesis**: `bin/minsky.mjs` imports from `../dist/index.js` (at line 51 — `from "../dist/index.js"`), but `novel/tick-loop/dist/` is gitignored and `pnpm install` does NOT build workspace packages by default. Result: on a fresh clone, the first `pnpm minsky` (or `node novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`) crashes with `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND: Cannot find module '/Users/.../novel/tick-loop/dist/index.js'`. The operator hit this immediately after cloning; the four prior P0 slices (auto-bootstrap / arch-detection / hardening) had verified `minsky doctor` works only on machines where `pnpm build` had already run. Pre-registration: post-fix, on a fresh clone with `dist/` deleted, `pnpm install` ALONE (no manual build step) leaves the repo in a state where `pnpm minsky doctor` exits 0 and prints the doctor output. Idempotent: subsequent `pnpm install` calls are O(seconds) — pnpm sees no work to do and skips the prepare hook's tsc invocation when nothing changed (TS incremental build cache OR a no-op `tsc -b` short-circuits). As a defensive backstop, when `bin/minsky.mjs` runs and finds `dist/index.js` missing, it emits a one-line clear error pointing at the build command instead of node's stack-trace ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND.
  - **Details**: (a) Add root-level `package.json` `prepare` script that runs `pnpm --filter @minsky/tick-loop build` after `pnpm install`. The `prepare` lifecycle hook runs once after `pnpm install` finishes for the current workspace (when `node_modules` is present), which is exactly the "after fresh-clone install" trigger we need. Per pnpm docs, `prepare` is the canonical hook for "build artifacts the package needs to be runnable". (b) `bin/minsky.mjs` gains a small dist-existence check at the top: before the import, `existsSync(resolve(HERE, "..", "dist", "index.js"))`; if absent, write a one-line error to stderr ("minsky: dist/ not built — run `pnpm install` from the repo root") and exit 1. This is a defensive backstop — if the prepare hook somehow fails (network drop during npm package fetch, tsc error, etc.) the operator gets actionable output instead of a node module-resolution stack trace. (c) Same defensive check + a `prepare` extension in `novel/tick-loop/package.json` itself: a `prepare` script there runs `pnpm build` so any consumer that adds `@minsky/tick-loop` as a dep also gets a built dist. (d) Update README.md "Installation" + tick-loop/README.md "Quick start" + AGENTS.md "Repository setup" with the fresh-clone command (`git clone … && pnpm install && minsky` — no separate build step needed). (e) Add a paired test that simulates the fresh-clone state by stat'ing for `dist/index.js` absence + asserting the error message + exit code shape; the test does NOT actually delete `dist/` (would race with concurrent test runs) but uses an injected `existsSyncFn` seam.
  - **Files**: `package.json` (add `prepare` script), `novel/tick-loop/package.json` (add `prepare` script), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (dist-existence check + clear-error branch), `novel/tick-loop/src/dist-existence-check.ts` (new pure helper), `novel/tick-loop/src/dist-existence-check.test.ts` (new paired tests), `README.md` (Installation section), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (Quick start), `AGENTS.md` (Repository setup).
  - **Touches**: `package.json`, `novel/tick-loop/package.json`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/src/dist-existence-check.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/dist-existence-check.test.ts`, `README.md`, `novel/tick-loop/README.md`, `AGENTS.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the dist-existence check (present → continue, absent → error+exit-1). Live integration test on a simulated fresh-clone state (`rm -rf novel/tick-loop/dist && pnpm install && pnpm minsky doctor`). Test runs both before AND after the fix to confirm the regression catches the failure mode and the fix resolves it. Manual confirmation: clone in `/tmp` from the remote, `pnpm install`, `pnpm minsky doctor` — output matches the M3 Max doctor output from slice 7 verification.
  - **Measurement**: `rm -rf novel/tick-loop/dist && pnpm install && pnpm minsky doctor` exits 0 and prints `minsky doctor — local-LLM stack health probe`. Without the fix, the same sequence exits 1 with `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND`. Wall-clock for `pnpm install` post-fix: target ≤30 s on a warm pnpm cache (the prepare hook's `tsc -b` adds ~3 s incremental). Test count: +3 paired tests for dist-existence-check.
  - **Pivot**: if the `prepare` hook causes issues (tsc compilation fails on a partial dependency tree, noisy install logs, broken CI semantics), retire the prepare hook and instead add a `setup.sh` step that does `pnpm install && pnpm -r build` — operator runs `./setup.sh` once after clone. The defensive dist-existence-check stays either way as the loud-fail backstop.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I've cloned minsky from scratch, ran pnpm install, then ran minsky and got module not found about tick-loop"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — pnpm's `prepare` hook is the standard mechanism for build-on-install); rule #2 (Strategy boundary — `dist-existence-check.ts` is pure over an injected existsSyncFn); rule #3 (test-first — red-first paired tests); rule #6 (stay-alive — ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND on first run is silent failure of the bootstrap UX; clear-error message is loud-crash at the right boundary per Armstrong 2007); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — this block IS the pre-registration). Composes with `minsky-cli-auto-bootstrap-local-llm` (parent P0) — the auto-bootstrap is meaningless if step 0 (`pnpm install`) doesn't produce a runnable CLI.
  - **Risk**: low. The `prepare` hook is the standard pnpm/npm pattern; failure modes are limited to tsc errors (which we'd want to surface anyway). The defensive dist-existence-check adds 2 lines of `existsSync` to `bin/minsky.mjs`'s startup — negligible cost (sub-millisecond).
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator live-run 2026-05-08 — fresh clone of `minsky` repo, ran `pnpm install`, then `minsky` (or `pnpm minsky`?) immediately failed with `Error [ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND]: Cannot find module '/Users/.../novel/tick-loop/dist/index.js' imported from /Users/.../novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`.

- [ ] `experiment-record-bin-checked-in` — eliminate `pnpm install` warning by moving `@minsky/experiment-record`'s `bin` to a checked-in launcher (mirror slice 8's pattern)
  - **ID**: experiment-record-bin-checked-in
  - **Tags**: p1, operator-directive, dx, fresh-clone, hardening
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "also on pnpm install it had a warning that it failed to create bin in experimental-record".
  - **Estimate**: 0.25d
  - **Hypothesis**: `novel/experiment-record/package.json` declares `"bin": { "experiment-record": "./dist/cli.js" }`, but `dist/` is gitignored. On fresh clone, `pnpm install` tries to create the bin symlink BEFORE running the `prepare` hook; the symlink creation fails (target file doesn't exist yet) and pnpm emits `WARN Failed to create bin at .../node_modules/.bin/experiment-record. ENOENT`. Slice 8's `prepare` hook then builds dist, but the bin symlink is already not-created and pnpm doesn't retry. Cosmetic for CI (the warning is non-fatal) but real for operators who try `pnpm exec experiment-record validate FOO.yaml` — they get "command not found" because the bin symlink wasn't created. Pre-registration: post-fix, `pnpm install` produces zero ENOENT warnings about experiment-record's bin, AND `node_modules/.bin/experiment-record` exists immediately after install (resolves to a checked-in launcher, not a gitignored compiled file). Mirrors slice 8's pattern in tick-loop: `bin/minsky.mjs` is a checked-in launcher that dynamic-imports from `dist/index.js` after an existsSync check.
  - **Details**: (a) New `novel/experiment-record/bin/experiment-record.mjs` — checked-in launcher (~30 lines). Same dist-existence check inlined as `bin/minsky.mjs` (slice 8). On dist present, dynamic-imports `parse` from `dist/index.js` and runs the same validate-or-error logic that's currently in `src/cli.ts`. (b) Update `novel/experiment-record/package.json`: `bin` field → `./bin/experiment-record.mjs` (instead of `./dist/cli.js`). Add `bin/experiment-record.mjs` to the `files` array. (c) `src/cli.ts` stays — it's still the source of truth + paired-test target for the validation logic. The launcher is the checked-in entry point that delegates. (d) `npm i` / `pnpm install` lifecycle: pnpm sees `bin` pointing at a checked-in file → symlink creation succeeds → no WARN. The `prepare` hook is unchanged.
  - **Files**: `novel/experiment-record/bin/experiment-record.mjs` (new), `novel/experiment-record/package.json` (bin field + files).
  - **Touches**: `novel/experiment-record/bin/experiment-record.mjs`, `novel/experiment-record/package.json`.
  - **Verification**: `rm -rf novel/*/dist novel/adapters/*/dist novel/bridges/*/dist *.tsbuildinfo node_modules/.bin/experiment-record && pnpm install` produces ZERO `Failed to create bin at .../experiment-record` warnings AND `ls -la node_modules/.bin/experiment-record` resolves to a valid symlink. `pnpm exec experiment-record validate /tmp/nonexistent.yaml` exits non-zero with the existing "cannot read /tmp/nonexistent.yaml" stderr (the validation logic).
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, `pnpm install 2>&1 | grep -c "Failed to create bin.*experiment-record"` returns 0. Pre-fix, the same grep returns ≥1 (typically 2 — the warning fires twice during pnpm's install + post-install passes). On a CI fresh-checkout, the same grep against the install log returns 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the launcher creates issues with the existing experiment-runner CI workflow, retire the launcher and instead drop the `bin` field entirely (the workflow uses `pnpm --filter @minsky/experiment-record build` then runs the binary by absolute path; the symlink was never load-bearing for CI). The defensive existsSync stays either way.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("also on pnpm install it had a warning that it failed to create bin in experimental-record"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — same checked-in-launcher pattern as `bin/minsky.mjs` from slice 8); rule #2 (dist-existence check is pure, injectable seam from `dist-existence-check.ts`); rule #3 (no new tests needed — the launcher is a thin shim over `parse`'s existing tests); rule #6 (stay-alive — the warning was silent failure of the operator's `pnpm exec experiment-record` UX); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD). Composes with `minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap` (slice 8) — same pattern, same defensive existsSync, same fresh-clone-UX target.
  - **Risk**: low. The launcher is ~30 lines of straightforward delegation; the validation logic stays in `src/cli.ts` (unchanged, paired tests still cover it). pnpm's bin-symlink creation succeeds because the launcher target is checked-in.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator live-run 2026-05-08 — observed `WARN Failed to create bin at /Users/.../node_modules/.bin/experiment-record. ENOENT: no such file or directory, open '.../node_modules/@minsky/experiment-record/dist/cli.js'` during `pnpm install` (both on local fresh-clone simulation and on CI's `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile` for slice 8's PR #387).

- [ ] `minsky-fresh-clone-health-checks` — slice 1 of self-healing: detect-and-explain the four most likely fresh-clone failures (node_modules absent, pnpm absent, Node major mismatch, dist stale) instead of leaking cryptic stack traces
  - **ID**: minsky-fresh-clone-health-checks
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, fresh-clone, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "Next let's add as much stable self-healing as reasonable to minsky & install commands". Slice 1 of three (slice 2: runtime resilience; slice 3: cross-machine dotfile). Aggressiveness: detect + auto-fix safe ops (anything inside `.minsky/` is fair game; outside is detect-and-warn with recovery hint).
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: Slice 8 (`minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap`, PR #387) covered ONE of the four likeliest fresh-clone failure modes — `dist/` not built. The remaining three still produce cryptic operator-hostile output: (i) `node_modules/` missing → `bin/minsky.mjs`'s dynamic `await import("../dist/index.js")` resolves the file but its transitive imports (`vitest` typedeps, `@types/node`, etc.) fail with `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND` pointing at node-internals; (ii) `pnpm` not on PATH on a fresh dev machine → `setup.sh` silently passes the prereq check (only inspects node / npx / git / claude / jq / curl / ntfy — pnpm is the actual install command yet not declared); (iii) Node major version too old (engines says `>=20`, the installed pnpm respects engines but emits an opaque `ERR_PNPM_UNSUPPORTED_PLATFORM` mid-install rather than a clear "your node is too old" up-front). Pre-registration: post-fix, on a fresh checkout simulated via `rm -rf node_modules`, running `node novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` exits 1 with a one-line stderr starting with `minsky: node_modules/ missing —` and ending with the recovery command `pnpm install` (no stack trace, no node-internal frames). On a host without `pnpm` on PATH, `./setup.sh --doctor` reports `RED — pnpm missing` (not the current silent green-pass). On a host with Node 18, `./setup.sh --doctor` reports `RED — node 18.x.y is below the >=20 engine requirement` (matches the engines field exactly). `minsky doctor` adds 4 substrate rows (`node_modules`, `pnpm-lock.yaml`, `dist/index.js`, `pnpm` on PATH) so the operator can see the install-time substrate at the same time as the local-LLM stack.
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/node-modules-existence-check.ts` exporting `checkNodeModules({ existsSyncFn, packageRoot }): { ok: boolean, missingPath?: string }` mirroring slice 8's `dist-existence-check.ts` shape. Paired test covers: present → ok, absent → not-ok with the missing path. (b) `bin/minsky.mjs` adds the node_modules check immediately after the dist-existence check. The check looks for `<PKG_ROOT>/node_modules` (the workspace package's own node_modules, NOT the workspace root's — pnpm's hoisting puts shared deps in the root but each package still gets its own `node_modules` directory with at least the package's `node_modules/.pnpm` entries). On absent → write a one-line stderr message naming the missing path + the recovery command (`pnpm install`) and exit 1. (c) `setup.sh` extends prereq checks: adds `pnpm` (RED if missing — install command requires it), adds Node major-version check (RED if `node --version | head -c 3` major is <20). The Node-major check is portable (works on any POSIX `node`); the pnpm check is `command -v pnpm`. Both gate on the engines field's lower bound — keep the threshold (20) in a single shell variable `MINSKY_NODE_MIN_MAJOR=20` near the top of the script. (d) `minsky doctor` (in `bin/minsky.mjs`'s `runDoctor`) adds the 4 substrate rows. The check uses `existsSync` for the file checks and `whichFn` for `pnpm`. Each row is GREEN/✓ if present, RED/✗ if absent — when any row is RED, doctor's banner becomes RED instead of YELLOW (operator can't run the daemon at all without these). (e) New paired tests for the substrate-row formatting (`emitDoctorRows`-shaped test that injects state and asserts the rendered lines). (f) README "Installation" section gets a new "Fresh-clone troubleshooting" sub-section listing the four detected failures + recovery commands. (g) `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` cross-links to the new doctor rows.

Test count delta: +6 paired tests (3 for `node-modules-existence-check`, 3 for `doctor-substrate-rows`).
  - **Pivot**: if the node_modules check produces false positives (e.g., a host that uses a non-standard package manager like Berry/Yarn that puts modules in a different path), gate the check on the presence of `pnpm-lock.yaml` at the repo root. If the Node major-version check breaks on a host that uses an exotic version manager that reports a non-standard `node --version`, retire the check and fall back to a `process.versions.node` parse inside the dist-existence-check (which already runs in node, so the check is portable).
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("Next let's add as much stable self-healing as reasonable to minsky & install commands"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — reuse slice 8's `dist-existence-check` pattern verbatim, no new abstractions); rule #3 (test-first — paired tests precede every new helper); rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — these are operator-actionable failures, the right boundary is a one-line message + clear recovery command, not a node-internal stack trace); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — this block IS the pre-registration). Composes with slice 8 (`minsky-cli-fresh-clone-bootstrap`, PR #387 — same defensive pattern, different file checks). Sources: Beyer et al., *Site Reliability Engineering*, 2016, Ch. 6 ("Monitoring Distributed Systems") — health checks must distinguish failure modes the operator can act on from internal bugs; cryptic stack traces conflate these.
  - **Risk**: low. Each new check is an `existsSync` call (sub-millisecond) plus a one-line stderr message on the failure path. The doctor rows are pure-rendering additions to the existing 8-row layout. The setup.sh changes are gated on the existing prereq-check step (idempotent, ledger-cached). No mutation of operator filesystem state outside of `.minsky/`.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator directive 2026-05-08 — open-ended request to harden minsky + install commands against the most likely fresh-clone / multi-machine failure modes, prioritized as slice 1 of three.

- [ ] `minsky-runtime-resilience` — slice 2 of self-healing: graceful-degrade on log-path / workers-dir / tick-loop-bin failures so the CLI never crashes at "the simple part" instead of the operator-actionable boundary
  - **ID**: minsky-runtime-resilience
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, runtime, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, slice 2 of three (slice 1 = fresh-clone-health-checks, PR #396, merged; slice 3 = cross-machine dotfile). Aggressiveness: detect + auto-fix safe ops (anything inside `.minsky/` is fair game; outside is detect-and-warn with recovery hint).
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: Three runtime failure modes still crash `minsky` instead of producing operator-actionable output: (i) `.minsky/workers/<id>.log` open fails with EACCES / EROFS / ENOSPC (typical when MINSKY_HOME points at a path the current user can't write — directly analogous to the `core.hooksPath` failure we shipped in PR #394/#395); (ii) `mkdirSync(WORKERS_DIR, { recursive: true })` itself throws EACCES on a read-only or wrong-owner MINSKY_HOME; (iii) the `bin/tick-loop.mjs` target the spawn dispatches into could be missing (deleted, never built, wrong PKG_ROOT) and `spawn(...)` would emit `ENOENT` with no clear pointer at the missing path. Each one currently produces a node stack trace pointing at the I/O call, not at the substrate misconfiguration. Pre-registration: post-fix, when `.minsky/workers/` is unwritable, `minsky` falls back to `/tmp/minsky-worker-<id>-<pid>.log` and emits a one-line stderr warning naming both paths + the underlying errno; daemon still starts, log is reachable. When MINSKY_HOME itself is unwritable (mkdir EACCES), `minsky` exits 1 with a one-line error naming the path + the recovery command (`chmod u+w <path>`, or set `MINSKY_HOME=<writable-path>`). When `bin/tick-loop.mjs` is missing, `minsky` exits 1 with a one-line error naming the path + the recovery command (`pnpm install`, or `git checkout HEAD -- novel/tick-loop/bin`).
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/log-path-fallback.ts` exporting `pickLogPath(opts: { primary, fallbackTmp, openSyncFn }): { path, fellBack, reason? }` — tries `primary`, on EACCES/EROFS/ENOSPC falls through to `fallbackTmp`, on a second failure throws (loud-crash per Armstrong 2007). The helper is pure-over-injection so the test layer can simulate each errno. (b) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/workers-dir-mkdir.ts` exporting `ensureWorkersDir(opts: { dir, mkdirSyncFn }): { ok: boolean, errCode?, recoveryHint? }` — wraps `mkdirSync({ recursive: true })` and classifies EACCES (recovery: chmod) vs EROFS (recovery: set MINSKY_HOME) vs other. (c) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/tick-loop-bin-existence-check.ts` mirroring `dist-existence-check.ts` shape — `checkTickLoopBinExists(opts: { path, existsSyncFn }) → { ok, path? }` plus a `formatTickLoopBinMissingMessage(path)` formatter. (d) `bin/minsky.mjs` wires all three helpers in the start-or-attach path: tick-loop-bin existence first (loud-fail before mkdir), then workers-dir mkdir (loud-fail with recovery hint), then log-path fallback (warn + continue). (e) `minsky doctor` adds a 13th row reporting whether the workers dir is writable (+1 substrate row above slice 1's 4). When ANY runtime substrate is broken, doctor banner stays consistent with slice 1's RED/exit-1 contract. (f) Update `novel/tick-loop/README.md` + `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` cross-link.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/log-path-fallback.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/log-path-fallback.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/workers-dir-mkdir.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/workers-dir-mkdir.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/tick-loop-bin-existence-check.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/tick-loop-bin-existence-check.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts` (re-exports), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (wire all three helpers), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (slice 2 section), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (cross-link).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/log-path-fallback.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/log-path-fallback.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/workers-dir-mkdir.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/workers-dir-mkdir.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/tick-loop-bin-existence-check.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/tick-loop-bin-existence-check.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/README.md`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each helper covering present / EACCES / EROFS / ENOSPC / unknown-errno paths. Live integration: (i) `chmod 000 .minsky/workers && minsky` falls back to `/tmp/minsky-worker-0-<pid>.log` with one-line warn; (ii) `MINSKY_HOME=/dev/null/notwritable minsky` exits 1 with mkdir-error message; (iii) `mv novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs /tmp/x && minsky` exits 1 with bin-missing message; (iv) `minsky doctor` shows a 13th substrate row "workers dir writable" (RED on chmod-000 .minsky/workers).
  - **Measurement**: `chmod 000 .minsky/workers && minsky 2>&1 | grep -c "Error: EACCES"` returns 0 post-fix (was ≥1 — the raw EACCES from openSync). `MINSKY_HOME=/dev/null/notwritable minsky 2>&1 | grep -c "operation not permitted"` returns 0 post-fix (was ≥1 — the raw mkdir error). Test count delta: +9 paired tests.
  - **Pivot**: if the log-path fallback to `/tmp` produces noise on multi-tenant hosts (e.g., a shared dev server where `/tmp/minsky-worker-0-*.log` paths collide), promote `/tmp` to a per-user `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/minsky-${USER}-worker-<id>-<pid>.log` path. If the EROFS branch is too defensive (hosts that mount sub-paths read-only intentionally), demote it to detect-only and let the operator's mkdir failure surface naturally.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 — slice 2 of three; rule #1 (reuse slice 1's pure-helper-with-paired-tests pattern); rule #3 (test-first — paired tests precede every helper); rule #6 (graceful-degrade-AT-the-right-boundary — log-write failure is operator-actionable, not a daemon-crash); rule #9 (pre-registration). Composes with slice 1 (`minsky-fresh-clone-health-checks`, PR #396 — same shape, different runtime layer). Sources: Beyer et al. (SRE) Ch. 6 + Armstrong 2007.
  - **Risk**: low. Each new helper is pure-over-injection, ≤80 LOC, paired-tested. The bin-side wiring is three try-catches around existing I/O calls; the existing tests still cover the happy path. No mutation outside `.minsky/`.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator directive 2026-05-08 — three failure modes identified by reading `bin/minsky.mjs`'s I/O call sites (line 161 `mkdirSync(WORKERS_DIR)`, line 179 `openSync(logPath, "a")`, line 180 `spawn(process.execPath, [TICK_LOOP_BIN, ...])`) against the multi-machine pain pattern from PRs #394/#395 (different-username dotfiles → unwritable paths).

- [ ] `minsky-cross-machine-dotfile-checks` — slice 3 of self-healing: detect dotfile-controlled git config paths that don't exist on the current machine and surface them in `minsky doctor` with a per-key recovery command
  - **ID**: minsky-cross-machine-dotfile-checks
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, dotfiles, multi-machine-sync, dx
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, slice 3 of three (slice 1 = fresh-clone-health-checks, PR #396, merged; slice 2 = runtime-resilience, PR #398, merged). Aggressiveness: detect + warn (git config is outside `.minsky/`, so per the operator's chosen aggressiveness — "detect + auto-fix safe ops" — we don't auto-mutate git config).
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: PRs #394/#395 shipped graceful-degrade for the lefthook permission denial caused by an invalid `core.hooksPath` from synced dotfiles. That covers the symptom. The general pattern — git config keys that reference filesystem paths via dotfiles synced across machines with different usernames — affects multiple keys: `core.hooksPath`, `core.attributesfile`, `core.excludesfile`, `commit.template`, `core.editor`, `init.templateDir`. Today, only the `core.hooksPath` failure is gracefully handled (because it triggers during `pnpm install`); the others fail later, often silently or with cryptic errors. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky doctor` adds a "git config sanity" section with one row per of the 3 highest-impact keys (`core.hooksPath`, `core.attributesfile`, `core.excludesfile`). Each row reports GREEN/✓ when unset OR set to a valid path; RED/✗ when set to a path that does not exist on this machine, with a one-line recovery command naming the config key + scope (`git config --global --unset core.hooksPath` for global, `--local --unset` for local). The doctor banner stays YELLOW (not RED — broken git config doesn't immediately block the daemon; it's just a footgun the operator should know about).
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/git-config-path-checks.ts` exporting `checkGitConfigPaths(opts: { keysToCheck, getGitConfigFn, existsSyncFn }): { brokenPaths: BrokenGitConfigPath[] }` where each broken-path record carries `configKey`, `configValue`, `origin` (`global` / `local` / `system` / `unknown`), and `recoveryCommand`. The helper is pure-over-injection so the test layer can simulate each (key × origin × valid/invalid) matrix. (b) `bin/minsky.mjs::runDoctor` adds a "git config sanity" section after the substrate rows. Each broken-path row is GREEN/✓ when valid OR unset, RED/✗ when set + path doesn't exist. The recovery command shown follows the actual scope from `git config --show-origin --get`. (c) `setup.sh --doctor` adds the same checks (calls `git config --show-origin --get <key>` directly via shell). (d) Update `novel/tick-loop/README.md` slice 3 section + `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` cross-link.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/git-config-path-checks.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/git-config-path-checks.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts` (re-exports), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (wire into runDoctor), `setup.sh` (add git config checks to --doctor), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (slice 3 section), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (cross-link).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/git-config-path-checks.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/git-config-path-checks.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `setup.sh`, `novel/tick-loop/README.md`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `checkGitConfigPaths` covering 3 keys × 4 outcomes (unset / set+exists / set+missing / set+EACCES). Live integration: (i) `git config --local core.hooksPath /tmp/nonexistent-xyz123 && minsky doctor` shows RED row for `core.hooksPath` with the unset recovery command + the broken value; (ii) `git config --local --unset core.hooksPath && minsky doctor` shows GREEN row; (iii) `./setup.sh --doctor` shows the same rows.

  - **Pivot**: if the check produces false positives (e.g., a host that LEGITIMATELY uses a hooks path that's lazily-created by another tool), promote the check from "missing" to "missing AND not lazily-creatable" by also probing parent dir writability. If `git config --show-origin` returns ambiguous results for inherited config (system → global → local merge), fall back to `--local`-scope-only checks.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 — slice 3 of three. PRs #394/#395 (graceful-degrade for `core.hooksPath` invalid-path → lefthook install gracefully fails). Rule #1 (don't reinvent — same pure-helper-with-paired-tests pattern). Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — broken git config is a config-bug not a runtime-bug; surface upfront in doctor rather than crash later). Rule #9 (pre-registration). Sources: Git docs on config scoping (system / global / local); Beyer et al. (SRE) Ch. 6.
  - **Risk**: low. Each check is a `git config --show-origin --get <key>` shell-out (sub-millisecond) plus an `existsSync` on the returned path. No mutation of operator git config — detect-only with recovery hint per the operator's aggressiveness choice.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator directive 2026-05-08 — three failure modes from PRs #394/#395 (the `core.hooksPath` cycle) generalized to the broader set of dotfile-controlled git config keys.

- [ ] `minsky-claude-exhaustion-persisted-state` — slice 4 of self-healing: persist last claude hard-limit hit in `.minsky/state.json` so a fresh `minsky` startup detects exhaustion without relying on a token-too-small live probe
  - **ID**: minsky-claude-exhaustion-persisted-state
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, self-healing, claude-exhaustion, dx
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens. It shouldn't have happened, it should have quickly detected that & switched to local model". Aggressiveness: detect + auto-fix safe ops (write to `.minsky/state.json` is INSIDE `.minsky/` so it's fair game per the operator's chosen aggressiveness).
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: The startup probe `claude --print "ping"` is a 1-token query; Anthropic's quota metering hits at the multi-K-token level (an iteration is typically 5-15K input tokens). When the operator's quota is exhausted, the 1-token probe can still return exit 0 — false-positive on `healthy`. The daemon then spawns claude on iteration 1, which fails with hard-limit; the existing per-iteration `decideProvider` logic correctly switches to local on iteration 2 — but the operator already saw iteration 1 spawn claude (the bug they reported). Plus, even if iteration 2 switches to local, that requires the local-LLM stack to already be installed; if it isn't (because `maybeBootstrapLocalLlm` skipped the bootstrap based on the false-positive probe), iteration 2 lands in `hold` mode. Pre-registration: post-fix, when `.minsky/state.json::last_claude_hard_limit.ts` is recent (within `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN` minutes; default 60), `minsky` startup SKIPS the live probe and goes directly to the local-LLM bootstrap path. The daemon writes this field whenever its iteration loop catches a hard-limit signal (via `isClaudeHardLimit(failure)`). Composes with: existing `decideProvider` (in-process per-iteration) + new persistence layer (cross-process / cross-restart).
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` exporting `readLastHardLimit(opts: { stateFilePath, readFileSyncFn, existsSyncFn, nowFn, ttlMs })` returning `{ exhausted: boolean, ageMs?, reason?, ts? }`; and `writeLastHardLimit(opts: { stateFilePath, readFileSyncFn, writeFileSyncFn, ts, reason })` that updates the state.json atomically (read → modify → write — same shape as setup.sh's ledger writes). (b) `bin/minsky.mjs::maybeBootstrapLocalLlm` consults `readLastHardLimit` BEFORE the live `probeClaude()` call. Recent → log `minsky: persisted hard-limit hit at <ts> (<N>m ago); skipping live probe and bootstrapping local-LLM` and proceed to bootstrap path. Stale → run probe as before. (c) Daemon spawn-strategy (`LlmProviderSpawnStrategy.spawn`) gets a new injected seam `persistHardLimit?: (failure) => Promise<void>` that's called when `isClaudeHardLimit(failure) === true`. Production wiring in `bin/tick-loop.mjs` sets it to a function that calls `writeLastHardLimit`. Test layer leaves it `undefined` (no-op). (d) `minsky --help` adds two new lines under "Operator escape hatches": `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred minsky` (force local immediately) and `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN=<N>` (configure persisted-state TTL). (e) `minsky doctor` adds a row "claude exhaustion (persisted)" showing GREEN ✓ when no recent hard-limit, YELLOW ⚠ with timestamp when recent. (f) Update `novel/tick-loop/README.md` slice 4 section + `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` cross-link.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts` (add `persistHardLimit` injected seam), `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts` (re-exports), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (wire read into maybeBootstrapLocalLlm + doctor row + --help), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire write seam in spawn strategy construction), `novel/tick-loop/README.md` (slice 4 section), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (cross-link).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/claude-exhaustion-state.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/index.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/README.md`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `readLastHardLimit` covering: state file absent, state file present + field absent, field present + within TTL, field present + stale, field present + corrupt JSON. Paired tests for `writeLastHardLimit` covering: state file absent (creates), state file present + field absent (adds), field present (overwrites). Live integration: (i) `echo '{"schema_version":"1","last_claude_hard_limit":{"ts":"<now>","reason":"test"}}' > .minsky/state.json && minsky` skips live probe and starts local-LLM bootstrap; (ii) `minsky doctor` shows YELLOW row "claude exhaustion (persisted)" with timestamp; (iii) `MINSKY_HARD_LIMIT_TTL_MIN=5 minsky` honors the env override.
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, `echo '...' > .minsky/state.json && pnpm minsky 2>&1 | grep -c "persisted hard-limit"` returns ≥1. Test count delta: +8 paired tests (5 read + 3 write).
  - **Pivot**: if persisted-state false-positives (operator's quota DID reset but persisted state hasn't been cleared), the live probe runs after TTL anyway — so the worst case is one extra wall-clock hour on local-LLM. If that proves unacceptable, lower the TTL default or add a `--force-claude` operator override. If `state.json` write contention with other minsky processes (multiple workers) causes corruption, switch to per-worker state files (`.minsky/state-worker-<id>.json`). If the spawn strategy seam introduces test-time async surprises (race between in-process state and on-disk state), default the seam to in-process-only and expose the on-disk persistence as an opt-in flag.
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens"). Slice 4 of self-healing trilogy. PRs #396/#398/#399 (slices 1-3 of self-healing). Rule #1 (don't reinvent — reuse the slice 1-3 pure-helper-with-paired-tests pattern). Rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the right boundary — the right boundary for "claude exhausted" is "skip claude and use local", not "spawn claude and let it fail"). Rule #9 (pre-registration). Composes with existing `LlmProviderSpawnStrategy` per-iteration logic. Sources: Beyer et al. (SRE) Ch. 6; Anthropic CLI docs on `claude --print` exit codes; Ries (Lean Startup) for build-measure-learn — persisted state IS the measurement layer.
  - **Risk**: low. Each new check is a `readFileSync` (sub-millisecond) on the existing `.minsky/state.json` file. Write is on the daemon's failure path (already an exceptional code path). No mutation outside `.minsky/`.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator live-run 2026-05-08 — "I ran minsky and it happily started claude even though it's out of tokens. It shouldn't have happened, it should have quickly detected that & switched to local model". Root cause analysis: 1-token probe is below Anthropic's metering threshold; existing in-process per-iteration `decideProvider` correctly fires on iteration 2 but the user already saw iteration 1's wasted claude spawn.

- [ ] `minsky-cli-context-aware-ux` — `minsky` (no args) reads the machine's full context (worker state, daemon state, claude state, git state, queue state) and offers a single confirm-or-multi-select prompt for what to do next
  - **ID**: minsky-cli-context-aware-ux
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, minsky-cli, ux, dx, multi-machine-sync
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-08, "I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)".
  - **Estimate**: 3d
  - **Hypothesis**: Today `minsky` (no args) collapses to "start-or-attach worker 0 with sane defaults". That's the right default for the dogfood-on-self loop, but not the right default for: a fresh checkout (no daemon ever ran, no `.minsky/state.json`), a machine that ran the daemon earlier and is mid-task (workers stopped between sessions), a machine where `main` advanced and the operator wants to merge / rebase before iterating, or a machine where claude has run dry. Pre-registration: post-fix, `minsky` (no args) reads ≤7 signals (workers running, daemon PID liveness, last iteration timestamp, claude probe state, local-LLM state, `git status` cleanliness, open daemon PR count + CONFLICTING count) and renders one of N pre-defined "scenarios" (clean-fresh-checkout / daemon-mid-iteration / claude-exhausted-with-local-stack / claude-exhausted-no-stack / WIP-needs-cleanup / git-dirty-cant-iterate / queue-empty). Each scenario carries a default action and a multi-select alternatives list. The operator confirms with `[Enter]` (default) or types a number to pick an alternative. Target: from `minsky` invocation to first action, ≤2 s p95 (the detection is fast; the prompt is human-time but not blocking). Operator-perceived UX: "I just type `minsky` and it tells me what to do next AND why".
  - **Details**: (a) New module `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts` exporting `gatherMinskyContext(opts: GatherOpts): Promise<MinskyContext>` — 7 parallel detection probes, each timeout-bounded at 500 ms. (b) Pure decision function `planMinskyAction(context: MinskyContext): MinskyActionPlan` returning `{ scenario, recommendedAction, alternatives }`. (c) Prompt module `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts` exporting `runInteractive(plan, opts: { stdin, stdout, isTty })` that handles `[Y/n]` confirm AND multi-select via numbered options (`1`/`2`/`3` keystrokes); on non-TTY (CI / launchd / piped), the recommended action runs without prompting (rule #6 — silence on non-interactive surfaces is correct, not failure). (d) `bin/minsky.mjs` no-args path becomes: `gatherMinskyContext` → `planMinskyAction` → `runInteractive` → execute the chosen action (which may delegate back to existing `runStartOrAttach`, `runLogs`, `runStop`, or new `runBootstrapLocalLlm`, `runMergeWipPrs`, etc.). (e) Snapshot tests for the 7 scenarios with synthetic context fixtures so the Markdown output stays stable.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.ts` (new pure decision), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.test.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (no-args path rewrite + back-compat for `minsky logs|stop|<id>`), `README.md` (retire the "Not a global CLI" disclaimer; add a "What `minsky` (no args) does" section).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-context.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-action-plan.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/minsky-prompt.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs`, `README.md`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each of the 7 scenarios with golden-file snapshots of the rendered prompt. Integration test: synthetic `.minsky/` directory representing each scenario, `minsky` non-interactive (`MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1`), assert the recommended action runs. Manual operator walkthrough: each of the 7 scenarios on a real machine produces an exampleive "yes, that's what I wanted" outcome (the soft acceptance criterion).
  - **Measurement**: `time minsky </dev/null >/dev/null 2>&1` p95 ≤2 s over 100 invocations (the detection layer's wall-clock budget). AND post-rollout: count of `minsky [<args>]` invocations where the operator types a positional argument vs no-args — the no-args fraction should rise to ≥60 % within 14 days (pre-rollout baseline: ~10 % since the no-args path is currently just "start worker 0").
  - **Pivot**: if the 7-scenario decision tree is too brittle (real machines hit 8th / 9th edge cases the table doesn't cover), retire the multi-select prompt and degrade to "list 5 actions, type the number" — preserves the context-aware detection but drops the "default action with confirm" UX. If detection is too slow (≥2 s p95), parallelise harder or retire individual probes (e.g., drop the `gh pr list` call which dominates wall-clock; keep only the local-state probes).
  - **Anchor**: operator directive 2026-05-08 ("I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)"); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `prompts` / `inquirer` / `enquirer` are industry-standard interactive-prompt libraries; pick whichever has the smallest dep footprint at decision time); rule #2 (Strategy boundary — `gatherMinskyContext` is pure over an injected probe seam; the prompt is the I/O); rule #6 (stay-alive — non-TTY mode runs the recommended action without prompting, so cron / launchd / CI never block on stdin); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD). Composes with `minsky-cli-auto-bootstrap-local-llm` (P0, queued) — the bootstrap is one of the recommended actions the prompt offers.
  - **Risk**: medium. Adding an interactive prompt to a CLI that historically ran unattended risks breaking the daemon's launchd / systemd surface (where stdin is closed). Mitigation: explicit non-interactive mode (`MINSKY_NON_INTERACTIVE=1` AND `process.stdout.isTTY === false`) where the recommended action runs without prompting. The launchd unit-files already pipe stdin from `/dev/null`, so the detection is automatic.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator request 2026-05-08 — "Overall I want minsky to be powerful and straightforward cli tool. I want the main UX for it to be just `minsky` and the cli will understand the context and figure out what to do next, with full support of suggestions and asking user to confirm the plan (and possibly multi-select choice)".

- [ ] `daemon-aider-brief-shrinker` — produce a slim brief for the local-LLM (aider+Qwen32B) path so iterations finish inside the watchdog window
  - **ID**: daemon-aider-brief-shrinker
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, local-llm, throughput, brief-shape, minsky-loop-bug, surfaced-by-live-run
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: Stock daemon brief is ~7-10 KB (priority-discipline gate, anti-noop guard, optimization-discipline gate, full task block, PR self-grade template, PR security-review template, fix-own-PR-on-CI-failure block). Plus aider auto-loads every file the brief references — TASKS.md, vision.md, the 4 files in the picked task's `**Files**:`, every `scripts/*.mjs` mentioned. Total context after auto-load: 30-50 KB. At Qwen2.5-Coder-32B-Instruct-4bit's ~14 tok/s steady-state on M3 Max 64GB, prompt processing alone (~12-15K input tokens) takes 14-18 min, plus N tokens of output, plus aider's edit-loop turns. The 30-min watchdog (`MINSKY_CLAUDE_PRINT_TIMEOUT_MS=1800000` for the local path; relabelled `local-spawn-timeout` in `buildIterationReason`) bites before aider finishes. Live-run 2026-05-07 against `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` confirmed: aider auto-loaded 9 files, hit the 30-min timeout with no edit produced. Pre-registration: post-fix, when provider is `local`, the brief omits everything that doesn't change aider's edit decision: drop the priority-discipline gate (the daemon already picked the task), drop the optimization-discipline gate (operator directive doesn't apply to survival mode), drop the PR self-grade and security templates (aider can't open PRs at Qwen pace anyway — it commits locally and the operator opens the PR). Keep: task description + Hypothesis + Details + Files. Target slim brief size ≤2 KB. Target rolling-7d p95 of `local-spawn-timeout` count <2/day per worker. Pivot if median local iteration still doesn't complete inside 30 min — fall back to "queue + log" mode where the daemon writes a timestamped TASKS.md note "would-have-picked: <task-id>" instead of dispatching aider, until claude recovers.
  - **Details**: (a) New `buildLocalBrief(task)` function in `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-brief.ts` (extracted alongside existing `buildDaemonBrief`) that produces a ≤2 KB brief: just the task ID, tag-line, Hypothesis, Details, Files. No gates, no templates, no anti-noop guard — those exist for the claude path's PR-opening workflow, which aider doesn't follow. (b) `LlmProviderSpawnStrategy` (the wrapper from slice 3) gains a `briefBuilder` seam: when provider is `local`, the wrapper calls `buildLocalBrief(task)` and substitutes the message arg before delegating to `buildAiderInvocation`. (c) `bin/tick-loop.mjs` plumbs the existing brief-builder factory through the wrapper. (d) Snapshot tests: `local-brief.snapshot.test.ts` asserts the slim brief is ≤2 KB for the 5 largest open P0 tasks. (e) Update `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` "Brief-size pivot threshold" section to "shipped — see daemon-aider-brief-shrinker".
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-brief.ts` (extract + add `buildLocalBrief`), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-brief.test.ts` (paired tests for both builders), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts` (briefBuilder seam), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.test.ts` (test the substitution), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire-in), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (mark pivot threshold shipped).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-brief.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-brief.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-spawn-strategy.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`
  - **Verification**: paired tests: stock brief (existing) / slim brief (new, ≤2 KB) / wrapper substitution (provider=local → slim, provider=claude → stock). Live-run on M3 Max 64 GB: dispatch one iteration with `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` against an in-tree task, assert aider produces ≥1 file edit inside the 30-min watchdog window. Snapshot test in CI catches brief-size regressions ≥10 % beyond the 2 KB target.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/llm-provider-throughput.mjs --since=$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) --json` returns `local.iterationsCompleted >= 1 per 24h` AND `grep -c "local-spawn-timeout" .minsky/workers/*.log` over the rolling 7d window ≤ `worker_count * 7 * 2`. The 2/day-per-worker ceiling matches `claude-print-timeout`'s ceiling so the daemon's overall timeout-frequency invariant catches both labels uniformly.
  - **Pivot**: if slim brief lands and median local iteration still doesn't complete in 30 min (e.g., aider loops on edit-disagreement with the 32B model's smaller effective context), retire the local-LLM dispatch path entirely for this hardware tier and ship "queue + log" mode: the daemon writes a timestamped TASKS.md note `would-have-picked-during-budget-pause: <task-id> @ <ISO-timestamp>` and ticks. Operator processes the queue when claude credits return. The local-LLM substrate stays in the codebase (it's tested and small) but is gated behind `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_DISPATCH=1`; the default becomes log-only.
  - **Anchor**: live-run 2026-05-07 (M3 Max 64 GB, Qwen2.5-Coder-32B-Instruct-4bit hit 30-min watchdog on `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` task, no edit produced); rule #2 (briefBuilder seam — Strategy boundary); rule #6 (let-it-crash — slim brief is the next minimum-viable change); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` § "Brief-size pivot threshold" (the same hypothesis written before code; this task lands the implementation).
  - **Risk**: low. The substitution is provider-conditional; the claude path is unchanged. The `buildLocalBrief` extraction is mechanical (move + delete the gate sections). Mitigation: snapshot tests catch size drift; operator can disable via `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_DISPATCH=0` if slim-brief output quality is worse than expected.

- [ ] `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` — daemon spawn-strategy must time out child `claude --print` processes so a stuck child doesn't silently freeze a worker for hours
  - **ID**: daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, watchdog, pick-next, minsky-loop-bug
  - **Pick-next**: yes — 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 caught worker-1's `claude --print --worktree daemon-1-security-privacy-priority-substrate` (PID 87396) hung at 0.1% CPU for 1h 56min; daemon parent waited indefinitely. Lost ~24 iterations of throughput. Operator manually killed PID 87396; parent recovered via failed-iteration log + next tick.
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: The daemon's `ProcessSpawnStrategy.spawn()` resolves only on child `close` event. If `claude --print` hangs (slow API, network drop, OOM, missing input on stdin), the parent waits forever. Pre-registration: post-fix, every `claude --print` spawn carries a per-iteration timeout (default 15 min — well above the 95th-percentile productive iteration but below the operator's tolerance for blind silence). Hung children are SIGKILLed and the iteration logs `failed` with reason `claude-print-timeout: <ms>ms`. Over a rolling 7d window, the count of `claude-print-timeout` reasons is the new visible-not-silent metric (Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6). Target ≤2 timeouts/day per worker; if more, the timeout is too aggressive — pivot to a configurable threshold per `MINSKY_CLAUDE_PRINT_TIMEOUT_MS`.
  - **Details**: (a) Add `timeoutMs?: number` to `ProcessSpawnStrategyOptions`. (b) When set, wrap the child in `setTimeout(timeoutMs)` that calls `child.kill('SIGKILL')` + records timeout reason. (c) The `ProcessSpawnStrategy.spawn` Promise resolves with `{ exitCode: -1, durationMs, stdoutTail, stderrTail: '<timed out after Nms>' }` so the daemon's outer loop sees a `failed` iteration and ticks again. (d) `bin/tick-loop.mjs` reads `MINSKY_CLAUDE_PRINT_TIMEOUT_MS` (default 900_000 = 15 min) and threads through. (e) Self-diagnose invariant `claudePrintTimeoutFrequencyInvariant` fires if rolling-7d timeout count > 14 (more than 2/day average across workers).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (`timeoutMs` opt + watchdog), `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.test.ts` (paired tests for fast / slow / hung child), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (env-var threading), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (`claudePrintTimeoutFrequencyInvariant`).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for spawn-strategy: happy path (resolves before timeout) / slow-but-completes (no false positive) / hung child (SIGKILL fires, exit code -1) / opt-out (no `timeoutMs` → legacy unbounded behaviour preserved).
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c "claude-print-timeout" .minsky/workers/*.log` over rolling 7d window ≤14. AND no single iteration shows daemon-parent's `claude --print` child running for >`timeoutMs + 30s` per `pgrep --parent <daemon-pid> -a | awk` over a 1min sampling window (chaos test).
  - **Pivot**: if the 15min default produces >2 false-positive timeouts/day on legitimate long iterations, raise to 30 min — but document the wall-clock-vs-budget tradeoff. If the timeout is set too low (e.g., 5 min), some legitimate iterations get killed mid-spawn. Don't retire the timeout — silence is failure (Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6) is the operator's stated tolerance.
  - **Anchor**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 (worker-1 PID 87396 hung 1h 56min); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `ProcessSpawnStrategy.spawn` is the boundary); rule #6 (let-it-crash — kill the hung child, the iteration loop catches the `failed` status); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); operator 2026-05-07 — "monitor + unblock + file tasks so next time minsky unblocks itself".
  - **Risk**: low. The timeout is opt-in via env var; legacy behaviour preserved when unset. Mitigation: ship with the env-var read but a safe default (15 min) so production immediately benefits.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 — worker-1 stuck for ~2h, ~24 iterations lost.

- [ ] `daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog` — when a daemon's open PR goes CONFLICTING for >Nh, force the daemon to rebase or escalate as `Blocked: needs-operator-rebase`
  - **ID**: daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, watchdog, conflict-resolution, minsky-loop-bug
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: The 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 ended with 5 daemon PRs (#321 / #324 / #331 / #339 / #341) stuck CONFLICTING because the daemon couldn't rebase its own worktree branches (force-push sandbox policy denies the push). One PR (#330, the resolveDiffBase fix) eventually rebased successfully; the others didn't. The pattern: as main moves under a daemon PR, the PR goes CONFLICTING and stays there. Pre-registration: post-fix, no daemon PR remains CONFLICTING for >2h; the watchdog either rebases via Mergiraf or files a `Blocked: needs-operator-rebase` task. Rolling-7d count of escalations ≤1/day; if higher, the daemon's rebase capability isn't sufficient — pivot to allowlist `--force-with-lease` on `daemon/<id>/<task-id>` branches.
  - **Details**: (a) Extend self-diagnose's `daemonPrStuckDirtyInvariant` (#239) to also classify `CONFLICTING` (not just `DIRTY`). (b) New daemon iteration step: when self-diagnose finds a CONFLICTING daemon PR, the iteration's brief becomes "rebase PR #N onto current main; resolve conflicts via Mergiraf if available; force-push with `--force-with-lease`". (c) On 2 retries failing, the daemon files a fresh TASKS.md entry `daemon-pr-stuck-rebase: PR #N conflicting for Nh; needs operator manual rebase` and labels the PR `Blocked: needs-operator-rebase`. (d) Composes with #273's Mergiraf merge driver (already shipped + activated): when conflicts are structural, Mergiraf auto-resolves; otherwise escalate.
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (extend `daemonPrStuckDirtyInvariant`), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-rebase.ts` + `.test.ts` (rebase decision + I/O wrapper), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire-in to runOneIteration's brief-builder).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-rebase.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-rebase.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for daemon-pr-rebase decision: clean-pr / conflicting-1h / conflicting-3h / 2-retries-exhausted. Integration test on a synthetic conflict (branch + main edit same line) → mergiraf auto-resolve.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot" --state open --json mergeable --jq '[.[] | select(.mergeable == "CONFLICTING")] | length'` over 7d rolling: median ≤1.
  - **Pivot**: if the daemon can't actually force-push from sandbox (the original blocker that caused this), pivot to "soft escalation" — file the rebase task and notify operator via ntfy. The daemon-side detection still works; only the auto-rebase action degrades.
  - **Anchor**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 (5 PRs stuck CONFLICTING at end of window); rule #1 (don't reinvent — Mergiraf merge driver shipped at #273); rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure rebase decision fed by injected I/O); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); composes with `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` (already filed P0).
  - **Risk**: medium. Force-pushing daemon branches risks history loss if the operator was reviewing. Mitigation: `--force-with-lease` (refuses if upstream advanced); cap-2 retries; explicit escalation path via the new TASKS.md filing.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 — 5 of 7 open daemon PRs CONFLICTING at end of window; force-push sandbox policy denied daemon's own rebase attempts.

- [ ] `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion` — when a TASKS.md task ships via a merged PR, the task block should auto-mark complete so daemons don't re-pick it
  - **ID**: daemon-task-rotation-on-completion
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, task-discipline, minsky-loop-bug
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07: worker-1 picked `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` task on iter 26-27 even though #309 had already shipped the substrate. Worker-1 re-created the same gate module + tests + brief compressions as PR #343 — closed as duplicate. Pattern repeats: when a task's substrate ships but the task block isn't manually removed, daemons keep re-picking it, wasting iterations. Pre-registration: post-fix, when a PR with title containing `feat(<task-id>)` merges, the daemon's iteration step removes the task block from TASKS.md if all the task's `**Acceptance**` criteria parse as satisfied. Visible-not-silent: removal commit message names the criteria-checker decision. Rolling-7d count of duplicate-PR creations (PR with `<task-id>` in title where `<task-id>` block doesn't exist on main) → 0.
  - **Details**: (a) New pure helper `decideTaskCompletion({ taskBlock, openPrs, mergedPrs }) → 'remove' | 'keep' | 'incomplete'` based on acceptance criteria checkboxes + merged-PR titles matching the task ID. (b) Daemon iteration runs this after each merge it observes; emits a TASKS.md edit + commit. (c) The decision is conservative — only auto-removes when ALL acceptance criteria parse as ✅ (operator can keep `**Acceptance**: TBD` to defer auto-removal).
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-task-completion.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (pure decision), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-task-rotation.ts` + `.test.ts` (I/O wrapper), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire-in after `runMetricsRender`).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/check-task-completion.mjs`, `scripts/check-task-completion.test.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-task-rotation.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-task-rotation.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `decideTaskCompletion`: all-acceptance-✅ + merged-PR-found → remove / mixed-✅-and-incomplete → keep / no-merged-PR → incomplete. Integration test: synthetic TASKS.md with one shipped task + matching merged PR → daemon iteration produces a TASKS.md commit removing the block.
  - **Measurement**: `git log --grep "feat(<id>)" --since=30d | wc -l > A`; `git log --grep "duplicate of #" --since=30d | wc -l > B`; `B/A` ≤ 0.05 (less than 5% of merged PRs are subsequently re-created as duplicates).
  - **Pivot**: if auto-removal mis-fires (removes blocks for tasks that aren't really done), tighten the criteria — require explicit `**Status**: shipped` field rather than parsing acceptance checkboxes. Don't retire the rotation — manual TASKS.md curation at scale doesn't keep up with daemon pickTask rate.
  - **Anchor**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 (worker-1 re-created #309 as #343); rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure decision); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); composes with `daemon-duplicate-work-detection` (next).
  - **Risk**: medium. Aggressive auto-removal could lose in-flight task context. Mitigation: only fire when an explicit merged PR with matching title exists; keep `**Pushback**` field which operators can use to veto.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 — worker-1 re-created already-merged work multiple times.

- [ ] `daemon-duplicate-work-detection` — `pickAndClaim` should consult open + recently-merged PRs for a task ID and skip / fix-iterate instead of opening a duplicate
  - **ID**: daemon-duplicate-work-detection
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, task-discipline, minsky-loop-bug
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: Same 9h-window pattern: worker-1 picked `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate`, ran an iteration, opened #343 — without checking that #309 (already merged) covered the task and that #322 (still open) had the same content. Pre-registration: post-fix, before any `gh pr create`, the daemon queries `gh pr list --search "<task-id> in:title"` and refuses with `noop, exiting — task already in flight (PR #N)` if any open or recently-merged PR matches. Rolling-7d duplicate-PR rate → 0.
  - **Details**: (a) Pure helper `decideDuplicate({ taskId, prs }) → { kind: 'open' | 'merged' | 'none', prNumber? }`. (b) Daemon's `runClaimedIteration` calls this after `pickAndClaim` but before the `gh pr create`. (c) On `open` → daemon's brief becomes "rebase + iterate on PR #N" (the existing `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` flow). (d) On `merged` → daemon writes the TASKS.md task-completion edit (composes with `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion`) and exits noop. (e) Composes with `pickAndClaim` (already shipped #298) — claim layer prevents same-task selection across workers; this prevents same-task PR creation across iterations.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-duplicate-pr.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (pure decision), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-duplicate-detection.ts` + `.test.ts` (I/O wrapper), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (wire-in to spawn step).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/check-duplicate-pr.mjs`, `scripts/check-duplicate-pr.test.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-duplicate-detection.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-duplicate-detection.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `decideDuplicate`: no-pr / open-pr / merged-pr-this-week / merged-pr-old / multiple-prs.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot" --state closed --search "merged:>$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) closed-as-not-planned"` ≤ 1/week (counting daemon PRs closed as duplicate).
  - **Pivot**: if `gh pr list` query is too coarse (mis-classifies unrelated PRs that mention the task ID), restrict to PRs authored by the daemon and with branch names matching `daemon/<id>/<task-id>`.
  - **Anchor**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 (worker-1's #343 was a duplicate of merged #309); rule #2 (Strategy seam); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); composes with #298 (`pickAndClaim`) and `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion`.
  - **Risk**: low. The check is read-only against the GitHub API; the conservative default is `noop, exiting` rather than corrupting state.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 — worker-1's #343, #322 patterns.

- [ ] `daemon-pr-age-watchdog` — flag open daemon PRs with >N commits and >Mh wall-clock age as "rebase or close" candidates
  - **ID**: daemon-pr-age-watchdog
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, watchdog, optimize-thrash, minsky-loop-bug
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07: worker-1 stacked 11+ brief-compression commits onto PR #322 over ~5 hours without the PR ever merging — accumulated −4,195 bytes/iter of token savings that never landed because the PR stayed CONFLICTING. The optimize-thrash pattern: workers keep polishing a stuck PR instead of opening a fresh one or closing the stuck one. Pre-registration: post-fix, no daemon PR has >5 commits AND >2h age without a green merge or a forced-rebase action. Rolling-7d count of "thrashed" PRs (commit-count × age-hours product crossing threshold) ≤1.
  - **Details**: (a) New self-diagnose invariant `daemonPrThrashInvariant` checking `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot" --state open --json commits,createdAt`. (b) When a PR has commits>5 AND ageHours>2 AND mergeable!="MERGEABLE", it's flagged. (c) The daemon's iteration brief on next pick of the matching task ID becomes "rebase PR #N or close it; do NOT add more commits". (d) Visible-not-silent: invariant emits the thrash list as part of the daemon's startup span.
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (`daemonPrThrashInvariant`), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` (paired tests).
  - **Touches**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`
  - **Verification**: paired tests: pr-fresh / pr-aged-fresh-commits / pr-aged-many-commits / pr-merged.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq -e '[.[] | select(.id == "daemon-pr-thrash")] | length == 0'` exits 0 over 7d rolling.
  - **Pivot**: if the threshold (5 commits / 2h) is too aggressive (legitimate iterative substrate work is long-lived), raise to 10 commits / 4h. Don't retire the watchdog — the optimize-thrash cost is invisible without it.
  - **Anchor**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 (PR #322 with 11+ commits / 5h wall-clock); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); composes with `daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog`.
  - **Risk**: low. The invariant is read-only.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window 2026-05-07 — worker-1's #322 thrash, ~−4,195 bytes/iter savings stranded.
