- [ ] `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` — daemon runs all in-tree CI lints locally before opening any PR; refuses to open if any fails
  - **ID**: daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, self-improvement, pick-next
  - **Pick-next**: yes (operator-flagged 2026-05-05 — supervisor should pick this up immediately after its current task closes).
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: Empirical observation 2026-05-05 (88+ supervisor iterations, 3 shipped features): the daemon's first-pass output reliably fails CI lints I've already shipped (markdownlint MD001, rule-12 scope opt-out, rule-3 doc-first, rule-6 catch annotations, rule-7 chaos parsing). Each failure costs an operator-side babysitting commit. If the daemon runs `pnpm lint && pnpm typecheck && pnpm vitest run && pnpm exec markdownlint-cli2 "**/*.md" && node scripts/check-rule-*.mjs` locally on its branch BEFORE calling `gh pr create`, every failure becomes a daemon-side fix iteration instead of an operator-side cleanup PR. Pre-registration: post-fix, ≥80% of daemon-authored PRs open with zero red CI checks (vs the current ~0% — every PR has needed at least one lint fix).
  - **Details**: (a) New step in the daemon's iteration end-of-task path: before `gh pr create`, run the full CI lint stack as defined by `.github/workflows/ci.yml`'s `needs:` aggregator. (b) If any check fails, the daemon iterates *on the fix* (one more claude --print invocation with the failure message in the brief) instead of opening the PR. (c) Cap retries at 3 per task; if still failing, open the PR with a `Blocked: pre-pr-lint-failures` label so the operator sees it but the gate isn't hidden. (d) Reuses `lefthook`'s `pre-push` hook stack — that's the same gate humans already pass through; the daemon should pass it before opening the PR. (e) Add a self-diagnose invariant `daemon-pr-lint-pass-rate` that watches the rolling 30d pass-rate; if it drops below 80% the invariant fires, suggesting the lint stack drifted ahead of the daemon's brief.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/pre-pr-lint-gate.ts` + tests, `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` (the canonical invocation), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire-in), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (new invariant), `docs/daemon-pre-pr-gate.md`.
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/pre-pr-lint-gate.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/pre-pr-lint-gate.test.ts`, `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `docs/daemon-pre-pr-gate.md`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the gate (happy path / one lint fails / 3 retries exhausted / opt-out via Blocked label); integration test that simulates a daemon PR with a deliberate rule-#7 violation and verifies the daemon retries instead of opening.
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm daemon-pr-lint:metrics` prints "Verdict: OK" once the rolling 30d window holds ≥10 PRs (slice 10/N: `scripts/daemon-pr-lint-metrics.mjs` — versioned + paired-tested; the original task-block one-liner used `--author "@minsky-bot"` which never matches a PR in this repo, so the metric was unmeasurable as written). Threshold ≥0.80 pinned in `ROLLING_30D_MIN_PASS_RATE`; minimum sample size ≥10 in `ROLLING_30D_MIN_N`; both mirrored in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs § daemonPrLintPassRateInvariant`. Also: `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq -e '[.[] | select(.id == "daemon-pr-lint-pass-rate")] | length == 0'` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the lint stack takes >5 min on a daemon iteration (the iteration's claude --print spawn budget is finite), pivot to a *staged* gate — only the fast lints (biome, typecheck, rule-3, rule-12) run pre-PR; the slow ones (vitest, supervisor-integration, lighthouse) gate via CI as today. Pre-PR slow-lints are nice to have but not load-bearing; the fast ones close 80% of the failure modes.
  - **Anchor**: rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — the daemon runs the same gate humans run); rule #2 (the lint stack is already a Strategy seam — `.github/workflows/ci.yml` is the canonical list); rule #9 (the 80% pass-rate is the pre-registered metric); empirical 2026-05-05 (88 iterations, 3 shipped, 5+ operator cleanup PRs).
  - **Risk**: medium. Local lint stack drift vs CI is the main risk — the daemon could pass locally and fail in CI. Mitigation: the `scripts/run-pre-pr-lint-stack.mjs` is canonical; CI imports it. Both run the same script.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 user request — "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself" + my analysis "the daemon's first-pass output reliably fails CI lints" identified two daemon self-improvements. This is one.

- [ ] `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` — when daemon's PR fails CI, daemon automatically opens a fix commit on the same branch instead of noop-iterating
  - **ID**: daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, self-improvement, pick-next
  - **Pick-next**: yes (operator-flagged 2026-05-05 — supervisor should pick this up immediately after `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` ships).
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: Empirical observation 2026-05-05: with `cross-repo-ci-action` task block in TASKS.md (PR #167 open), the daemon iterated 80+ times producing brief refreshes / noops because the PR can't merge while CI fails, the task can't be removed while the PR is open, and the daemon won't fix CI on its own PR. **Deadlock pattern**. Fix: when the daemon detects its PR exists for the current task AND the PR has failing CI checks, the daemon iteration's brief becomes "fix CI failures on PR #N" instead of "redo the task". Operator never has to intervene; the daemon closes its own loop. Pre-registration: post-fix, time-from-PR-open-to-merge for daemon-authored PRs drops from "indefinite — operator must intervene" to "≤2 daemon iterations median".
  - **Details**: (a) In the daemon's task-pick step (right before claude --print), check if `gh pr list --head <branch>` returns an open PR for the current task ID's branch. (b) If yes AND the PR has failing CI checks, fetch the failure logs (`gh run view --log-failed <id>`) and pass them to claude --print as the brief: "Fix the failing CI checks on PR #N. Failure summary: <log excerpt>". (c) The daemon's claude pushes the fix commit; CI re-runs; next iteration checks again; loop until green or 3 retries. (d) After 3 retries, the daemon labels the PR `Blocked: daemon-stuck` and synthesises a new TASKS.md entry summarising what's blocked (operator-actionable). (e) Composes with `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` (above) — that gate cuts most failures at PR-open time; this gate handles the residue.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.ts` + tests (the decision function: open-PR-and-failing? → which-failure-class? → fix-brief), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.ts` + tests (the fix-iteration entry), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire-in).
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-pr-state.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon-fix-own-pr.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`
  - **Verification**: paired tests for daemon-pr-state (no-pr / pr-clean / pr-failing / pr-3-retries-exhausted); integration test that opens a synthetic PR with a deliberate failure, runs one daemon iteration, asserts a fix commit landed.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot" --state closed --search "merged:>$(date -v-30d -u +%Y-%m-%d)" --json createdAt,closedAt --jq '[.[] | (((.closedAt|fromdate) - (.createdAt|fromdate)) / 60)] | sort | .[length/2|floor]'` (median minutes from PR open to merge for daemon PRs over rolling 30d) ≤ 240 (4h — accounts for human review on substantive changes; CI-fix-only iterations close in <30min).
  - **Pivot**: if the daemon's fix iteration takes >3 retries reliably (>20% of failing PRs), the failure classes the daemon faces aren't fixable by claude --print alone — pivot to a "human escalation" mode: after 1 retry, the daemon labels the PR `needs-operator` and stops iterating. Don't build infinite-retry — that wastes the budget without producing value.
  - **Anchor**: rule #6 (let-it-crash AT the boundary — the daemon's own PR is its boundary; a green CI is the contract); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6 (the operator-escape-hatch is `Blocked: daemon-stuck`); rule #9 (the 4h median is the pre-registered metric); empirical 2026-05-05 (PR #167's 80-iteration deadlock).
  - **Risk**: medium-high. The daemon could iterate destructively if its fix-brief is wrong (e.g., suppressing a lint instead of fixing the violation). Mitigation: the cap-3 retries + `Blocked: daemon-stuck` escalation; also, the in-tree pre-push lint stack catches obvious destructive changes.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 user request — "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself" + my analysis identified the deadlock. This is the second daemon self-improvement.

- [ ] `daemon-self-detect-throughput-issues` — daemon's self-introspection runs identify low-throughput patterns (high noop rate, deadlock, lint-fail loops) and file them as P0 tasks autonomously
  - **ID**: daemon-self-detect-throughput-issues
  - **Tags**: p0, self-diagnose, meta, supervisor, observability
  - **Pick-next**: queue after the two above ship (depends on their measurement infrastructure).
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator-promoted 2026-05-05 (must deliver today): user "ensure that it gets delivered today" after observing the operator-spotted #180/#181/#182 collision pattern that this task would have caught.
  - **Hypothesis**: Operator request 2026-05-05: "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself". The two tasks above (`daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate`, `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure`) were authored by the operator after observing 88 iterations of low throughput. **Minsky should have noticed first.** The self-diagnose pattern (PR #156 / scripts/self-diagnose.mjs) is the natural surface — extend it with throughput-class invariants: (1) `daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high` (>3 consecutive iterations on the same task with no commit → fire), (2) `daemon-pr-stuck-on-ci-failure` (≥2 failed CI runs on a daemon PR with no daemon-authored fix commit → fire), (3) `daemon-iteration-vs-shipped-ratio` (rolling 7d: shipped-PR-count / iteration-count ≥ 0.05 — i.e., at least 1 PR per 20 iterations; below that fires), (4) `daemon-in-flight-pr-collision` — observed 2026-05-05 on PRs #180/#181/#182: daemon shipped 3 overlapping PRs for `daily-changelog-for-humans` because each iteration didn't check `gh pr list --head` for an existing branch on the same task before authoring a new one; invariant fires when ≥2 open PRs exist with overlapping file-sets AND the same task-id in their commit message; suggested-fix: in `runIteration` pre-spawn step, query `gh pr list --json files,headRefName --search "is:open"`, refuse to author a new PR if any open PR's files overlap >50% with the current task's expected file-set, OR continue work on the existing branch instead. (5) `daemon-task-id-staleness` — when a task block has been removed from TASKS.md but the daemon still has work in flight referencing it, refuse to keep iterating on the stale task. Each invariant fires → emits a P0 TASKS.md entry the daemon can pick up. Pre-registration: post-shipping, the gap between "operator notices an inefficiency" and "task block exists for it" drops from "operator-author-time" (hours-days) to "≤1 day" (the rolling-window measurement frequency). Iron-rule: if the invariant set itself becomes the bottleneck (false positive rate ≥ 20%/week), tighten the thresholds before retiring.
  - **Details**: (a) Three new invariants in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (one per throughput failure mode above). (b) Each invariant reads from `.minsky/tick-loop.out.log` (iteration counts) + `gh pr list` (PR state). (c) The supervisor's existing self-diagnose-on-boot path (already wired in `distribution/systemd/run-tick-loop.sh`) picks them up automatically — no new wire-in needed. (d) Each invariant's `suggestedTaskTitle` matches a known P0 pattern (mirrors the format of `daemon-pre-pr-lint-gate` / `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` so the daemon can synthesise without re-deriving the brief from scratch).
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (3 new invariant exports + their `defaultInvariants()` registration), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` (paired tests for each invariant), `docs/self-diagnose-throughput-invariants.md`.
  - **Touches**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs`, `docs/self-diagnose-throughput-invariants.md`
  - **Verification**: ≥6 paired tests (each invariant: pass case + fail case); live regression check — re-run against the 2026-05-05 supervisor state (88 iterations, 3 PRs) and assert all 3 invariants would have fired.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq '[.[] | select(.id | startswith("daemon-"))] | length'` returns the count of throughput-class violations on the live supervisor. After this task ships, that count gates dogfood-loop health: 0 = healthy; ≥1 = a daemon self-improvement task is needed (and the invariant has filed it).
  - **Pivot**: if the invariants fire false-positives ≥20%/week (e.g., a legitimate long-running task is flagged as deadlock), tighten the thresholds OR add per-task-class exclusions. Don't retire the architecture; tune it.
  - **Anchor**: Liskov 1987 (invariants as substrate of correctness); rule #9 (each invariant pre-registered with its hypothesis + threshold); the operator's 2026-05-05 directive "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself" — load-bearing; the existing self-diagnose pattern (PR #156) as the substrate.
  - **Risk**: medium. The invariants depend on the daemon's iteration-log format being stable — if a future PR changes the span shape, the invariants silently stop working. Mitigation: paired tests pin the format; rule-4 OTEL coverage is the canonical schema; if the format changes, the tests fail loudly first.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 user request "I expect minsky to come up with these issues itself, add a p0 task to update that investigation". This block IS that investigation — meta-self-diagnose, the next layer up from PR #156.

- [ ] `self-diagnose-iteration-log-probe-format` — fix the `recentIterations` probe in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` so it actually parses `.minsky/tick-loop.out.log`
  - **ID**: self-diagnose-iteration-log-probe-format
  - **Tags**: p0, self-diagnose, follow-up
  - **Estimate**: 1d
  - **Hypothesis**: Discovered 2026-05-05 dogfooding PR #184: the `recentIterations` probe expects `JSON.parse(line)` against `{evt: "iteration", taskId, committedSha, ts}` shape, but the supervisor actually emits `[span] tick-loop.iteration {"iteration.index":N,"iteration.status":"completed","task.id":"...","iteration.reason":"..."}` (OTEL span-attribute style, no `committedSha` field). Live `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json` returned `[]` even when the daemon was on iteration 27 of consecutive noops on the same task — `daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high` should have fired but couldn't because `readIterationsFromLog` returned `[]`. Pre-registration: after the fix, running self-diagnose against a log with ≥4 consecutive non-committed iterations on one taskId surfaces a `daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high` finding. Two parts: (a) align the parser with the live log format (`[span] tick-loop.iteration` prefix + dotted-attribute fields), (b) add a structured `iteration.committed` boolean to the supervisor's iteration span so "noop" detection isn't a heuristic over `iteration.reason` text.
  - **Details**: (a) Update `parseIterationLogLine` in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` to strip the `[span] tick-loop.iteration` prefix and read `iteration.index`, `task.id`, `iteration.reason`. (b) Heuristic for `committed`: `iteration.reason.match(/PR #\d+ (opened|merged|landed)/)` OR `git log --since=<iteration.timestamp>` shows a new commit. (c) OR (preferred) extend the supervisor span emit in `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` to include `iteration.committed: boolean` and `iteration.committedSha: string` directly — then this probe stays simple. (d) Add a regression test that loads a captured-from-prod log fragment and asserts the invariants fire/don't fire as expected.
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (parser), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` (regression test against a captured supervisor log fragment), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (optional: structured `iteration.committed` field).

  - **Verification**: replaying the 2026-05-05 supervisor log through `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json` MUST surface `daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high` (the daemon spent iterations 25-27 noop'ing on `daily-changelog-for-humans`).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq '[.[] | select(.id == "daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high")] | length'` returns ≥1 when invoked against a log with ≥`threshold` consecutive noops; returns 0 otherwise. Live regression: replaying the 2026-05-05 log produces exactly the finding.
  - **Pivot**: if the heuristic for "committed" produces ≥10% false positives over a week, switch to the structured-field approach (option c) — don't retire the invariant.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) parser handles `[span] tick-loop.iteration {...}` lines; (2) regression test loads real supervisor log fragment; (3) `daemon-noop-iteration-rate-too-high` fires on the 2026-05-05 noop streak when replayed.
  - **Anchor**: rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); rule #2 (Strategy seam — production probe vs synthetic test data); Liskov 1987 (invariants must observe the actual system, not a hypothetical one).
  - **Risk**: low. Pure parser fix; substrate already shipped in PR #184.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 dogfood — the operator ran `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json` against a supervisor stuck in a 4-iteration noop streak; the new throughput invariants returned no findings because the probe couldn't read the live log format.

- [ ] `daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens` — every iteration tries to improve daemon's own speed and decrease token consumption (one measurable optimization per loop)
  - **ID**: daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, optimization, self-improvement
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/**`, `scripts/iteration-cost-rolling-p95.mjs`
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator-promoted 2026-05-05 ("Add p0 so that in every loop of minsky it tries to improve speed of itself and decrease tokens consumption").
  - **Estimate**: 1w (substrate slice ships in initial PR; subsequent slices ratchet)
  - **Hypothesis**: The daemon currently iterates without a per-iteration optimization gate — it ships task-progress code, but the daemon itself never consciously trims its own brief, eliminates redundant `gh` round-trips, or compresses log lines. Over hundreds of iterations this leaves measurable speed + token waste compounding silently. Pre-registration: with the optimization-discipline gate in `buildDaemonBrief` (this PR's substrate slice), every iteration emits either an optimization commit OR an `optimization: none-this-iteration` reason — visible-not-silent. Over a 14-day window, the rolling-7d daemon iteration p95 wall-time drops by ≥10% AND/OR rolling-7d input-token median drops by ≥10%. If neither moves, the gate is generating noise — pivot to a stricter eligibility filter (≥10-byte savings minimum) before retiring.
  - **Details**: (a) Substrate (this PR): extend `buildDaemonBrief` with an `## Optimization-discipline gate` section listing eligible optimization patterns (brief-shrinking, cached-prompt extension, skip-earlier gate, log-line dedup, round-trip elimination), an anti-vanity guard (must be measurable in tokens / wall-time / round-trip count), and a `none-this-iteration` carve-out. (b) Follow-up slice: per-iteration metrics — emit `tick-loop.iteration.duration_ms`, `tick-loop.iteration.tokens_in_delta`, `tick-loop.iteration.tokens_out_delta` as span attributes. (c) Follow-up slice: `daemon-iteration-cost-regression` self-diagnose invariant that fires when rolling p95 of either metric increases >20% week-over-week. (d) Follow-up slice: dashboard's "Throughput" section adds a "Cost" tile showing those rolling p95s. (e) Each shipped iteration explicitly notes the optimization (or its absence) in its iteration reason — this is the operator-readable feedback signal.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (extend `buildDaemonBrief`), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.test.ts` (paired tests for optimization gate), follow-ups: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (per-iteration cost spans), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (regression invariant), `novel/dashboard-web/src/throughput.ts` (Cost tile).
  - **Verification**: rolling-7d daemon iteration p95 wall-time on `main` measured at fix-time + 14d via `node scripts/iteration-cost-rolling-p95.mjs --window=7d` (script in follow-up slice).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/iteration-cost-rolling-p95.mjs --window=7d --metric=duration_ms` returns ≥10% decrease vs. the baseline measured at substrate-merge time AND/OR `--metric=tokens_in_delta` returns ≥10% decrease. Concrete: baseline p95 wall-time ~`<measured-at-substrate-merge>` ms; target p95 ≤ baseline × 0.9 by day 14 OR documented why not. Daemon iteration log carries either a commit-bound optimization OR an explicit `optimization: none-this-iteration: <reason>` line per iteration — `grep -c 'optimization:' .minsky/tick-loop.out.log | awk '$1 == iteration_count'` (every iteration accounted for).
  - **Pivot**: if iterations ship 1-byte/whitespace "optimizations" to satisfy the gate, tighten the eligibility to ≥10-byte savings minimum or a measurable wall-time delta of ≥1ms before retiring. If the metric-regression invariant fires false-positively due to CI runner variance, switch from p95 to p50 trimmed mean. Don't retire the gate — silence-is-failure (Beyer SRE 2016) means an iteration without a stated optimization choice is itself a bug.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `buildDaemonBrief` carries the optimization-discipline gate; (2) every daemon iteration's reason contains either an optimization commit reference OR `optimization: none-this-iteration: <reason>`; (3) span attributes for per-iteration duration_ms + tokens_in_delta + tokens_out_delta land on the existing `tick-loop.iteration` span; (4) `daemon-iteration-cost-regression` self-diagnose invariant ships; (5) dashboard's Throughput section gains a Cost tile.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-05 — "Add p0 so that in every loop of minsky it tries to improve speed of itself and decrease tokens consumption"; rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6 (silence-is-failure); rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure builder fed by tasksMd content); composes with `daemon-self-detect-throughput-issues` (#184) — defensive (catch regressions) vs. offensive (compress proactively).
  - **Risk**: low. Substrate slice is a pure-builder extension covered by paired tests; follow-up slices add measurement infrastructure, none of which changes runtime behaviour beyond the existing tick loop.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 operator directive — "Add p0 so that in every loop of minsky it tries to improve speed of itself and decrease tokens consumption. Then actually implement it, then continue minsky."

- [ ] `daemon-pr-self-grade-format-baked` — bake the strict pr-self-grade format into `buildDaemonBrief` so daemon never ships malformed `**Match:**` blocks
  - **ID**: daemon-pr-self-grade-format-baked
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, supervisor, throughput, brief, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.test.ts`, `scripts/pre-push-pr-self-grade.mjs`
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: Discovered via 2026-05-05 speed-comparison measurement (operator-vs-daemon PR open→merge): daemon ships PR bodies with `**Predicted.**` / `**Match:** Yes` (period or colon-inside-bold), but the `pr-self-grade` lint regex requires `**Predicted**:` / `**Match**: yes` (colon-outside-bold, lowercase value). Daemon hits this on ~10% of PRs, costing 1-2 fix iterations each (~30min wasted per occurrence; observed concretely on PR #201 today, two iterations). Pre-registration: with the format baked into the brief as a copy-paste-ready template, daemon's pr-self-grade fail rate drops below 2%/week (down from observed ~10%); median PR open→merge for daemon drops by ≥3 minutes (the median fix-and-rebase round-trip for this specific failure).
  - **Details**: (a) Extend `buildDaemonBrief` with a `## PR self-grade template (copy-paste verbatim)` section emitting the exact strict format: `- **Predicted**: …` / `- **Observed**: …` / `- **Match**: yes | no | partial` / `- **Lesson**: …`. (b) Add an explicit "DO NOT MODIFY THIS FORMAT" anti-rewrite directive — claude tends to reformat to its own bold/period preference. (c) Add a paired test that asserts the brief contains the exact substrings the lint regex matches. (d) Optional: add a pre-push hook that runs `node scripts/check-pr-self-grade.mjs <pr-body-file>` before opening the PR (bake-out the failure rather than catching it post-spawn).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (extend `buildDaemonBrief`), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.test.ts` (paired tests for the new section), optionally `scripts/pre-push-pr-self-grade.mjs`.
  - **Verification**: spawn daemon iteration with the new brief; assert the produced PR body matches `scripts/check-pr-self-grade.mjs` regex on first try (no fix iteration). Replay PR #201's body shape: with old brief → fails; with new brief → passes.
  - **Measurement**: rolling 7d post-merge: `gh pr list --author '@me' --state all --search 'created:>=YYYY-MM-DD' --json statusCheckRollup --jq '[.[] | select(.statusCheckRollup[] | select(.name=="pr-self-grade" and .conclusion=="FAILURE"))] | length / [.] | length'` returns < 0.02 (was ~0.10 pre-fix).
  - **Pivot**: if daemon still mis-formats despite the baked template, switch from "copy-paste this template" to "the harness writes the self-grade block FROM YOUR ITERATION OUTPUT" — i.e., move format generation out of claude's hands entirely. Don't retire the lint.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) brief carries copy-paste-ready PR self-grade template; (2) anti-rewrite directive present; (3) paired test asserts substring match; (4) post-merge 7d rolling pr-self-grade fail rate < 2%.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-05 operator-vs-daemon speed measurement (median open→merge: operator ~4 min, daemon ~23 min; ~6× gap); rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure brief builder); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — the lint regex IS the format spec); composes with `daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens`.
  - **Risk**: low. Pure-builder extension; covered by paired tests; the lint regex is already deterministic.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 operator directive — "Measure speed of implementing a minsky feature here in claude code vs implementing it through minsky itself. Open tasks to improve it." Speed-comparison surfaced PR-self-grade-format-loop as a recurring 30min-cost failure mode.

- [ ] `daemon-cross-iteration-prompt-cache` — share `claude --print` prompt prefix across iterations to hit Anthropic's prompt cache
  - **ID**: daemon-cross-iteration-prompt-cache
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, supervisor, throughput, prompt-cache, optimization, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs`, `docs/prompt-cache-discipline.md`, `scripts/measure-prompt-cache-hit-rate.mjs`
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Hypothesis**: Discovered via 2026-05-05 speed-comparison: operator's foreground Claude session ships PRs in median ~4 min vs daemon's ~23 min — a 6× gap. Major contributor: the daemon spawns a fresh `claude --print` per iteration, so Anthropic's prompt cache (5min TTL, ≥1024 tokens) never hits. The operator's continuous session benefits from prompt-cache reads at 1/10th the cost of fresh tokens (per Anthropic's Sept 2025 caching docs). Pre-registration: with cross-iteration prompt-prefix sharing live (e.g., daemon emits the brief with cache-control breakpoints at the policies, glossary, and pattern-index sections; subsequent iterations within the 5min TTL window reuse the cache), per-iteration token cost drops by ≥40% AND/OR per-iteration wall-time drops by ≥20%. If neither moves, prompt cache isn't the bottleneck — pivot to investigating the tool-call thrash hypothesis (operator-driven session vs daemon's spawn issues different number of tool calls per task).
  - **Details**: (a) Audit `buildDaemonBrief` output for cache-friendliness — order content from most-stable (rule citations, glossary anchors, file-level policies) at the top to most-volatile (current task block, today's iteration log) at the bottom. Anthropic caches the longest-common-prefix; volatility breaks the chain. (b) Add `cache_control: { type: "ephemeral" }` annotations at the policy/glossary/pattern-index boundaries when constructing the API call. (c) Wire daemon to use the Anthropic SDK directly (not `claude --print`) so it can set `cache_control` headers — OR document why `claude --print` already supports this (likely yes via system prompt caching). (d) Measure baseline iteration cost via the new `tick-loop.iteration.tokens_in_delta` span attribute (filed as slice 2 of `daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens`); ship the cache change; remeasure. (e) Note: prompt cache is per-session — within a 5min TTL window, multiple spawns hit the same cache. Daemon's tick interval is 5min by default, so rapid-fire iterations would benefit; the pivot is the tick interval (already shipping in CI today via the watchdog).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (re-order `buildDaemonBrief` for cache-friendliness), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (if SDK swap needed; investigate first), `docs/prompt-cache-discipline.md` (the operator-facing explanation), follow-up: `scripts/measure-prompt-cache-hit-rate.mjs` (rolling-7d cache-hit telemetry).
  - **Verification**: replay 24h of daemon iterations against an Anthropic-API-stub that records prompt-cache attempts; assert ≥80% of iterations within a 5min window land cache reads (vs 0% baseline).
  - **Measurement**: `tick-loop.iteration.tokens_in_delta` rolling-7d median drops by ≥40% post-merge (baseline measured at substrate-merge time of `daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens`'s slice 2). AND `tick-loop.iteration.duration_ms` rolling-7d median drops by ≥20%.
  - **Pivot**: if `claude --print` doesn't expose `cache_control` and the SDK swap is too invasive, pivot to "shrink the brief instead" — apply the `optimization-discipline gate` (#207) recursively for 4 weeks targeting the brief itself; if that gets the duration delta but not the token delta, retire the cache approach with a documented "stuck behind CLI tooling — revisit on Anthropic SDK upgrade".
  - **Acceptance**: (1) brief content re-ordered for cache-friendliness; (2) cache hit rate ≥80% within 5min windows (measured via the SDK-level cache_creation_input_tokens vs cache_read_input_tokens fields); (3) per-iteration token cost ≥40% lower; (4) per-iteration wall-time ≥20% lower; (5) `docs/prompt-cache-discipline.md` documents the contract.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-05 operator-vs-daemon speed measurement (6× median gap); Anthropic prompt-caching documentation (Sept 2025; 1024-token min, 5min TTL, 90% cache-read discount); rule #1 (don't reinvent — Anthropic ships the cache, we use it); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `claude --print` is the seam; SDK swap is a one-file change at `bin/tick-loop.mjs`); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); composes with `daemon-self-optimize-speed-tokens` (offensive — compress brief), this task (offensive — cache the prefix).
  - **Risk**: medium. Requires either a documented `claude --print` cache-control surface OR an SDK-level swap. Mitigation: investigate first (slice 0 — research, 1d); only commit to implementation if `claude --print` already supports it.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 operator directive — "Measure speed of implementing a minsky feature here in claude code vs implementing it through minsky itself. Open tasks to improve it." Speed-comparison showed daemon at 6× operator's median open→merge; prompt cache miss is the leading single contributor (per Anthropic's 90% cache-read discount math).

- [ ] `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` — launch N non-conflicting Minsky processes on the same repo via Claude Code's native `--worktree` flag + `flock`-based TASKS.md row claim
  - **ID**: daemon-parallel-worktree-launch
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, supervisor, throughput, parallel, worktree, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/**`, `scripts/check-tasks-md-touches-glob.mjs`, `.gitattributes`, `pnpm-workspace.yaml`
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator-promoted 2026-05-05 ("Add p0 to implement parallel launch of multiple non conflicting minsky processes on the same repo").
  - **Estimate**: 1w (substrate slice in 1d; the rest ratchets)
  - **Hypothesis**: The daemon currently runs serially — one tick = one `claude --print` spawn. Operator throughput is bounded by p95 single-iteration wall-time × tasks-in-queue. With N parallel workers each owning its own git worktree + `flock`-claimed TASKS.md row, throughput multiplies (up to the API rate-limit ceiling). 2026 research surveyed 14+ existing tools; Claude Code's native `--worktree` flag (Cherny, Feb 2026) provides the per-process isolation primitive for free. Pre-registration: post-implementation, with N=3 workers, daily merged-PR count ≥ 1.5× the serial-baseline measured over a 7-day window. If <1.2×, parallel coordination overhead dominates — pivot to N=2 OR retire to serial-only with documented reason. **Decision: build-on-top-of Claude Code `--worktree` + thin `flock` claim layer.** Reject Conductor / Crystal / Vibe Kanban (GUI-first); reject Composio agent-orchestrator (would replace Minsky's own loop); reject Redis/etcd locks (single-host overkill per Kleppmann 2016).
  - **Details**: (a) Substrate slice — `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-claim.ts` exposes `acquireTaskClaim(taskId, opts): { release, expiresAt }` using `flock(2)` on `.minsky/locks/task-<id>.lock` with `LOCK_NB`; lease TTL written into the lock body so external operators can see who holds what. (b) Slice 2 — `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` learns `--worker-id <n>` and `--workers-total <N>`; per-worker spawn invokes `claude --worktree daemon-<worker-id>-<task-id>` (Anthropic's flag, auto-cleanup on session end). (c) Slice 3 — TASKS.md task-row `**Touches**: <glob>[, <glob>…]` field + pre-spawn glob-overlap check against open daemon PRs (`gh pr list --json files`). Refuse to start the worker if any open PR's files overlap any `Touches:` glob of the candidate task. (d) Slice 4 — sweeper: every tick, run `git worktree prune --expire 1.day.ago`, unlink `.git/index.lock` files older than 5 minutes (the Claude Code #11005 mitigation), expire stale TTL claims. (e) Slice 5 — register Mergiraf as `merge=mergiraf` in `.gitattributes` so cross-worker rebase storms self-resolve on overlapping files (33 languages, tree-sitter-backed). (f) Slice 6 — `pnpm-workspace.yaml` adds `enableGlobalVirtualStore: true` so per-worktree `node_modules` doesn't blow disk. (g) Slice 7 — observability: per-worker `tick-loop.worker.<id>.iteration` spans; new `claim_collision`, `stale_lock_recovered`, `worktree_orphan_pruned` counters in dashboard. Document the failure modes inventory (see Research notes below) in `novel/tick-loop/PARALLEL_WORKTREE.md`.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-claim.ts` + `.test.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-claim.flock-helper.mjs` (thin native-flock wrapper or `proper-lockfile` adoption), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (`--worker-id` / `--workers-total` flags + per-worker dispatch), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (pre-spawn `gh pr list` glob-overlap check), `scripts/check-tasks-md-touches-glob.mjs` (lint that every task block carries a `**Touches**:` field), `.gitattributes` (mergiraf driver), `pnpm-workspace.yaml` (`enableGlobalVirtualStore`), `novel/tick-loop/PARALLEL_WORKTREE.md` (failure-modes doc), `novel/dashboard-web/src/parallel-workers.ts` + tests (per-worker tile).
  - **Verification**: launch 3 workers on a 5-task TASKS.md; assert each worker picks a different task within ≤500ms via `flock` (no two workers can hold the same `.minsky/locks/task-<id>.lock`). Then crash one worker mid-iteration; assert the other 2 finish, and the next tick reclaims the abandoned task without manual intervention. Replay the 2026-05-05 #198/#199 collision pattern: with the pre-spawn glob-overlap check live, the second worker's spawn refuses with `collision-prevented: PR #198 already touches files X,Y`.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/parallel-worker-throughput.mjs --window=7d --workers=3` returns ≥1.5× the serial-baseline merged-PR/day rate. Concrete: baseline serial daemon (today) = ~10 PRs/day; target with N=3 ≥ 15 PRs/day. AND `grep -c 'collision-prevented:' .minsky/tick-loop.out.log` is ≥1 the first time two workers pick overlapping tasks (proves the pre-spawn check fires). AND the rolling-7d ghost-lock recovery counter is non-zero (proves the sweeper found and recovered at least one stale `.git/index.lock`).
  - **Pivot**: if N=3 produces <1.2× serial-baseline, pivot to N=2 — the API rate-limit (per Anthropic's published 2-4 concurrent ceiling) is the real bottleneck. If `flock`-based TTL leases prove too coarse (workers crash and steal each other's tasks under 30m), switch to `fcntl(F_SETLK)` byte-range OFD locks (POSIX, finer granularity) before retiring. If Mergiraf produces ≥3 wrong auto-merges/week, demote it to advisory-only and re-add a human/CI gate at the merge step. **Don't retire parallelism** — even N=2 is a strict improvement; the floor is "at least one extra worker available for `daemon-fix-own-pr-on-ci-failure` while the primary keeps shipping".
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `acquireTaskClaim` ships with paired tests covering happy-path / crash-recovery / stale-TTL-eviction; (2) `--worker-id`/`--workers-total` CLI flags route correctly; (3) `**Touches**: <glob>` field lints clean across TASKS.md (CI gate); (4) pre-spawn glob-overlap check refuses with `collision-prevented:` reason when an open daemon PR overlaps any `Touches:` glob; (5) `git worktree prune` + stale `.git/index.lock` sweeper run every tick; (6) Mergiraf registered as `.gitattributes` driver; (7) `pnpm-workspace.yaml` enables `enableGlobalVirtualStore`; (8) `novel/tick-loop/PARALLEL_WORKTREE.md` documents the 12 known pitfalls (pre-commit hooks per worktree, submodules, ghost locks, etc.); (9) parallel-worker dashboard tile ships; (10) launching 3 workers shows zero claim collisions across 100 iterations in CI.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-05 — "Add p0 to implement parallel launch of multiple non conflicting minsky processes on the same repo. I assume we need bulletproof git worktrees solution. Extensively research existing solutions and try adopting them"; rule #1 (don't reinvent the wheel — adopt Claude Code's native `--worktree`); rule #2 (Strategy seam — claim layer fed by injected I/O); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD); Kleppmann 2016 ("How to do distributed locking" — single-host `flock` is sufficient); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6 (silence-is-failure for stale locks).
  - **Risk**: medium. Git is fundamentally a single-process tool — concurrent operations across worktrees can corrupt `.git/`. Mitigations: serialize `git fetch` via `flock .git/fetch.lock`; sweeper recovers ghost `.git/index.lock` (Claude Code #11005); per-worker branch namespace `daemon/<worker-id>/<task-id>` makes branch collisions impossible; Mergiraf reduces post-merge rebase pain. Pre-commit hooks-per-worktree (issue #808) and submodule-in-worktree (issue #3032) are real but rare in this repo's surface.
  - **Research** (2026-05-05): full research report in branch `feat/file-daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` git history; key findings: (i) Claude Code's `--worktree` flag (Cherny, Feb 2026) is the per-process isolation primitive — auto-cleanup on session end. (ii) `flock(2)` on a per-task lockfile is the right coordination primitive for single-host (per Kleppmann). (iii) Mergiraf (mergiraf.org) is a tree-sitter-backed semantic merge driver — 33 languages, 428/7415 kernel conflicts auto-resolved in published benchmarks. (iv) pnpm's `enableGlobalVirtualStore` cuts per-worktree `node_modules` from ~2GB to ~50MB. (v) Known sharp edges: pre-commit hooks install per-worktree (`pre-commit/pre-commit#808`), submodules + worktrees + pre-commit corrupts the submodule repo (`pre-commit/pre-commit#3032`), Claude Code background ops leak `.git/index.lock` (`anthropics/claude-code#11005`). (vi) Rejected: Conductor / Crystal / Nimbalyst / Vibe Kanban / Superset (GUI-first); Composio agent-orchestrator (would replace Minsky's own loop); dagger/container-use (Docker dep we don't need); Redis/etcd (overkill); CRDTs (overkill — `flock`+fsync gives strict serializability free); git-spice/git-branchless (different problem — solves stacked-PR rebase, can be added later). (vii) Anchors: [Cherny worktree announcement](https://www.threads.com/@boris_cherny/post/DVAAnexgRUj/), [Claude Code subagents docs](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/sub-agents), [dagger/container-use](https://github.com/dagger/container-use), [Mergiraf](https://mergiraf.org/), [pnpm git-worktrees guide](https://pnpm.io/next/git-worktrees), [git-worktree(1)](https://git-scm.com/docs/git-worktree), [Kleppmann distributed locking](https://martin.kleppmann.com/2016/02/08/how-to-do-distributed-locking.html).
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) lease TTL value — what's p99 tick duration in current `tick-loop.out.log`? Need histogram. (b) worker count per host — published wisdom says 2–4 concurrent Claude sessions before rate-limits dominate; does Minsky's API class admit more? (c) `Touches:` spec — extend the markdown task-block (low-friction) or add a sidecar `tasks.lock.json` (machine-clean)? (d) Mergiraf trust level — auto-resolve silently, or always require human/CI gate? (e) telemetry — does the existing observability surface emit `claim_collision` / `stale_lock_recovered` / `worktree_orphan_pruned` counters? Without those, no measurable hypothesis (rule #9).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-05 operator directive — "Add p0 to implement parallel launch of multiple non conflicting minsky processes on the same repo. I assume we need bulletproof git worktrees solution. Extensively research existing solutions and try adopting them. Do more research".
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, below) — this block provides the worker-spawn substrate (`flock` claim, `claude --worktree`, glob-overlap check). The parent adds role-pin + orchestrator entrypoint + cross-layer chaos.

- [ ] `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` — Claude (top layer, brain) fans work out to N local-model workers in git worktrees; chaos-engineered cross-layer stability
  - **ID**: claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, orchestrator, local-llm, parallel, worktree, chaos-engineering, role-separation
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/**`, `novel/sidecar-bootstrap/**`, `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`, `scripts/chaos-*.mjs`, `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md`
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10, "I want claude to be the brains of this (top layer) and everything below to be run by local models but with full list of features of claude … extremely stable about this, with chaos engineering and other minsky principles".
  - **Estimate**: 4d (composes three existing blocks; net new code is the role-pin + entrypoint + cross-layer chaos invariants)
  - **Composes**: this block is the parent that wires three already-filed substrates plus one already-shipped layer into one coherent operator surface:
    - parent of `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` (P0, line 426) — provides `flock` claim, `claude --worktree`, glob-overlap check, mergiraf, sweeper. Worker-spawn shape lives there.
    - parent of `task-aware-model-router` (P1, line 544) — provides the 4-bucket classifier + provider router. This task adds the **role-pin override** (orchestrator iterations always Opus; worker iterations always local-first under `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`).
    - parent of `spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring` (P2, line 717) — provides the watchdog substrate (kill stuck child, rebase stuck PR, body-patch). This task adds the **cross-layer** chaos slice (orchestrator-death-recovery; worker-hang-detection-from-orchestrator-side).
    - builds on `llm-provider-selector` (`novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts`, shipped via #358/#365/#401) — the existing `decideProvider` is the per-process gate; this task threads the role into its input.
  - **Hypothesis**: Operator 2026-05-10 wants the two-layer architecture: (i) **orchestrator** runs from a Claude Code session (Opus reasoning over the queue, decomposition, code-review of worker output, merge decisions); (ii) **workers** are local-Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B via aider in `git worktree`s, one per claimed task. Today every iteration calls `decideProvider` with the same inputs, so a worker iteration that exits the budget-paused band routes back to Claude — burning the cap that should belong to the orchestrator. Pre-registration: post-fix, with N=4 workers + 1 orchestrator running for a 24h window, **(a)** orchestrator process consumes ≥90 % of the Claude tokens spent in the window (the 5h-cap envelope is defended for the brain), **(b)** worker processes consume ≥80 % of their iterations on local-Qwen (provider attribute on `tick-loop.iteration` spans), **(c)** sustained merged-PR throughput ≥ 1.5× the serial-baseline (same ratchet as #daemon-parallel-worktree-launch), **(d)** zero operator-manual-intervention events triggered by cross-layer failure (orchestrator crash mid-fanout, worker hang during harvest). If (a) <70 %, the role-pin is leaking — workers are stealing Claude budget; pivot the router to a hard env-gated check rather than a soft preference. If (b) <50 %, local-Qwen is failing too often on the worker bucket distribution; pivot worker default to Sonnet/Haiku-cheap-cloud rather than local. If (c) <1.2×, parallel coordination dominates; pivot to N=2. If (d) ≥1/day sustained 7 days, the chaos invariants are insufficient; pivot to per-worker process-supervisor (launchd KeepAlive per worker) before adding more N.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet; each slice is one PR with paired tests + rule-#9 self-grade):
    - **Slice 1 — role-pinned provider input** (1d): extend `decideProvider`'s input shape with `role: "orchestrator" | "worker"` and a per-role default-provider table. Orchestrator role: hard-pinned to `claude-opus` regardless of budget state, with the existing circuit-break-and-notify path being the *only* exception (when Opus is genuinely unavailable, the orchestrator pauses rather than degrading — degraded brains across an N-worker fanout is worse than waiting). Worker role: defaults to local-Qwen if `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` (the env var shipped via #401), with auto-promote to cloud per #task-aware-model-router slice 4's quality-gate. Ship paired tests for the 8 cells (2 roles × 4 budget states).
    - **Slice 2 — orchestrator entrypoint** (1d): `pnpm minsky orchestrate --workers=N [--dry-run]` in `novel/tick-loop/bin/orchestrate.mjs`. The orchestrator spawns N background workers (each = `pnpm minsky --worker-id <i> --workers-total <N> --role=worker`), tails their `.minsky/workers/<id>.log`, and harvests their PR URLs as they ship. The orchestrator's own iteration is a Claude Code session that picks the next decomposition target from TASKS.md and emits N non-overlapping `Touches:`-globbed task assignments to the workers via `.minsky/workers/<id>.assignment.json` (a Strategy seam — the workers read assignments, not pull from TASKS.md, eliminating the row-claim race for the assigned set; the `flock` claim from #daemon-parallel-worktree-launch remains for the *unassigned* tail of TASKS.md so workers don't starve when the orchestrator is between fanouts). Operator opens Claude Code, types `pnpm minsky orchestrate --workers=4`, and the brain-vs-hands separation is live.
    - **Slice 3 — cross-layer chaos invariants** (1d): three new invariants in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + paired tests, following the `self-diagnose-on-start` (#self-diagnose-on-start) authoring pattern:
      - `orchestrator-budget-monopoly`: rolling-1h ratio of orchestrator-Claude-tokens to worker-Claude-tokens ≥ 9.0 when ≥1 worker is alive. Violation = role-pin is leaking.
      - `worker-local-utilization`: rolling-1h ratio of worker iterations on `local-qwen` provider ≥ 0.8. Violation = local stack is broken or auto-promote is over-firing.
      - `orchestrator-detached-worker-finish`: when the orchestrator's PID exits (clean or crash) with workers still alive, each worker MUST either (a) finish its claimed task and ship a PR within its existing 30-min iteration TTL OR (b) self-terminate cleanly via SIGTERM trap. Violation = a worker zombied past orchestrator death. Tested by `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` (new, paired with `chaos-budget-exhaust.mjs`'s pattern).
    - **Slice 4 — chaos test harness for the inverse** (0.5d): `scripts/chaos-worker-hang.mjs` — pauses one worker's `aider` child via `SIGSTOP` and asserts the watchdog (#spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring) detects the hang within 60s and the orchestrator reassigns the worker's `Touches:` glob to a fresh worker without touching the original PR. Paired with the existing `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` (P0).
    - **Slice 5 — operator UX + dashboard tile** (0.5d): the dashboard surfaces orchestrator vs worker token-spend split (composes with `dashboard-web-rich-runs-view`'s "Token budget" section) and a per-worker provider mix bar.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts` (slice 1 — extend input with `role`), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.test.ts` (slice 1 — 8 new cells), `novel/tick-loop/bin/orchestrate.mjs` (slice 2 — new entrypoint), `novel/tick-loop/src/orchestrator.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2 — pure decomposition + assignment dispatch), `novel/tick-loop/src/worker-assignment.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2 — `.minsky/workers/<id>.assignment.json` Strategy seam), `package.json` (slice 2 — `bin: { "minsky-orchestrate": "..." }`), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (slice 3 — three new invariants), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` (slice 3 — paired tests), `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 3), `scripts/chaos-worker-hang.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 4), `novel/dashboard-web/src/orchestrator-tile.ts` + tests (slice 5), `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md` (operator-facing — flow diagram + the role-separation rationale + the failure-mode inventory).
  - **Verification**: paired tests at every slice. Integration test (`test/orchestrator-fanout.integration.test.ts`): boot 2 workers + 1 orchestrator against a fixture TASKS.md with 4 non-overlapping tasks; assert orchestrator-token spend ≥ 90 % of cloud tokens, worker-token spend ≥ 80 % on local. Chaos: kill the orchestrator at iteration 2; assert workers finish their claim + ship PR + self-terminate within 30 min. Inverse chaos: SIGSTOP one worker's aider child; assert the watchdog reassigns within 60s.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/orchestrator-fanout-ratio.mjs --window=24h --json` returns `{"orchestrator_claude_tokens": Oc, "worker_claude_tokens": Wc, "worker_local_iterations": Wl, "worker_total_iterations": Wt, "merged_prs": M, "operator_interventions": I}`. Acceptance thresholds (rolling 24h, post-slice-3): `Oc / (Oc + Wc) ≥ 0.9`, `Wl / Wt ≥ 0.8`, `M ≥ 1.5 × serial_baseline`, `I = 0`. AND `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq -e '[.[] | select(.id | startswith("orchestrator-") or startswith("worker-"))] | length == 0'` exits 0 in the steady state. Cross-link with #task-aware-model-router slice 0's `iteration-routing-baseline.mjs` — same span attribute set, this script aggregates by role.
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis cells (a)–(d). Layered pivots: if role-pin leaks (a<70 %), retire the soft preference and switch to a hard env gate (`MINSKY_ROLE=worker` makes `decideProvider` *refuse* to route to Opus). If local-Qwen worker success drops (b<50 %), retire local for worker default and use Haiku-as-default-worker — keeps the orchestrator-Opus-monopoly while abandoning the "local-only-on-electricity" goal. **Don't retire role separation**; even if both pivots fire, the brain-vs-hands split is the load-bearing decision.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `decideProvider` accepts `role` and returns role-correct provider in all 8 cells with paired tests; (2) `pnpm minsky orchestrate --workers=N` ships and harvests PRs; (3) three new self-diagnose invariants ship with paired tests; (4) `scripts/chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` and `scripts/chaos-worker-hang.mjs` ship with paired tests; (5) integration test passes; (6) measurement script exits 0 in steady state; (7) `docs/orchestrator-fanout.md` documents the role-separation rationale + the 6 known cross-layer failure modes (orchestrator crash, worker crash, mlx-server crash, claude exhaustion mid-fanout, worktree corruption, mergiraf wrong-merge); (8) operator can launch the whole flow with one command from inside Claude Code.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #1 (don't reinvent — composes existing substrates rather than designing a novel orchestrator from scratch); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `worker-assignment.ts` is the seam between orchestrator and workers; fed by injected I/O); rule #6 (stay alive — orchestrator-detached-worker-finish invariant codifies it); rule #7 (graceful degrade — orchestrator pauses rather than degrading on Opus-unavailable); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis/Success/Pivot/Measurement above); rule #13 (security-privacy — local-routing on workers keeps more code on-device, reducing data-egress surface); Basiri et al. 2016, "Principles of Chaos Engineering", *IEEE Software* (steady-state hypothesis — the three new invariants); Hewitt 1973 (actor model — orchestrator and workers as actors with `.minsky/workers/<id>.assignment.json` as the message-passing seam); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 6 (silence-is-failure — `orchestrator-detached-worker-finish` invariant prevents zombie workers); the load-bearing post cited by #task-aware-model-router (97/88/61/29 bucket-quality numbers — workers' bucket distribution is dominated by single-file/multi-file slices, where local matches cloud).
  - **Risk**: medium-high. (a) **Role-pin race**: if the orchestrator's Claude session is itself spawned from inside Claude Code (the operator's session), the parent Claude session and the orchestrator child both contend for the same 5h cap. Mitigation: the orchestrator's `claude --print` invocations carry a distinct project key so token accounting splits cleanly; if the operator's parent session burns the cap, the orchestrator pauses (existing budget-guard); the workers continue on local. (b) **Worker context-window overflow**: aider+Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B has a smaller effective context than Opus; `daemon-aider-brief-shrinker` (P0, line 177) is a precondition. (c) **Orchestrator-as-single-point-of-failure**: if the orchestrator crashes, a fresh fanout can't be scheduled. Mitigation: slice 3's `orchestrator-detached-worker-finish` invariant ensures workers don't zombie; the operator restarts the orchestrator from inside Claude Code. (d) **Cross-layer telemetry drift**: orchestrator and worker spans must agree on the `role` attribute. Mitigation: spans emitted by a shared helper that reads `MINSKY_ROLE` once at boot; integration test asserts the attribute is non-empty on every span. (e) **Mergiraf wrong-merge across cross-worker overlaps**: if mergiraf auto-resolves a conflict incorrectly between two worker PRs, the merged main is wrong. Mitigation: orchestrator's review gate (it reads each worker PR before merging — that's the brain's job).
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) does the orchestrator run from the operator's Claude Code session (interactive) or from a separate `claude --print` session spawned by `pnpm minsky orchestrate`? Trade-off: interactive gives the operator visibility but ties the fanout's life to the operator's terminal; spawned gives daemon-like persistence but consumes a Claude session slot. (b) when both orchestrator and workers are alive, who edits TASKS.md? Proposal: only the orchestrator writes to TASKS.md; workers write to their assignment file and emit findings as PR-body Self-grade lessons that the orchestrator picks up post-merge. (c) `MINSKY_ROLE` semantics — does it default to `worker` (safer — never accidentally burns Opus) or to `orchestrator` (operator-friendly — `pnpm minsky` from inside Claude Code Just Works)? Proposal: default `orchestrator` when launched interactively (`isatty(stdout)`), default `worker` when launched as a `--worker-id` child.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"I start minsky from claude code … on the way where it's optimal minsky spawns more local agents that run on my local machine to work on parallel tasks of minsky in git worktrees. Main minsky worker (claude) handles those workers. Everything is extremely stable about this, with chaos engineering and other minsky principles. Essentially I want claude to be the brains of this (top layer) and everything below to be run by local models but with full list of features of claude."* The composition of #daemon-parallel-worktree-launch + #task-aware-model-router + #spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring captures the substrate; this block adds the role-pin, the operator entrypoint, and the cross-layer chaos invariants.

- [ ] `self-diagnose-on-start` — supervisor probes invariants at boot, escalates failures via TASKS.md
  - **ID**: self-diagnose-on-start
  - **Tags**: observability, supervisor, self-detection, rule-7, rule-9
  - **Estimate**: 3d
  - **Hypothesis**: every dogfood-surfaced bug to date has been "running state silently violates an invariant the operator-only-noticed-after-the-fact": (a) cache_read sum bug pegged every plan to 100 % used and only the operator noticed the homogeneous `budget-paused` log stream; (b) dashboard's 10 metric values stayed `(stub)` indefinitely because no probe asserted "after T minutes uptime, ≥1 metric should resolve to a real value". Encoding these invariants in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` and running them at supervisor start (and on a 5-min tick thereafter) means the next equivalent bug surfaces as a P0 TASKS.md entry within 5 min of regression — escalated automatically through the channel `/next-task` already drains. Pre-registered metric: time-from-regression-to-task-block-existing drops from "human notices, multiple hours" to "≤5 min" for the class of invariant-violation bugs. v0 ships with the seed invariant (`token-monitor-not-all-pegged`), the runner, the writer, and the supervisor wire-in. Subsequent invariants are appended in follow-up PRs (each one a 1-file change).
  - **Details**: (a) `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (already shipped in this PR) — pure invariant runner + seed invariant + TASKS.md writer + CLI. (b) `distribution/systemd/run-tick-loop.sh` runs `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --write-tasks-md --append-to TASKS.md` once at supervisor start; failures are written into the P0 section but the supervisor continues (advisory, not blocking — rule #7 graceful-degrade). (c) Add a 5-min `setInterval` probe in `tick-loop` to re-run invariants between iterations; on transition from `ok→violation` for any invariant, emit an OTEL span `tick-loop.self-diagnose.violation-detected` and a notifier push (the same surface budget-paused uses). (d) Each new invariant is a 1-export addition to `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + paired test; the runner accepts them automatically. (e) Document the invariant-authoring pattern in `docs/self-diagnose-authoring.md` — "what makes an invariant: must hold under every legal supervisor state; must fail loudly under at least one observed bug; must carry suggestedTaskTitle + suggestedFix that themselves comply with rule #9."
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (this PR), `scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` (this PR), `distribution/systemd/run-tick-loop.sh` (this PR — supervisor wire-in), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (follow-up — interval probe), `docs/self-diagnose-authoring.md` (follow-up).
  - **Verification**: (a) `pnpm vitest run scripts/self-diagnose.test.mjs` — 7 paired tests covering runner + seed invariant + writer (already passing). (b) Supervisor log on next start contains `self-diagnose:` line. (c) When the cache_read regression is re-introduced (revert PR #155 in a scratch branch), `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` exits 1 and surfaces the invariant.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq '. | length'` → integer count of violations; on a clean supervisor it is `0`. Regression test: `git stash; git revert <PR#155-merge-sha> --no-commit; node scripts/self-diagnose.mjs --json | jq -e '[.[] | select(.id == "token-monitor-not-all-pegged")] | length == 1'` exits 0 (the seed invariant catches the seeded bug). Tracking metric: time-to-task-block-existing for invariant-class regressions, measured manually at first (one data point per regression), promoted to OTEL span `self-diagnose.violation-detected.duration` once ≥3 invariants ship.
  - **Pivot**: if invariants false-positive ≥1 task per week (probe drift or transient supervisor states getting flagged), add a `consecutiveFailures: 2` retry gate before surfacing — the runner becomes "fail twice in a row, then escalate" rather than "fail once, escalate". Don't retire the architecture; tune the probe-stability axis. If even with retries the false-positive rate stays high (≥1/week sustained 4 weeks), pivot from "invariant set + boot probe" to "anomaly detection over OpenObserve metrics" — but that requires the span→metric pipeline to be wired (separate P0; out of scope here).
  - **Acceptance**: (1) seed invariant ships and catches the cache_read bug under revert; (2) supervisor logs show self-diagnose ran at boot; (3) writing findings to TASKS.md round-trips through `/next-task` (a self-detected task is pickable like any other); (4) ≥6 paired tests cover the runner + seed invariant + writer.
  - **Anchor**: Liskov 1987 (invariants as the substrate of correctness — invariant violation IS the bug); Brilliant, Knight, Leveson, "Analysis of Faults in an N-Version Software Experiment", *IEEE TSE* 1990 (one version probes the other); Hewitt 1973 (TASKS.md as actor message store — escalation channel reuse); rule #7 (graceful degrade — supervisor never blocks on self-diagnose); rule #9 (every violation carries hypothesis + measurement + pivot + anchor in its synthesised task block).
  - **Risk**: medium. The probe surface is the runtime state of every novel package; an invariant that's wrong is itself a bug source. Mitigation: each invariant ships with paired tests pinning its decision function, and the Pivot threshold (≥1 false-positive/week) is the explicit retire signal.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "i want minsky to be able to detect bugs in its own launched state. so maybe as soon as minsky starts, it also analyzes its own bugs and delegates fixing itself to the parent". Seed invariant (`token-monitor-not-all-pegged`) directly encodes the bug PR #155 fixed: had this invariant been live before that PR, the cache_read regression would have surfaced as a self-detected P0 the moment the supervisor restarted.

- [ ] `worker-model-per-machine-config` — local-LLM worker model is per-machine: env var → gitignored `.minsky/local-config.json` → repo default; pin this Mac to `mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit` (Opus-quality dense)
  - **ID**: worker-model-per-machine-config
  - **Tags**: p0, local-llm, per-machine, model-pin, recency-checked, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts`, `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (new), `.minsky/local-config.json` (per-machine, gitignored — example committed in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10, "I'm getting qwen3.6:27b. Update minsky's tasks so that this model will be used by default for local runs on THIS machine. Note that on other machine I might want a different model".
  - **Estimate**: 1d (Slice A: resolution chain + test; Slice B: bootstrap/invocation consolidation + recency anchor).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — the worker-role provider default reads the resolved model from this resolution chain rather than the hard-coded `DEFAULT_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL` constant. Composes with the existing `decideProvider`/`MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` env (#401 shipped).
  - **Hypothesis**: today the worker model is hard-coded twice — `DEFAULT_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL = "mlx-community/Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B-Instruct-4bit"` in `local-llm-bootstrap.ts:242` and `DEFAULT_AIDER_MODEL = "openai/mlx-community/Qwen2.5-Coder-32B-Instruct-4bit"` in `llm-invocation.ts:121`. The two strings already disagree (Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B vs Qwen2.5-Coder-32B), which is a divergence bug latent in main. A second, distinct symptom: per-machine hardware is heterogeneous (M1 Max 32GB unified ≠ M3 Max 64GB ≠ DGX Spark) and the right model differs by tier; pinning one constant in the repo forces the lowest common denominator. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** bootstrap (downloader, cache probe) and aider invocation read from the *same* resolved model id — divergence between the two strings is impossible by construction (one resolution function, two well-typed accessors); **(b)** on this M1 Max 32GB, `pnpm minsky` resolves to `mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit` (the per-machine pin); **(c)** on a hypothetical second machine without the per-machine file and without the env var, `pnpm minsky` resolves to the repo default unchanged from today (no behaviour regression for un-configured machines); **(d)** the worker bucket-1 (single-file slice) success rate on Qwen3.6-27B-Dense is within ±5 pp of the prior Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B baseline once #task-aware-model-router slice 0's measurement substrate lands — the recency-checked Terminal-Bench 59.3 (Opus-parity) and SWE-bench Verified 77.2 numbers should hold up. If (d) fails (>5 pp regression), pivot per-machine pin back to the MoE; the operator's "Opus-like" preference does not override observed merge rate.
  - **Details**:
    - **Slice A — resolution chain** (0.5d): new module `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` exporting `resolveLocalModel({ env, configFilePath, repoDefault }) → { localModel, aiderModel, source: "env" | "config-file" | "repo-default" }`. Pure function; reads `env.MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL` first, then attempts to parse the JSON at `configFilePath` (`.minsky/local-config.json`), then falls back to `repoDefault`. Both `localModel` (the bootstrap/HF id) and `aiderModel` (the aider-prefixed `openai/<id>`) come from the same source-of-truth — when only the bootstrap id is given, `aiderModel` is computed as `"openai/" + localModel`. Paired tests cover the 3-row precedence matrix × 2-row well-formed-vs-malformed JSON × 2-row presence-of-aiderModel-override.
    - **Slice B — bootstrap/invocation consolidation** (0.5d): replace the two diverged constants in `local-llm-bootstrap.ts` and `llm-invocation.ts` with calls to `resolveLocalModel(...)`. The repo-default constant remains exactly one place — `DEFAULT_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL` in `local-llm-bootstrap.ts` — and `llm-invocation.ts` derives its aider id from that. The existing `pivot-local-llm-model-id` rule-#9 record (cited in `local-llm-bootstrap.ts:233`) is updated with the consolidation note.
    - **Operator UX**: the example `.minsky/local-config.json` ships in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` with a comment explaining: this file is `.gitignore`d, never committed, lives only on the machine that authored it; absence is fine (repo default kicks in); presence overrides; env var beats both. Cross-machine sync stays out-of-scope (operator manages it via dotfile management or just doesn't sync — heterogeneous hardware is the point).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` + `.test.ts` (new, slice A), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts` (slice B — replace constant), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts` (slice B — derive aider id from resolved model), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.test.ts` (slice B — update tests for the new resolution flow), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` (operator-facing example + the `.gitignore` reminder + the "for THIS machine" pin), `validated-learnings.md` (one-line entry — recency-checked May 2026 pick is Qwen3.6-27B Dense for the 32GB-Apple-Silicon tier, citing the Opus-parity Terminal-Bench number).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `resolveLocalModel`. Integration test: with `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL=foo` set, the bootstrap probe reports `foo` as the missing model id; with the env var unset and a well-formed `.minsky/local-config.json` containing `{"localModel": "bar"}`, the probe reports `bar`; with both unset and absent, the probe reports `DEFAULT_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL`.
  - **Measurement**: `node -e "const {resolveLocalModel} = require('./novel/tick-loop/dist/local-config.js'); console.log(JSON.stringify(resolveLocalModel({env: process.env, configFilePath: '.minsky/local-config.json'})))"` returns `{"localModel": "mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit", "aiderModel": "openai/mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit", "source": "config-file"}` on the operator's M1 Max. AND `grep -c 'DEFAULT_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL\|DEFAULT_AIDER_MODEL' novel/tick-loop/src/{local-llm-bootstrap,llm-invocation}.ts` returns ≤ 1 (single source of truth — the constant exists only as the repo default in `local-llm-bootstrap.ts`; `llm-invocation.ts` no longer carries an independent constant). AND the rolling 7d worker bucket-1 success rate on this machine, post-#task-aware-model-router slice 0, is within ±5 pp of the prior Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B baseline (recorded as `iteration.routing.bucket=single-file` × `iteration.routing.provider=local-qwen` span attrs).
  - **Pivot**: if Qwen3.6-27B-Dense's per-token throughput on this M1 Max drops below 6 tok/s sustained (worker iterations exceeding the watchdog window), revert this machine's pin to the prior MoE (`mlx-community/Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B-Instruct-4bit`) by editing `.minsky/local-config.json` — no code change needed (that's the whole point of the resolution chain). If the resolution chain itself proves brittle (e.g., malformed JSON crashes the daemon at boot), pivot to a one-shot env-var-only mode and retire the JSON file half. **Don't retire per-machine config** — the heterogeneous-hardware argument holds even if Qwen3.6-27B turns out wrong; some machines have more RAM or different generations.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `resolveLocalModel` ships with paired tests covering the precedence matrix (env > config-file > repo-default) plus malformed-JSON graceful-degrade (rule #7 — falls through to repo-default with a one-line `[local-config] WARN` log, not a crash); (2) `local-llm-bootstrap.ts` and `llm-invocation.ts` both source their model id from `resolveLocalModel` — divergence between the two strings is impossible by construction; (3) the `pivot-local-llm-model-id` rule-#9 record is updated with the consolidation note; (4) `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` shows the example `.minsky/local-config.json` and the precedence rules; (5) on this M1 Max, the resolved model is `mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit` (operator pinned via `.minsky/local-config.json` 2026-05-10); (6) on a fresh clone of any branch with no per-machine file and no env var, the resolved model equals the prior committed default (no surprise migrations).
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `resolveLocalModel` is the seam between operator intent and runtime); rule #7 (graceful-degrade — malformed JSON falls through to repo-default); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(d) above); recency-checked May 2026 model picks (cited in `validated-learnings.md`): Qwen3.6-27B Dense matches Claude 4.5 Opus on Terminal-Bench 2.0 (59.3 vs 59.3 — [TokenMix](https://tokenmix.ai/blog/qwen-3-6-27b-review-dense-beats-moe-2026)); SWE-bench Verified 77.2 ([Buildfast](https://www.buildfastwithai.com/blogs/qwen3-6-27b-review-2026)); Q4_K_M ~25.57 tok/s on Apple-Silicon-Max class ([Simon Willison's measurement, cited in HN thread](https://news.ycombinator.com/item?id=47863217)); MLX repo `mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit` ([HF page](https://huggingface.co/mlx-community/Qwen3.6-27B-4bit)). Memory rule `feedback_verify_model_recency_at_filing_time` mandates recency-check at filing time — this slice's anchor IS that check.
  - **Risk**: low-medium. (a) **Resolution-chain bugs leak the worker default**: if `resolveLocalModel` mis-parses a malformed JSON and silently returns an undefined string, the bootstrap downloader fetches nothing and the daemon halts on first iteration. Mitigation: paired tests cover the malformed-JSON branch + the rule-#7 graceful-fallback; integration test asserts the daemon boots cleanly with a deliberately-broken `.minsky/local-config.json`. (b) **Per-machine drift across operator's machines**: if the operator runs Minsky on multiple Macs with different per-machine configs and forgets which is which, debugging "why does this machine ship slower PRs?" is harder. Mitigation: the resolved model is logged at boot (`[local-llm] resolved model = <id> (source = <env|config-file|repo-default>)`); the dashboard surfaces it as part of the supervisor health summary (composes with `dashboard-web-rich-runs-view`). (c) **Recency drift**: Qwen3.6-27B is the May 2026 pick; six months from now there may be a better dense model in the same RAM tier. Mitigation: the per-machine file is mutable — the operator updates one line; no code change. The repo default is reviewed quarterly per `validated-learnings.md`'s recency-anchor convention.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-A implementation iteration): (a) when both env var and config file specify a model, which wins? Proposal: env var wins (matches `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER` precedence shipped via #401; consistent with twelve-factor "config in env" baseline). (b) does the resolved model id propagate to the dashboard's supervisor-health summary, or stay daemon-internal? Proposal: surfaces — operator sanity-check that the right model is actually loaded. (c) does the ARCHITECTURE.md `.orchestrator/state/` convention extend to `.minsky/`? Today `.minsky/` is fully gitignored (`.gitignore:46`) so the per-machine config file slots in cleanly. Document the precedent in `ARCHITECTURE.md` as a one-line addition.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"I want opus-like approach for my models, so I'm ok with slower run but yet reasonable (as eg opus), which model should be for me then? … I'm getting qwen3.6:27b. Update minsky's tasks so that this model will be used by default for local runs on THIS machine. Note that on other machine I might want a different model."* The recency check that selected Qwen3.6-27B Dense — Terminal-Bench 2.0 Opus-parity, SWE-bench Verified 77.2, fits 32GB at Q4 — is documented in this PR's body and in `validated-learnings.md`.

- [ ] `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` — first-class second local stack (opencode → LM Studio → MLX → Qwen3-14B) parallel to aider+mlx_lm.server+Qwen3.6-27B; operator picks per machine via env / config-file
  - **ID**: support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack

  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts` (new `buildOpencodeInvocation`), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts` (extend planner), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-probes.ts` (LM Studio probe variant), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (env var wire-in), `.minsky/local-config.json` schema (extend), `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (new), `scripts/check-mlx-server.mjs` (extend probe shape).

  - **Estimate**: 5d (substrate slice in 1d; the rest ratchets per slice).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — workers in worktrees can route to either local stack per-machine. Composes with `worker-model-per-machine-config` (P0, line 478 — extend the resolved type to carry `agent` + `probeUrl` alongside `localModel`), `daemon-local-model-self-tune` (P1, this PR — extend recommender to consider `(agent, model)` pairs), `task-aware-model-router` (P1 — bucket router routes among `claude-opus | claude-sonnet | claude-haiku | local-aider | local-opencode`).
  - **Hypothesis**: today Minsky's local path is hard-tied to one stack — `aider --message <brief>` against `mlx_lm.server` on port 8080. The hard-coding spans 6 places: `DEFAULT_AIDER_MODEL` constant (`llm-invocation.ts:121`), `buildAiderInvocation` argv shape (aider-specific `--openai-api-base` / `--openai-api-key` / `--no-auto-commits` / `--message`), `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_PROBE_URL` default (`http://127.0.0.1:8080/v1/models`), `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_AIDER_BIN` env (aider-bin only, no opencode-bin parallel), `local-llm-bootstrap.ts` planner (probes for `pipx`+`mlx_lm`+`aider` only), `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL_ID` env (writes aider's `openai/<id>` form only). A second stack — `opencode run "<brief>"` against LM Studio's OpenAI-compatible server on port 1234, MLX backend, Qwen3-14B (~7.5 GB Q4 — fits 16 GB Macs and leaves more headroom on 32 GB for concurrent workers) — is provider-equivalent (LM Studio's `/v1/chat/completions` matches mlx_lm.server's) but unreachable today without forking 6 files. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode pnpm minsky` boots cleanly against a running LM Studio server with Qwen3-14B loaded, dispatches a worker iteration via `opencode run`, and the iteration's `tick-loop.iteration` span carries `iteration.routing.{agent: "opencode", backend: "lm-studio", model: "qwen3-14b"}`; **(b)** the existing aider+mlx_lm.server path is unchanged when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT` is unset (back-compat); **(c)** on a fresh machine where neither stack is installed, `pnpm minsky` (no args) detects which stack the operator has and selects accordingly — if both are present, `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT` env wins, else `.minsky/local-config.json`'s `agent` field wins, else falls back to aider for back-compat; **(d)** the 5-row chaos table for the new path covers `lm-studio-not-running` (port 1234 unreachable), `opencode-bin-missing` (loud-crash per spawn-strategy), `qwen3-14b-context-overflow` (smaller window than Qwen3.6-27B's 256K — needs a brief-shrink test), `lm-studio-model-mid-iteration-swap` (operator changes model in the GUI; iteration's spans must reflect the actual model the LLM saw), `opencode-config-malformed` (graceful-degrade per rule #7, falls through to claude). If any of (a)–(d) fails, the slice is incomplete; pivot to "aider-only with documented opencode integration deferred". **Don't pivot the goal** — opencode being mainstream-supported on Apple Silicon (May 2026 — multiple operator-shared blogs) makes it a load-bearing alternative path; the question is implementation order, not whether to support it.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet; each slice is one PR with paired tests + rule-#9 self-grade):
    - **Slice 1 — agent abstraction + buildOpencodeInvocation** (1d): new `buildOpencodeInvocation({ brief, command?, model?, configPath?, cwd? }) → LlmInvocation` in `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts`, structurally parallel to `buildAiderInvocation`.
