Argv shape: `opencode run "<brief>" --model <id>` when `model` is set; brief delivered via single argv (opencode's documented non-interactive form). The provider config (LM Studio baseURL + model) lives in opencode's own `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json` (per opencode's docs); Minsky's `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT_CONFIG_PATH` env (new) overrides for tests/per-machine setups. Paired tests cover argv shape × brief escaping × cwd handling × model-override branch.
    - **Slice 2 — env-var-driven dispatcher + spawn-strategy wiring** (1d): new `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=aider|opencode` env var (default `aider` for back-compat). `bin/tick-loop.mjs` reads it once at boot and selects between `buildAiderInvocation` and `buildOpencodeInvocation` when constructing the local `ProcessSpawnStrategy`. The `LlmProviderSpawnStrategy` wrapper is unchanged — agent is per-process, not per-iteration (a per-iteration agent switch is overkill at this stage; revisit if `task-aware-model-router` ever wants it). Boot log line gains `agent=<aider|opencode>` to surface the choice. Paired tests + integration test (`MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode MINSKY_TICK_DRY_RUN=1 pnpm minsky --max-iterations=1` boots and dispatches via the opencode shape).
    - **Slice 3 — probe-URL default per agent + LM Studio detection** (1d): `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_PROBE_URL` already exists (#358 substrate); slice 3 makes the *default* per-agent — when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode`, default to `http://127.0.0.1:1234/v1/models` (LM Studio's documented default port); when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=aider`, keep `http://127.0.0.1:8080/v1/models`. The probe payload shape is identical (both expose OpenAI-compatible `/v1/models`), so no probe-code change. Auto-bootstrap planner (`local-llm-bootstrap.ts`) adds an LM Studio detection step: shell out to `which lms` (LM Studio's bundled CLI) AND test for `~/Applications/LM Studio.app` (Mac install path); if present + opencode is selected, the planner is "graceful-degrade — operator must start LM Studio's server via the GUI or `lms server start`" rather than auto-spawning (LM Studio is a GUI app; we don't have the install primitives to start it from CLI in all cases).
    - **Slice 4 — per-machine config extension + resolveLocalAgentConfig** (1d): extend `resolveLocalModel` (filed in #worker-model-per-machine-config slice A) → `resolveLocalAgentConfig` returning `{ agent: "aider"|"opencode", model: "...", probeUrl: "...", source: "env"|"config-file"|"repo-default" }`. `.minsky/local-config.json` schema extended with optional `agent` + `probeUrl` fields; defaults preserve back-compat. Paired tests cover the 3-way precedence × 2 agents × malformed-JSON graceful-fallback.
    - **Slice 5 — chaos table + invariants + docs** (1d): chaos table for the opencode path (5 rows above); 3 new self-diagnose invariants (`opencode-config-readable` — opencode.json parses; `lm-studio-server-reachable` — port 1234 returns 200 when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode`; `qwen3-14b-context-pressure` — slim brief is ≤2 KB, same as `daemon-aider-brief-shrinker` invariant but for the smaller-context model); new `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (operator-facing, mirrors `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`); extend `minsky doctor` to list both stacks and show which is configured.
  - **Files** (per slice): `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-invocation.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 1 — `buildOpencodeInvocation` + 15+ paired tests), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slices 2 + 3 — env-var wire-in + per-agent probe URL default), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-llm-bootstrap.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 3 — LM Studio detection step), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (slice 4 — extend resolution chain; this file is created by `worker-model-per-machine-config` slice A), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 5 — three new invariants), `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (slice 5 — new operator-facing guide), `novel/tick-loop/src/doctor-substrate-rows.ts` (slice 5 — extend `minsky doctor` rows).
  - **Verification**: paired tests at every slice. Integration tests: (a) `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode MINSKY_TICK_DRY_RUN=1 pnpm minsky --max-iterations=1` boots cleanly and the iteration span carries `iteration.routing.agent=opencode`; (b) `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=aider` (or unset) preserves the existing aider+mlx_lm.server flow byte-for-byte (back-compat snapshot); (c) chaos test `chaos-lm-studio-not-running.mjs` — operator stops LM Studio mid-iteration, daemon detects and falls back to claude on next iteration; (d) chaos test `chaos-opencode-config-malformed.mjs` — opencode.json is corrupted, daemon graceful-degrades per rule #7 and the iteration's reason carries `local-config-malformed: <detail>`.
  - **Measurement**: post-slice-2: `node -e 'process.env.MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT="opencode"; require("./novel/tick-loop/dist/index.js").bootSummary()'` returns `{agent: "opencode", probeUrl: "http://127.0.0.1:1234/v1/models", model: "<resolved>"}`. Post-slice-5: rolling 7d `iteration.routing.agent=opencode` span count is non-zero on machines where the operator has set the env (live-fire validation of the new path); `iteration.routing.agent=aider` count is unchanged on machines that haven't set the env (back-compat). Acceptance threshold: ≥50 successful opencode-routed iterations on a single operator machine across the 7d window before declaring slice 5 shipped (without the live-fire signal, the integration could silently fail and we'd never know).
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis cells (a)–(d). If opencode's headless `run` mode proves unstable (e.g., hangs without timeout, doesn't exit cleanly on completion — see opencode issue #13851 cited in 2026-05 reports), pivot slice 1 to use `opencode serve` + `opencode run --attach <url>` (the long-lived server pattern) instead of one-shot `opencode run`. If LM Studio's `lms server start` CLI proves not-bundled with the GUI (some installs lack it), pivot slice 3 to "operator must manually start the server in the GUI; daemon detects the running server via the probe; refuses to dispatch when unreachable". If the slim brief proves too small for opencode's tool-use loop (more turns required than aider's diff-fenced single-shot), pivot to a slightly larger opencode-specific brief variant (`buildOpencodeBrief` parallel to `buildLocalBrief` from #406). Hard pivot floor: even if all of slice 5's chaos invariants prove flaky, slices 1–4 alone make the new stack reachable for operators willing to babysit; that's strictly better than today's "fork the repo to use opencode".
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `buildOpencodeInvocation` ships with 15+ paired tests; (2) `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` selects opencode at boot; (3) per-agent probe URL defaults work; (4) `resolveLocalAgentConfig` extends the resolution chain with `agent` + `probeUrl`; (5) three new self-diagnose invariants ship with paired tests; (6) `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` documents the operator path; (7) `minsky doctor` lists both stacks; (8) live-fire validation: ≥50 successful opencode iterations on the operator's M1 Max within 7d of slice 5 merge.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #1 (don't reinvent — opencode is a mainstream OSS coding agent in 2026, mature enough that adopting it as a second stack is cheaper than designing a novel one); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT` env is the seam; `buildOpencodeInvocation` is the new Strategy implementation parallel to `buildAiderInvocation`); rule #6 (stay alive — back-compat preserved on machines that haven't opted in); rule #7 (graceful-degrade — malformed config, unreachable server, missing binary all fall through to claude); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(d) above); rule #13 (security-privacy — LM Studio runs locally, no data egress; opencode's MCP integration surface needs review before any cloud-enabled tools are wired); recency-checked May 2026 sources: [opencode docs — providers](https://opencode.ai/docs/providers/) (LM Studio config example with `@ai-sdk/openai-compatible` package); [opencode CLI docs](https://opencode.ai/docs/cli/) (`opencode run "<prompt>"` non-interactive mode + `opencode serve` headless server); [LM Studio OpenAI-compat docs](https://lmstudio.ai/docs/developer/openai-compat) (port 1234, `/v1/chat/completions` shape); [LM Studio v0.4.1 Anthropic-compat](https://lmstudio.ai/blog/claudecode) (Jan 2026 — `/v1/messages` endpoint enables Claude Code routing too, future-proofs the seam); [Falkingham 2026-05-08](https://peterfalkingham.com/2026/05/08/getting-local-ai-working-for-me-lm-studio-opencode-and-hermes/) (operator-shared write-up of the working flow); the [groxaxo/opencode-local-setup repo](https://github.com/groxaxo/opencode-local-setup) (reference implementation of opencode + LM Studio + Ollama + vLLM auto-sync). Memory rule `feedback_verify_model_recency_at_filing_time` mandates recency-check at filing time — this slice's anchor IS that check.
  - **Risk**: medium. (a) **Opencode headless mode immaturity** — issue #13851 (2026) reports non-interactive mode hangs in some pipelines. Mitigation: slice 1's pivot to `opencode serve` + `--attach`; chaos test `chaos-opencode-hang.mjs` catches the regression. (b) **LM Studio GUI dependency** — LM Studio is a GUI app; on headless servers (Linux supervisors, future cloud tier) it's not a fit; aider+mlx_lm.server stays the default for those. Mitigation: `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=aider` is the default; opencode is opt-in. (c) **Qwen3-14B context window** — 14B has a smaller effective context than 27B; multi-file refactor briefs may not fit. Mitigation: slice 5's `qwen3-14b-context-pressure` invariant; brief-shrinker (#406, shipped) already targets ≤2 KB which fits any model's window. (d) **Fragmenting the "local" identity** — operators who switch between aider and opencode mid-week may see throughput dispersion. Mitigation: per-machine pin via `.minsky/local-config.json` (slice 4); auto-tuner (#410) treats `(agent, model)` as the unit of recommendation, not just `model`. (e) **opencode auto-commit semantics** — unlike aider's `--no-auto-commits`, opencode's git behaviour isn't fully documented. Slice 1 verifies via integration test that opencode does NOT commit silently, OR adds an opencode-equivalent flag if it does.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) does `opencode run "<brief>"` exit cleanly after the brief completes, or does it stay open expecting more input? If the latter, brief delivery moves to `opencode serve` + `run --attach`. (b) does opencode auto-commit to git? If yes, the daemon's brief instructs it explicitly (parallel to aider's `--no-auto-commits` discipline); if no, the daemon's commit step has to either invoke `git commit` itself or rely on opencode's tool-use to do it. (c) does opencode read a per-iteration `--model <id>` flag, or only read from `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json`? If only the config file, slice 1 writes the config file at iteration time (Strategy seam — `writeOpencodeConfig` parallel to the brief-builder). (d) what's the default model name LM Studio exposes for Qwen3-14B — bare `qwen3-14b` or full HF path? Verify against a live LM Studio install before pinning the slice-3 default. (e) does `lms server start` exist on every LM Studio install, or only when the operator opts in via the GUI's "Bundled CLI" checkbox? Slice 3's "graceful-degrade — operator must start manually" path is the rule-#7 fallback when `lms` isn't on PATH.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"I need full support of opencode → LM Studio → MLX runtime → Qwen3-14B in minsky in every single action. Define gaps, list of tasks."* Composes with the existing aider+mlx_lm.server path; doesn't replace it. The 6-place hard-coding inventory above (DEFAULT_AIDER_MODEL, buildAiderInvocation, MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_PROBE_URL default, MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_AIDER_BIN, local-llm-bootstrap.ts planner, MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM_MODEL_ID write-shape) IS the gap analysis the operator asked for; each slice closes one or more of those places. Live-fire 2026-05-10 (this PR's verification): the operator's M1 Max with Qwen3.6-27B-4bit on mlx_lm.server proved the aider+mlx_lm path works end-to-end (PR #406 + #411 chain shipped); this task is the parallel-stack layer that lets the operator A/B against opencode+LM Studio+Qwen3-14B without forking the repo.

- [ ] `claude-usage-aware-strategic-model-router` — daemon reads live Claude usage (5h window + weekly + monthly), persists it, and picks the highest-quality model that fits the remaining budget; "best model by default, downgrade only when forced"
  - **ID**: claude-usage-aware-strategic-model-router
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, daemon, budget-aware, model-router, performance-by-default, follow-up-of-task-aware-model-router
  - **Touches**: `novel/adapters/token-monitor/src/{maciek,index}.ts` (extend snapshot with monthly window + remaining-fractions), `novel/budget-guard/src/index.ts` (continuous remaining-% surface alongside the existing 4-state action), `novel/tick-loop/src/strategic-model-router.ts` (new — pure picker), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts` (input shape extends to carry strategic pick), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (wire-in), `.minsky/state.json` schema (extend — `claudeUsageHistory` ring buffer for trajectory tracking + exhaustion-time prediction), `scripts/check-mlx-server.mjs` (no change — orthogonal), `docs/strategic-model-router.md` (new — operator-facing).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10, *"I want minsky to be able to strategically be able to switch to the best model available based on claude's remaining usage for this week/5 hours/month. So I want it to smartly be able to pick the right model (with best performance by default) based on remaining usage. I need it to read actual remaining usage left and keep it updated."*
  - **Estimate**: 6d (substrate slice in 1d; the rest ratchets per slice).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — orchestrator role gets the strategic best-fit pick per iteration. Composes with `task-aware-model-router` (P1, line 614 — this task's bucket-classification feeds the strategic picker as one input among several), `daemon-local-model-self-tune` (P1 — same recommender substrate, now agent + model + strategic-budget all together), `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` (P0 — workers' agent choice composes with the strategic picker's model choice), `worker-model-per-machine-config` (P0 — per-machine overrides still win when set).
  - **Hypothesis**: today the daemon's model decision is binary (claude-vs-local) gated by 4 budget states (`normal | graceful-degrade | weekly-cap-warn | circuit-break-and-notify`). This is too coarse for the operator's actual policy: *"best model by default, downgrade only when forced"*. The operator wants Opus 4.7 1M when the 5h window has >50% remaining, Sonnet 4.6 when 30–50%, Haiku 4.5 when 10–30%, local when <10% OR weekly headroom <20% OR monthly cap exhausted. The substrate already exposes `tokensRemainingInWindow / windowSizeTokens / weeklyHeadroomFraction / observedAt` (`novel/adapters/token-monitor/src/index.ts:30-41`); what's missing is **(a)** monthly tracking (no `monthlyHeadroomFraction` field today), **(b)** a continuous remaining-% surface (BudgetGuard's `BudgetAction` enum collapses fine-grained data into 4 buckets — see `novel/budget-guard/src/index.ts:28-32`), **(c)** a per-model cost map (Opus 4.7 ≈ 15 USD / 75 USD per Mtok; Sonnet 4.6 ≈ 3 USD / 15 USD; Haiku 4.5 ≈ 1 USD / 5 USD; local ≈ electricity), **(d)** a pure picker `pickStrategicModel({ snapshot, taskBucket, modelCatalog }) → { model, reason }` that walks the catalog from highest-quality to lowest and returns the first model whose cost fits the rolling-iteration spend rate × seconds-until-window-reset, **(e)** a refresh cadence (the daemon's existing every-5-min tick is too coarse; the strategic picker needs sub-30s freshness when the operator is mid-session), **(f)** a usage-trajectory ring-buffer in `.minsky/state.json` so the picker can predict exhaustion time (linear regression over last N tick-deltas) and de-rate the pick when the trajectory predicts crossing a threshold within the iteration's expected wall-time. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(α)** on a fresh 5h window with operator at 0% consumed, the picker returns `{ model: "claude-opus-4-7", reason: "5h-remaining=99%, weekly-remaining=82%, monthly-remaining=88%, all above quality-tier-1 thresholds" }`; **(β)** at 60% consumed within the 5h window the picker returns `{ model: "claude-sonnet-4-6", reason: "5h-remaining=40%, between sonnet-floor=30% and opus-floor=50%" }`; **(γ)** at 92% consumed AND/OR weekly-headroom 15% the picker returns `{ model: "local-<resolved-via-#worker-model-per-machine-config>", reason: "5h-remaining=8%, below haiku-floor=10% — drop to local" }`; **(δ)** the snapshot is refreshed every ≤30s when the daemon is iterating AND every ≤300s when idle (auto-tuned by the iteration cadence — same TTL pattern as the local-LLM probe cache shipped via #358). If any of (α)–(δ) fails, the slice is incomplete; pivot to ratchet thresholds rather than retiring the architecture (the architecture is what the operator asked for; the threshold values are tuneable). Specific pivot triggers: if the picker thrashes (changes model >3× per 5h window on stable workload), tighten the hysteresis band to ±5pp; if iteration outcomes degrade (>10pp drop in merge-rate when sonnet routes a bucket the catalog said it could handle), bump the per-bucket quality floor.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet; each slice is one PR with paired tests + rule-#9 self-grade):
    - **Slice 1 — extend TokenSnapshot with monthly + remaining-fractions** (1d): add `tokensRemainingInWeek`, `weekSizeTokens`, `tokensRemainingInMonth`, `monthSizeTokens`, `monthlyHeadroomFraction`, `secondsUntilWeekReset`, `secondsUntilMonthReset` to `TokenSnapshot`. Update `MaciekTokenMonitor` to compute these from the same JSONL log it already parses (week boundary = `Date#getDay() === 1` Monday 00:00 UTC; month boundary = `Date#getDate() === 1` 00:00 UTC; running cumulative sum since last boundary). Update `StubTokenMonitor` to default monthly fields. 20+ paired tests. **Back-compat**: existing fields preserved unchanged; old callers that read only the 5h fields still work.
    - **Slice 2 — continuous remaining-% surface in BudgetGuard** (0.5d): new `BudgetGuard.snapshotRemainingPercents() → { fivehour: number, weekly: number, monthly: number, observedAt: string }` returning the raw fractions (0..1) without collapsing to the 4-state `BudgetAction`. Composes with the existing `decide(...)` (which keeps its 4-state output for back-compat with `circuit-break-and-notify` paused-sentinel handling). Paired tests covering boundary values (0, 0.5, 0.99, 1.0).
    - **Slice 3 — model catalog data file** (0.5d): new `novel/tick-loop/src/model-catalog.ts` exporting `MODEL_CATALOG: ModelCatalogEntry[]` with rows for each Anthropic + local model: `{ id, agent, qualityTier: 1|2|3|4, costPer1MtokInput: number|null /* null=local */, costPer1MtokOutput: number|null, fivehourFloor: number, weeklyFloor: number, monthlyFloor: number }`. Recency-checked May 2026: Opus 4.7 1M (tier 1, 15/75 per Mtok, fivehour-floor 0.5); Sonnet 4.6 (tier 2, 3/15, floor 0.3); Haiku 4.5 (tier 3, 1/5, floor 0.1); local-aider+Qwen3.6-27B-4bit (tier 4, 0/0, floor 0). Pure data; no logic; 5+ tests asserting the catalog is sorted by qualityTier ascending and floors are monotone descending.
    - **Slice 4 — pure pickStrategicModel** (1d): `novel/tick-loop/src/strategic-model-router.ts` exports `pickStrategicModel({ remaining, taskBucket, catalog, hysteresis }) → { model: string, agent: "claude" | "local", reason: string, source: "strategic-router" | "fallback" | "operator-pin" }`. Algorithm: walk catalog ascending by qualityTier (highest quality first); for each, check whether `remaining.fivehour >= entry.fivehourFloor` AND `remaining.weekly >= entry.weeklyFloor` AND `remaining.monthly >= entry.monthlyFloor`; return the first that passes. If nothing passes, return the lowest-tier (local). Hysteresis: when the previous pick was `X` and the current pick would be `Y` (different from X), require the remaining-% to be ≥5pp below the floor that gates Y vs X — otherwise stick with X. Prevents thrash when remaining hovers near a threshold. 30+ paired tests covering: each tier × each window × hysteresis-stable × hysteresis-cross.
    - **Slice 5 — wire pickStrategicModel into decideProvider input + spawn-strategy** (1d): extend `DecideProviderInput` with optional `strategicPick: { model, agent }` field. When set AND `agent === "claude"`, the dispatch passes `--model <id>` to claude (Anthropic CLI accepts model override per-invocation). When `agent === "local"`, dispatches the local strategy. The existing `forceClaude` / `preferLocal` / `localRatio` knobs still win as hard overrides. `bin/tick-loop.mjs` reads `MODEL_CATALOG` + the BudgetGuard's continuous `snapshotRemainingPercents()` + the iteration's task-bucket (from #task-aware-model-router slice 1 once shipped; for now, default `multi-file`), invokes `pickStrategicModel(...)`, and threads the result into `LlmProviderSpawnStrategy`. Boot log gains `strategic-pick=<model>` line.
    - **Slice 6 — refresh cadence + persistence + trajectory** (1d): the daemon refreshes `TokenSnapshot` every ≤30s when iterating (currently ad-hoc — the budget-guard caches but doesn't proactively re-fetch). Add `MINSKY_USAGE_REFRESH_INTERVAL_MS=30000` env (default 30s active, 300s idle). Persist a ring buffer of `(observedAt, fivehourRemaining, weeklyRemaining, monthlyRemaining)` tuples in `.minsky/state.json` (cap 100 entries). Add `predictExhaustionMs({ history }) → { fivehourMs?: number, weeklyMs?: number, monthlyMs?: number }` pure function — linear regression over the ring buffer, returns ms-until-zero per window. Picker consumes the prediction: when `predicted-exhaustion-ms < expectedIterationWallMs × 1.5` for a tier's gating window, de-rate to next tier. Composes with #self-diagnose-on-start as a new invariant `usage-prediction-converges` (predicted exhaustion time should not flap >2× across consecutive ticks under stable workload).
    - **Slice 7 — chaos table + self-diagnose invariants + dashboard tile** (0.5d): chaos table for the strategic-router path (5 rows: stale snapshot, monthly-window-clock-drift, picker-thrash-during-hysteresis-bug, claude-CLI-rejects-our-model-override, predicted-exhaustion-NaN-on-empty-history). 3 new self-diagnose invariants (`usage-snapshot-fresh` — observedAt is within 5×refreshInterval; `picker-output-in-catalog` — every emitted pick maps to a `MODEL_CATALOG` entry; `usage-prediction-converges` from slice 6). Dashboard tile showing remaining-%× per window + current strategic pick + predicted exhaustion time per window.
    - **Slice 8 — operator override surface + docs** (0.5d): `MINSKY_STRATEGIC_PIN_MODEL=<id>` env locks the picker to one model regardless of remaining-% (operator escape hatch — the strategic picker is advisory; operator's literal pin always wins, mirrors `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=claude-only` precedent). `docs/strategic-model-router.md` ships the operator-facing routing matrix + example trajectories + the `MODEL_CATALOG`'s recency-check anchor process.
  - **Files** (per slice): `novel/adapters/token-monitor/src/{index,maciek}.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 1), `novel/budget-guard/src/index.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2), `novel/tick-loop/src/model-catalog.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 3), `novel/tick-loop/src/strategic-model-router.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 4), `novel/tick-loop/src/llm-provider-selector.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 5), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slices 5-6), `novel/tick-loop/src/usage-history-state.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 6 — ring buffer + linear-regression predictor), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` + `state.json` writer (slice 6), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 7), `novel/dashboard-web/src/strategic-router-tile.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 7), `docs/strategic-model-router.md` (slice 8).
  - **Verification**: paired tests at every slice. Integration test: replay 100 fixture snapshots into the picker, assert the pick crosses tier boundaries at the documented thresholds. Live-fire (manual): on this M1 Max, run the daemon for 24h with `MINSKY_USAGE_REFRESH_INTERVAL_MS=30000` and observe `tick-loop.strategic-pick` spans rotate through opus → sonnet → haiku → local as the 5h window saturates. Chaos: `chaos-stale-usage-snapshot.mjs` (force `observedAt` 10 min in the past; assert picker de-rates by one tier — stale data is not trustworthy).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/strategic-pick-trajectory.mjs --window=24h --json` returns `{"picks": [{"observedAt", "model", "remaining"}, ...], "tier_minutes": {opus_minutes, sonnet_minutes, haiku_minutes, local_minutes}, "thrash_count": N}`. Acceptance thresholds (rolling 24h post-slice-7): **(a)** `tier_minutes.opus_minutes / total_minutes ≥ 0.5` on a typical Max20 day (proves "best model by default" — operator gets Opus most of the time); **(b)** `thrash_count ≤ 3` (proves hysteresis works); **(c)** the 100-iteration historical replay test (slice 4) shows ≥95% agreement with operator-labelled expected picks; **(d)** `iteration.routing.strategic_pick` span attribute emitted on every iteration (rule #4 visible-not-silent — operator can grep the dispatch decisions). Concrete log probe: `grep -c '"strategic_pick"' .minsky/workers/*.log` over 24h is ≥ iteration count (every iteration carries the pick).
  - **Pivot**: see Hypothesis cells (α)–(δ). Tier-floor pivots: if `opus_minutes` falls below 30% on Max20 (operator is paying for the tier but rarely getting Opus), the floors are too conservative — relax `opus.fivehourFloor` from 0.5 to 0.3. If `thrash_count` exceeds 10/day, hysteresis is too narrow — widen from ±5pp to ±10pp. If predicted-exhaustion proves unreliable (linear regression assumes stationary spend rate; spiky workload breaks it), pivot slice 6 to median-of-last-N-tick-deltas instead of regression. **Don't retire** the multi-window architecture — even if monthly tracking proves noisy (Anthropic's monthly cap reset is operator-account-specific, not calendar-aligned), the 5h + weekly subset is still strictly better than today's 4-state surface.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `TokenSnapshot` extended with monthly + remaining-fractions (slice 1, 20+ tests). (2) `BudgetGuard.snapshotRemainingPercents()` returns continuous %s (slice 2, 10+ tests). (3) `MODEL_CATALOG` data file with 4+ entries, recency-anchored (slice 3, 5+ tests). (4) `pickStrategicModel` pure function (slice 4, 30+ tests). (5) `decideProvider` accepts `strategicPick` input + `bin/tick-loop.mjs` wires through (slice 5, paired tests). (6) Refresh cadence + ring-buffer history + exhaustion predictor (slice 6, paired tests + integration). (7) 3 new self-diagnose invariants + dashboard tile (slice 7). (8) `MINSKY_STRATEGIC_PIN_MODEL` operator escape hatch + `docs/strategic-model-router.md` (slice 8). (9) Live-fire 24h sustained: `tier_minutes.opus_minutes / total_minutes ≥ 0.5`, `thrash_count ≤ 3`.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #1 (don't reinvent — the substrate `TokenSnapshot` + `MaciekTokenMonitor` + `BudgetGuard` already exist; this task extends rather than replaces); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `pickStrategicModel` is the seam between budget signal + task bucket + model catalog and runtime dispatch); rule #6 (stay alive — never crash on stale/missing snapshot; degrade to local rather than halting); rule #7 (graceful degrade — chaos rows codify the failure modes); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (α)–(δ) above plus tier-minute and thrash-count measurement); rule #13 (security-privacy — the snapshot reads `~/.claude/projects/<cwd>/<session>.jsonl` which is already inside Minsky's threat model from the existing MaciekTokenMonitor); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 3 (error-budget framing — tokens as the budget you spend, the strategic picker as the spend-rate-aware controller); Card & Mackinlay 1999 (glanceable display — the dashboard tile surfaces remaining-% per window so the operator can sanity-check the picker's input); Doerr 2018 (OKRs — "best model by default" is the OKR the picker optimizes; tier-minutes is the KR); the existing `task-aware-model-router` (P1, line 614) — that task's bucket-classification feeds this picker; this task is the budget-aware lateral that completes the picture.
  - **Risk**: medium-high. (a) **MaciekTokenMonitor parser drift** — Anthropic changes the JSONL schema (already happened once: `cache_read` field added 2026-04, broke parser per PR #155). Mitigation: paired tests against committed fixtures; snapshot-shape regression guard. (b) **Monthly window definition drift** — Anthropic's monthly cap may reset on the operator's billing date, not calendar month. Mitigation: slice 1's `secondsUntilMonthReset` is computed from a documented anchor (`MINSKY_BILLING_CYCLE_DAY` env; default 1st-of-month UTC); operator can pin to their actual billing day. (c) **Model-pricing drift** — Anthropic adjusts published prices. Mitigation: `MODEL_CATALOG` has `recordedAt` field; recency-check process documented; quarterly refresh. (d) **Picker oscillation under spiky workload** — large iteration mid-window jumps remaining-% by 10pp+ in one tick, picker thrashes. Mitigation: hysteresis band (slice 4); minimum settle-window (10 iterations between picks). (e) **Catalog-floor mis-calibration** — operator has a different opinion of "Opus is worth it down to 50%". Mitigation: every floor is operator-overridable via env (`MINSKY_STRATEGIC_FLOOR_OPUS_FIVEHOUR=0.3`). (f) **Strategic pick conflicts with `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`** — operator has explicitly opted into local; strategic picker would route to claude. Mitigation: `forceClaude` / `preferLocal` / `localRatio` ALWAYS win over the strategic pick (it's advisory; operator's literal pin is hard).
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) does Anthropic's session JSONL include enough data to compute monthly cumulative spend, or do we need a separate persistent counter? Proposal: try parsing first; if data is too sparse, fall back to a `~/.claude/.minsky/monthly-spend.json` operator-managed file plus an opt-in OTel pipeline. (b) what's the precise gating policy when `secondsUntilWindowReset < expectedIterationWallMs`? Proposal: de-rate to next tier so we don't start an iteration that will be killed mid-flight by the window roll-over. (c) does the picker run per-iteration or per-tick? Proposal: per-iteration (the dispatch decision is per-iteration; running the picker every tick wastes work when the daemon is idle). (d) is `claude --model <id>` actually supported by the CLI we spawn (`claude --print` with model override), or do we need to set `ANTHROPIC_MODEL` env per-spawn? Proposal: verify in slice 5; the CLI documentation suggests both work but the env-var path is more portable. (e) how does the strategic picker compose with `task-aware-model-router`'s bucket classifier? Proposal: bucket-aware picker — the catalog's per-tier floors are PER-bucket (architecture tier requires lower floors than docs tier; cheapness threshold scales with iteration importance).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"I want minsky to be able to strategically be able to switch to the best model available based on claude's remaining usage for this week/5 hours/month. So I want it to smartly be able to pick the right model (with best performance by default) based on remaining usage. I need it to read actual remaining usage left and keep it updated."* Three load-bearing pieces in that directive: **(i)** "based on claude's remaining usage for this week/5 hours/month" — three windows, not one (today only 5h is granular; weekly is binary; monthly is absent); **(ii)** "best performance by default" — the picker's optimization target is quality, not cost; cost is a constraint, not the objective; **(iii)** "read actual remaining usage left and keep it updated" — slice 6's refresh-cadence + ring-buffer + predictor address the "actual" and "keep updated" parts.

- [ ] `minsky-multi-agent-executable` — minsky callable from CLI, Claude Code, and opencode with similar maximum functionality (MCP server + CLI + slash commands)
  - **ID**: minsky-multi-agent-executable
  - **Tags**: p0, operator-directive, mcp-server, multi-agent-surface, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (extend with `serve-mcp` subcommand), `novel/minsky-mcp/**` (new package), `novel/tick-loop/src/{commands,actions}/*.ts` (extract command handlers as pure functions for reuse across CLI / MCP / slash-command surfaces), `.claude/skills/minsky/SKILL.md` (new — Claude Code slash command), `opencode.json` example with `mcp` block referencing the local Minsky MCP server, `docs/minsky-multi-agent-surface.md` (new — operator-facing).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10, *"I want minsky to be executable from cli, from claude, from opencode with similar maximum available functionality. Add tasks and implement it."*
  - **Estimate**: 5d (extract command handlers + MCP server + Claude skill + opencode integration + docs).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — when minsky exposes an MCP surface, the orchestrator role can be played by ANY MCP-capable agent (Claude Code today, opencode, future agents). Composes with `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` (P0 — opencode is one of the consumers), `claude-usage-aware-strategic-model-router` (P0 — exposes the picker as an MCP tool so an agent can ASK "what model should I use right now?" without spawning the daemon).
  - **Hypothesis**: today minsky is invocable only as a shell command (`pnpm minsky`, `pnpm minsky doctor`, `pnpm minsky bootstrap-local-llm`, etc.). Agents (Claude Code, opencode) can already invoke these via their Bash tool, but each invocation pays the full daemon-spawn cost (~2-3s startup) and the agent has to parse text output. For "similar maximum functionality" across CLI / Claude / opencode, the right substrate is a single MCP server (Anthropic's Model Context Protocol — supported by Claude Code natively and by opencode via its `mcp` config block) that exposes minsky's commands as typed tools. CLI stays as the thin client; Claude Code consumes via MCP; opencode consumes via MCP; the same handler runs all three. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** `pnpm minsky serve-mcp` starts an MCP server (stdio transport per the MCP spec) exposing ≥6 tools (`status`, `start`, `stop`, `restart-mlx-server`, `doctor`, `pick-strategic-model`); **(b)** Claude Code's `~/.config/claude/mcp.json` (or repo-level `.claude/mcp.json`) gains an entry referencing the local Minsky MCP server, and a `/minsky` slash command in Claude Code surfaces those tools without an explicit Bash invocation; **(c)** opencode's `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json` `mcp` block gains an entry referencing the same MCP server, and `opencode run` can invoke minsky's tools mid-session; **(d)** every command handler is a pure function tested in isolation — the CLI / MCP / slash-command surfaces are thin adapters. Pivot: if MCP's stdio transport proves brittle for long-lived Minsky tools (the daemon needs persistence; MCP servers are typically per-session), pivot to HTTP transport (MCP over HTTP is published in the 2026-04 spec update) so the daemon can be a long-running HTTP server clients connect to.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet):
    - **Slice 1 — extract command handlers as pure functions** (1d): today `bin/minsky.mjs` mixes argv parsing with command logic. Extract handlers into `novel/tick-loop/src/commands/{status,start-mlx,stop-mlx,restart-mlx,doctor,pick-strategic-model}.ts` exporting `runX(input): Promise<XOutput>` with typed input/output. CLI becomes a thin argv parser → handler dispatcher. 30+ paired tests across the handlers.
    - **Slice 2 — `pnpm minsky serve-mcp` MCP server** (1d): new `novel/minsky-mcp/` package exposing the handlers as MCP tools per the [MCP spec](https://modelcontextprotocol.io/specification). Uses the official `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` Node bindings. Stdio transport for v0; HTTP transport as the slice-3 ratchet if needed. Each tool's input schema mirrors the handler's typed input; output is the typed output, JSON-serialised.
    - **Slice 3 — Claude Code integration** (1d): `.claude/skills/minsky/SKILL.md` (new) declares the slash command. Operator pastes a one-liner into `~/.config/claude/mcp.json` to register the server; subsequent Claude Code sessions get `/minsky status`, `/minsky pick-strategic-model`, etc. Documentation includes the exact paste-able JSON.
    - **Slice 4 — opencode integration** (0.5d): example `opencode.json` `mcp` block under a new doc section showing how to register Minsky's MCP server. Operator's per-machine `opencode.json` can include the entry; `opencode run` then invokes Minsky tools as part of its agent loop.
    - **Slice 5 — chaos invariants + docs + minsky doctor extension** (1d): chaos table (5 rows: MCP server crash, transport disconnect, malformed tool input, concurrent tool calls, version-mismatch between client and server). 3 new self-diagnose invariants. `docs/minsky-multi-agent-surface.md` with the full operator path for each agent. `minsky doctor` extension shows MCP server health.
  - **Files** (per slice): `novel/tick-loop/src/commands/*.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 1, 30+ tests), `novel/minsky-mcp/{package.json,src/index.ts,src/index.test.ts}` (slice 2 — new package), `novel/tick-loop/bin/minsky.mjs` (slices 1+2 — extract dispatcher + add `serve-mcp` subcommand), `.claude/skills/minsky/SKILL.md` (slice 3 — new), `docs/minsky-multi-agent-surface.md` (slice 5), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 5 — three new invariants).
  - **Verification**: paired tests at every slice. Integration tests: (a) `pnpm minsky serve-mcp` starts and responds to MCP `tools/list` request with all 6 tools; (b) sample Claude Code session via the slash command produces the expected output for `/minsky status`; (c) sample opencode session with the MCP block configured can call `pick-strategic-model` mid-iteration. Chaos: `chaos-mcp-server-crash.mjs` (kill server mid-call; client gets a clear error).
  - **Measurement**: post-slice-3, the operator's Claude Code `/minsky pick-strategic-model` response time is ≤1s (vs ~3s for `pnpm minsky pick-strategic-model` shell invocation, since MCP avoids the per-call daemon-spawn cost). Acceptance threshold: ≥6 tools exposed; ≥1 successful end-to-end Claude Code session and ≥1 successful end-to-end opencode session calling Minsky tools without manual fallback.
  - **Pivot**: if MCP stdio transport doesn't work cleanly with a long-running daemon (the daemon needs cross-call state — claim ownership, hysteresis, etc.), pivot slice 2 to HTTP transport. If MCP's tool-call latency is dominated by JSON-schema validation overhead (>200ms per call on slow machines), pivot to a lighter shape (gRPC, plain HTTP/JSON without schema validation). If the operator finds Claude Code's slash-command surface awkward, pivot slice 3 to a subagent definition (`~/.config/claude/agents/minsky.md`) that auto-invokes Minsky tools as part of the agent's reasoning.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `commands/*.ts` pure functions with 30+ paired tests. (2) `pnpm minsky serve-mcp` starts an MCP server. (3) `.claude/skills/minsky/SKILL.md` ships with the operator-paste JSON. (4) `opencode.json` example documented. (5) `docs/minsky-multi-agent-surface.md` walks through the operator path for each agent. (6) Live-fire: ≥1 successful call from each surface (CLI, Claude Code slash command, opencode mid-iteration).
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #1 (don't reinvent — MCP is the documented standard for agent-tool integration; adopting it gives Claude Code + opencode + future agents the same surface for free); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `commands/*.ts` are the seam between argv-parsing/MCP/slash-command surfaces); rule #6 (stay alive — MCP server crashes are graceful-degrade, fall through to direct CLI); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(d) above); [Anthropic MCP spec](https://modelcontextprotocol.io/specification); [Claude Code MCP integration docs](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/mcp); [opencode MCP config docs](https://opencode.ai/docs/mcp/).
  - **Risk**: medium. (a) **MCP SDK version churn** — `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` is pre-1.0; API may shift. Mitigation: pin a specific version in `package.json`; quarterly refresh process. (b) **Daemon state vs MCP per-call statelessness** — MCP tool calls are typically stateless; minsky's daemon has session state (claims, hysteresis, ring buffer). Mitigation: the MCP server reads from / writes to the same `.minsky/state.json` the daemon uses; concurrent-write coordination via the existing `flock` claim layer. (c) **Multi-agent concurrent calls** — Claude Code AND opencode both calling `start-mlx-server` simultaneously. Mitigation: `flock`-protected lifecycle commands (already exist in the daemon's claim layer). (d) **Operator confusion** — three surfaces (CLI / Claude / opencode) means three places to look when something goes wrong. Mitigation: `minsky doctor` extension surfaces ALL three surfaces' health in one view.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) which transport — stdio or HTTP? Stdio is simpler but per-session; HTTP is more flexible but requires port management. Proposal: ship stdio in slice 2, ratchet to HTTP in slice 3 if the long-lived daemon use case requires it. (b) does Minsky's MCP server expose ALL daemon commands or only a curated subset? Proposal: curated subset for v0 (the 6 lifecycle + picker tools listed in (a)); add tools as operators surface needs. (c) how does the MCP server interact with the running daemon? Proposal: read-only operations (status, doctor, pick-strategic-model) read from `.minsky/state.json`; write operations (start, stop, restart) shell out to the existing CLI subcommands so there's one source of truth for lifecycle logic. (d) what happens when the MCP client and the running daemon disagree (e.g., daemon thinks it's at iteration 50, MCP client just called `stop` — which wins)? Proposal: write operations always win (the `stop` invocation kills the daemon process); reads return the most-recent persisted state.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"I want minsky to be executable from cli, from claude, from opencode with similar maximum available functionality. Add tasks and implement it."* The composing tasks (#claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout, #support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack, #claude-usage-aware-strategic-model-router) all point at minsky as the load-bearing daemon; making it agent-callable as a first-class tool surface is the natural next ratchet.

- [ ] `local-agent-config-validation-at-boot` — pre-spawn validation of opencode/aider config + structured failure-class attribute on iteration spans
  - **ID**: local-agent-config-validation-at-boot
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, observability, local-llm, follow-up, surfaced-by-real-fire
  - **Touches**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (new `local-agent-config-readable` invariant), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (extend `buildIterationReason` to emit `failure_class` attribute), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (pre-iteration probe gate when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT` is set), `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (operator recovery path).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10 real-fire test of `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` revealed an opaque iteration failure when `<repo>/opencode.json` carried an unrecognized `attachment` key. Iteration burned 30s before failing; the operator-recovery path (parse the stderr → identify the bad key → fix `opencode.json`) was discoverable but not surfaced.
  - **Estimate**: 1d (1 invariant + 1 pre-iteration probe + 1 doc section + paired tests).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` (P0, line 529 — closes the operator-config-validation gap that slice 5's chaos table promises). Composes with `claude-usage-aware-strategic-model-router`'s self-diagnose substrate (slice 7, just shipped — adds another invariant alongside `model-catalog-invariants-hold`).
  - **Hypothesis**: when the operator's `opencode.json` is invalid (e.g., `Unrecognized key: attachment` per opencode 1.14.46's strict schema), `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` iterations fail with an opaque `iteration.reason` that mixes a bun warning + the actual config error. Today's failure mode buries the actionable message in stderr; the operator has to grep. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** a self-diagnose invariant `local-agent-config-readable` runs at supervisor boot and surfaces "opencode.json fails opencode 1.14.46 schema (key X)" as a structured TASKS.md finding the moment the operator restarts the daemon; **(b)** every `iteration.failed` span carries a `failure_class` attribute (one of `local-agent-config-error` / `local-agent-binary-missing` / `local-server-unreachable` / `local-spawn-timeout` / `unknown`) so the operator can `grep -c '"failure_class":"local-agent-config-error"' .minsky/workers/*.log` for trend; **(c)** when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` is set AND `opencode --version` exits non-zero on boot, the daemon refuses to dispatch local iterations with a clear "fix opencode config first" reason rather than burning 30s per iteration on `Unrecognized key`. Pivot: if the schema validation shape proves brittle (opencode adds new top-level keys frequently and minsky's check rejects them as unknown), pivot to a stderr-tail regex matcher (`/Unrecognized key: \w+/`) instead of an explicit allowlist.
  - **Details**:
    - **Slice 1 — `local-agent-config-readable` self-diagnose invariant** (0.5d): new invariant in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` exporting `localAgentConfigReadableInvariant({readConfig, runVersionCheck})`. Two-step check: (1) parse `<repo>/opencode.json` if present (graceful-degrade if missing — opencode falls through to global config); (2) if `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` is set, exec `opencode --version` and capture stderr; non-zero exit → invariant fires with the stderr tail in `evidence`. Wired into `defaultInvariants()`. 5 paired tests covering: config-missing-graceful, config-malformed-JSON, config-rejected-by-opencode, agent=aider-skips-opencode-check, all-clean-passes.
    - **Slice 2 — structured `failure_class` on iteration spans** (0.5d): extend `buildIterationReason` in `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` to also return a `failure_class` field. Classifier is a pure function that pattern-matches the iteration's stderrTail: `Unrecognized key|Configuration is invalid` → `local-agent-config-error`; `command not found|ENOENT` → `local-agent-binary-missing`; `ECONNREFUSED|HTTP 5\d\d` → `local-server-unreachable`; `timed out after \d+ms|claude-print-timeout|local-spawn-timeout` → `local-spawn-timeout`; else `unknown`. Span emission in `runStrategyIteration` adds `iteration.failure_class` to the existing `iteration.reason`/`iteration.status` tuple. 8+ paired tests covering each class + the unknown fallthrough.
    - **Slice 3 — pre-iteration probe gate** (optional ratchet — defer if slice 1's invariant proves sufficient): when `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` is set, the bin runs `opencode --version` once at boot (cached for the daemon's lifetime); if it fails, the local-strategy refuses to dispatch and every iteration fails fast with `failure_class: "local-agent-config-error"`. Prevents 30s timeouts on every iteration when the config is broken.
    - **Slice 4 — operator recovery doc** (0.25d): extend `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (filed in #support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack slice 5) with a "When the iteration fails with `local-agent-config-error`" section: how to read the stderr, common bad keys (operator's own `attachment` was the canonical case), where to find opencode's schema docs.
  - **Files**: `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 1), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2 — extend `buildIterationReason` + add `classifyFailure` pure helper), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slice 3 — pre-iteration probe), `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (slice 4).
  - **Verification**: paired tests at every slice. Integration test: deliberately break `opencode.json` (add `"attachment": {}`); restart daemon; assert `local-agent-config-readable` invariant fires with `evidence` containing `attachment`. Live-fire (manual): with the operator's current `opencode.json` (which has the `attachment` key), the daemon's first boot surfaces the issue as a TASKS.md finding within 10s of supervisor start.
  - **Measurement**: `grep -c '"failure_class":"local-agent-config-error"' .minsky/workers/*.log` over 7d → operator-actionable trend metric (high → fix the config; low → other failure classes). Acceptance: post-fix, the test scenario (broken opencode.json + `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode`) surfaces a self-diagnose finding with the structured `failure_class` within ≤10s of daemon start.
  - **Pivot**: if the schema-validation check adds boot latency >500ms (operator-noticed), pivot to a lazier check that runs only on the first iteration and caches the result. If the regex classifier produces ≥1 mis-classification per week (e.g., a different opencode error gets bucketed as `unknown` when it's really a config error), tighten the regex set with a paired test that captures the real-world stderr.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-10 real-fire — operator's `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` iteration failed with opaque error `Configuration is invalid at /Users/cbrwizard/apps/minsky/opencode.json — Unrecognized key: attachment`; iteration.reason mixed a bun warning + the config error. Recovery path was discoverable but not surfaced. Rule #2 (Strategy seam — classifier is a pure function fed by stderr-tail input); rule #4 (visible-not-silent — `failure_class` span attribute makes the failure mode greppable); rule #7 (graceful-degrade — invariant fires once at boot rather than per-iteration); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(c) above); composes with #self-diagnose-on-start substrate.
  - **Risk**: low. (a) The schema-validation check is just running `opencode --version` and capturing stderr; opencode itself does the validation. The only failure mode is opencode being missing entirely (then `--version` fails, which IS the right signal). (b) The `failure_class` regex set may need expansion as new error patterns surface; that's a paired-test ratchet, not architectural risk.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) does `opencode --version` actually load the project `opencode.json`, or skip it? Verify experimentally before relying on it as the validation channel. If it doesn't, fall back to `opencode models` which DOES load config (per the operator's earlier session) and produces the same error. (b) should the pre-iteration probe (slice 3) be opt-in (`MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT_BOOT_PROBE=1`) or default-on? Proposal: default-on; the cost is sub-second and the value is high. (c) does the `failure_class` belong on the iteration span only, or also on a new `tick-loop.iteration.failure-class.histogram` aggregated metric? Proposal: span only for v0; histogram is an OTEL-export concern that ratchets with the existing OTEL slice.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 real-fire test of `pnpm minsky` with `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=opencode` and `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`. Iteration failed in 30s with `Configuration is invalid at /Users/cbrwizard/apps/minsky/opencode.json — Unrecognized key: attachment`. The operator's `opencode.json` (which the operator was iterating on in a separate Claude session) had an `attachment` key that opencode 1.14.46 rejects. The daemon happily dispatched the iteration, opencode failed, the iteration was marked failed — but the actionable signal (which key, which file) was in the stderr tail rather than a structured failure-class attribute the operator could grep. This task surfaces it.

- [ ] `local-server-concurrency-aware-worker-spawn` — local-LLM server (mlx_lm.server / LM Studio) is single-inference; N parallel workers all routed local serialize and divide throughput by N
  - **ID**: local-server-concurrency-aware-worker-spawn
  - **Tags**: p0, daemon, concurrency, local-llm, parallel-workers, follow-up, surfaced-by-real-fire
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/auto-scale-runner.ts` (concurrency-aware autoscale: cap workers at 1 when all routed local), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (boot-time detection of local-server concurrency; emit `tick-loop.local-server.contention` span), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (new `local-server-concurrency-mismatch` invariant), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` + `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (per-stack concurrency notes).
  - **Pick-next**: yes — operator 2026-05-10 real-fire of 3-worker local-only spawn revealed all 3 aider clients serializing on the single mlx_lm.server. Throughput was ~1/3× a single-worker run; watchdog timeouts piled up across all 3.
  - **Estimate**: 2d (1 self-diagnose invariant + autoscale-cap logic + paired tests + docs).
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446 — its N-worker fanout assumed claude scale-out, not the local-server bottleneck). Composes with `support-opencode-lmstudio-mlx-qwen3-14b-stack` (P0 — both opencode and aider hit the same single-inference server). Composes with `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` (P0 — its `--workers-total=N` flag works fine for git/file claim but is a footgun for local routing).
  - **Hypothesis**: `mlx_lm.server` and `LM Studio` (in their default configurations) serve ONE inference at a time; concurrent client requests queue on the server side. When `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1` + `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` are set AND the operator spawns N workers via `--workers-total=N`, every iteration routes local, all N aider/opencode clients hammer the same server, and effective throughput collapses to `~1/N × single-worker`. Compounding: each iteration's wall-time grows N-fold under contention, which is more likely to hit the `MINSKY_CLAUDE_PRINT_TIMEOUT_MS` watchdog → all N iterations fail simultaneously rather than 1 succeeding while N-1 wait. Today (2026-05-10) the auto-scale runner has no awareness of this; it scales workers based on TASKS.md queue depth + recent failure rate, not local-server capacity. Pre-registration: post-fix, **(a)** when `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1` AND `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`, the auto-scale runner caps `currentWorkers` at 1 (regardless of `MINSKY_AUTO_SCALE_MAX_WORKERS`); operator can override via `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT=N` if their backend (e.g., vLLM, sglang) supports concurrent inference. **(b)** the supervisor emits a `tick-loop.local-server.contention` span every tick when `currentWorkers > MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` (default 1 for mlx_lm/LM-Studio, 8 for vLLM); operator can grep the supervisor log for capacity-headroom signal. **(c)** the `local-server-concurrency-mismatch` self-diagnose invariant fires when `pgrep -f "tick-loop.mjs --worker-id"` count > the local-server concurrency cap. (d) the bin's parallel-worker boot log warns the operator: `WARN: spawning N workers but local-server capacity is 1; expect ~1/N effective throughput. Set MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT=N in your env if your local-LLM backend handles concurrent inference (vLLM, sglang).` Pivot: if operators routinely run vLLM-class backends (which DO handle concurrent inference well), the default-1-cap is wrong — pivot to probe-based detection (`GET /v1/models?details` returns concurrency capability on some servers).
  - **Details**:
    - **Slice 1 — `local-server-concurrency-mismatch` self-diagnose invariant** (0.5d): runs at supervisor boot + every 5min thereafter. Reads `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` (default 1), counts `tick-loop.mjs --worker-id` processes, fires when count > cap AND any of those workers' `iteration.provider:"local"` (non-zero local fraction). Evidence: PID list + `iteration.provider` ratio over last 10 iterations. Suggested fix: reduce `--workers-total` OR set `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` to match backend capability.
    - **Slice 2 — concurrency-aware auto-scale** (0.5d): `decideAutoScale` (pure function in `auto-scale-runner.ts`) gains an `effectiveLocalConcurrencyCap` input. When `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1` is set AND `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred` is set AND `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` ≤ 1, the decision returns `verdict: "hold", reason: "local-server-single-inference: cap is 1 but currentWorkers=N"` rather than scaling up. Operator's hard-set `--workers-total` still wins (we don't terminate already-spawned workers; we just stop scaling further). Paired tests for the new branch.
    - **Slice 3 — boot-log warning** (0.25d): `bin/tick-loop.mjs` emits a single-line WARN when `--workers-total > MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` AND `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1`. Operator-actionable; doesn't refuse to start (rule #7 — operator can override).
    - **Slice 4 — per-tick contention span + docs** (0.5d): every iteration when local-routing emits `tick-loop.local-server.contention { workers: N, cap: 1, contention: true|false }`. Docs sections in `local-llm-fallback.md` (mlx_lm.server is single-inference) and `local-llm-opencode.md` (LM Studio default is single-inference; concurrent-inference modes require Pro tier as of 2026-05).
    - **Slice 5 — alternative backend documentation** (0.25d): a new `docs/local-llm-concurrent-inference.md` covers vLLM + sglang + LM Studio Pro as paths to concurrent local inference. Operator-pinned configurations + per-backend `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` recommendations.
  - **Files** (per slice): `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 1), `novel/tick-loop/src/auto-scale-runner.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slices 3+4), `docs/local-llm-fallback.md` + `docs/local-llm-opencode.md` (slice 4), `docs/local-llm-concurrent-inference.md` (slice 5, new).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the autoscale branch + the self-diagnose invariant. Live-fire (manual): spawn 3 workers with `MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1 MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`; assert auto-scale runner logs `local-server-single-inference: cap is 1 but currentWorkers=3`; assert the boot WARN fires; assert the self-diagnose invariant fires within 5min.
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, `grep -c '"local-server.contention":true' .minsky/workers/*.log` over 7d → 0 on operator-tuned setups (correct cap set); ≥1 on misconfigured setups (operator-actionable signal). Direct: with `--workers-total=3 MINSKY_LOCAL_LLM=1 MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`, the auto-scale verdict is `hold` rather than `up`; no second / third worker is spawned by the autoscaler beyond what the operator manually launched.
  - **Pivot**: if vLLM-class backends (which DO handle 8-16 concurrent requests well) become operator-default, flip the cap default from `1` to a probe-based discovery (try a small concurrent-2 request; if both succeed in <2× single-request time, raise cap). If operators commonly run `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` higher than the actual server can handle (over-promised env), add a runtime check that compares completion times tick-over-tick and auto-de-rates.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `local-server-concurrency-mismatch` self-diagnose invariant ships with paired tests. (2) `decideAutoScale` returns `hold` reason when local cap is 1 and currentWorkers > 1. (3) `bin/tick-loop.mjs` emits boot WARN when over-spawned. (4) `tick-loop.local-server.contention` span emitted per tick under contention. (5) `docs/local-llm-concurrent-inference.md` documents the vLLM + sglang + LM-Studio-Pro paths. (6) Live-fire: with the operator's current setup (mlx_lm.server, single-inference), spawning 3 workers via the existing `--workers-total=3` route surfaces a self-diagnose finding within 5min.
  - **Anchor**: 2026-05-10 real-fire of 3-worker local-only spawn — three aider clients serialized on the single `mlx_lm.server`; each iteration grew N-fold under contention; all three hit the 7-min watchdog. Rule #2 (Strategy seam — `effectiveLocalConcurrencyCap` is the seam between operator's `--workers-total` directive and the autoscaler's verdict); rule #4 (visible-not-silent — boot WARN + per-tick contention span); rule #7 (graceful-degrade — operator's hard-set `--workers-total` still wins; we just stop autoscaling); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(d) above). Anthropic / opencode docs reference: [LM Studio's concurrent-inference docs](https://lmstudio.ai/docs/developer/api-concurrency) (Pro-tier feature 2026); [mlx_lm.server source — single inference per process](https://github.com/ml-explore/mlx-lm/blob/main/mlx_lm/server.py); [vLLM concurrent inference baseline](https://docs.vllm.ai/en/latest/serving/openai_compatible_server.html) (default 8 concurrent).
  - **Risk**: low-medium. (a) **operator footgun** — operator sets `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT=10` but their backend can only handle 1; auto-scale spawns 10 workers; throughput collapses. Mitigation: slice 2's pivot — if completion times grow N-fold under contention, auto-de-rate the env value with a self-diagnose finding. (b) **kill-running-workers temptation** — when contention is detected, do NOT terminate already-spawned workers (rule #6 — let-it-crash boundaries; we just stop autoscaling further). (c) **over-conservative default** — operators running vLLM get throttled to 1 worker by default. Mitigation: documented `MINSKY_LOCAL_SERVER_MAX_CONCURRENT` env + a probe-based ratchet in slice 2's pivot.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) does mlx_lm.server reject concurrent requests outright, or does it queue them? Verify via a small chaos script; if it queues, the rule-#7 graceful-degrade is "queueing happens, observer sees N-fold latency"; if it rejects, "5xx fast-fail per concurrent client". (b) does LM Studio have a documented concurrent-inference flag? Some 2026 versions support it; check the docs operator linked. (c) should the per-iteration brief carry an `expected_concurrency_cap` attr so the picker (slice 4 of strategic-router) knows to prefer claude when local capacity is 1 and workers > 1? Proposal: yes — composes into the strategic-router's `pickStrategicModel` input.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 real-fire test. Operator: *"continue calling minsky on itself and actively spawn workers for that; but each of those workers must be local agent"*. Spawned 3 workers via `--workers-total=3` with `MINSKY_LOCAL_AGENT=aider`, `MINSKY_LLM_PROVIDER=local-preferred`, all 3 routed `iteration.provider:"local"` (correct), all 3 spawned aider (correct), all 3 aider clients hit the same `mlx_lm.server` simultaneously and serialized. The flock-based claim layer worked correctly (3 different tasks). The single-mlx_lm.server bottleneck wasn't surfaced anywhere — operator only sees it in `ps aux` showing 3 aider procs at 0% CPU each.

<!-- Security P0 sweep (user brief 2026-05-04: "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything"). Six tasks below operationalise the threat model end-to-end. They are P0 because Minsky's blast radius is large: the supervisor has full disk read on `~/.claude/projects/` (every Claude Code session log on the machine — chats, code, secrets pasted in chats), spawns `claude --print` per iteration (auth token in env), serves an HTTP dashboard (potentially exposed on a LAN), publishes spans to OTEL (potentially with PII), and edits any file in the repo (which can include `.env`, credentials, lock files). A single regression in any of these axes is a real leak. The tasks below cover: secret-scanning at commit (block leaks before push), supervisor sandboxing (constrain the daemon's syscall surface), token / credential hygiene (the things the supervisor reads), OTEL/dashboard data minimisation (no PII in spans, no public binding by default), supply-chain hardening (lockfile integrity + SBOM + SLSA), and an external security audit gate (third-party review before the cloud tier ships). The P0 framing is deliberate — security regressions are silent and discovered late; rule-#10 deterministic-enforcement is the lever. -->

- [ ] `secret-scanning-precommit-and-ci` — gitleaks (or trufflehog) scan in pre-commit + CI; secrets detected = block merge
  - **ID**: secret-scanning-precommit-and-ci
  - **Tags**: security, p0, leak-prevention, rule-10
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: The supervisor edits arbitrary files in the repo per iteration (including config, env templates, plist files); without a deterministic gate, a single regression can write `OPENAI_API_KEY=...` / `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=...` / a private RSA key into a tracked file and push it. Industry baseline: Anthropic / GitHub / npm / etc. all rotate compromised tokens within 24h of detection, but the leak window before detection is real (median TTD for leaked tokens on public GitHub is hours; Truffle Security 2023 study). A `gitleaks` (or `trufflehog`) scan in lefthook pre-commit + GH Actions CI catches secrets before they ship. **Pre-registration**: 0 secrets in the repo at baseline (verified by initial scan); 0 secrets allowed to land in any future PR. Pivot if scan rate is too noisy (>2 false positives per month → tune the allow-list / gitleaks `.gitleaks.toml` config).
  - **Details**: (a) Add `gitleaks` to lefthook's pre-commit hook (already used for biome/typecheck/test); fail commit on any finding. (b) Add `.github/workflows/ci.yml` job `secret-scan` that runs `gitleaks detect --redact --no-banner --exit-code 1` on the PR diff; mark `needs:` in the `ci` aggregator. (c) `.gitleaks.toml` config tuned for the project — start with the default ruleset, allow-list any false positives encountered (each allow-list entry must reference a TASKS-id justifying the exclusion). (d) **One-time historical audit**: run `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all"` against all reachable history; any historical leak goes into a P0 rotation task (separate; needs immediate human approval per the no-cross-repo / no-message-board rule, since rotating an API key is a human-visible action). (e) Operator escape hatch: `MINSKY_SKIP_SECRET_SCAN=1` for the local pre-commit hook only (NOT for CI — CI is non-bypassable).
  - **Files**: `.lefthook.yml` (new pre-commit step), `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (new job + needs entry), `.gitleaks.toml` (new — tuned config), `docs/security/secret-scanning.md` (operator guide explaining the override + how to add allow-list entries).
  - **Verification**: paired tests via fixture commits (a synthetic test with a fake AWS-style key in a temp branch — `gitleaks` rejects it; same fixture without the key — passes); CI job blocks merge on the seeded fixture; `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all"` against current main returns 0 findings.
  - **Measurement**: `gitleaks detect --log-opts="--all" --no-banner --exit-code 1; echo $?` returns 0 against main (no historical leaks). After merge: `gh api repos/fyodoriv/minsky/actions/workflows --jq '.workflows[] | select(.name == "secret-scan") | .state'` returns "active". Per-PR: every PR's checks include a passing `secret-scan` job.
  - **Pivot**: if gitleaks's default ruleset produces ≥3 false positives in the first month, swap to trufflehog (more aggressive entropy detection but more tunable per-pattern). The lefthook + CI integration is reversible — only the scanner binary changes.
  - **Acceptance**: zero secrets in current main (verified by full-history scan); pre-commit hook blocks new secrets locally; CI blocks new secrets on every PR; the historical-audit task is filed as a separate task (since rotation is a human action).
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #1, "no secrets in the repo, ever"); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement — secret detection is a CI lint, not a hope); Truffle Security "The State of Secrets Sprawl 2023" (median TTD for public GitHub secrets is in hours; the cost of a leak is real); Beyer SRE 2016 Ch. 5 (defence in depth — pre-commit catches operator slips; CI catches everything else); rule #2 (the scanner is a Strategy seam — gitleaks → trufflehog pivot is one config change).
  - **Risk**: low-medium. False positives are the main operational risk; mitigation is the allow-list + pivot threshold.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything."

- [ ] `supervisor-sandbox-syscall-restriction` — restrict the supervisor's filesystem + network reach to the minimum it actually needs
  - **ID**: supervisor-sandbox-syscall-restriction
  - **Tags**: security, p0, sandbox, supervisor, blast-radius
  - **Estimate**: 2w
  - **Hypothesis**: Today the launchd / systemd-user supervisor runs as the operator's full UID with no syscall restrictions — it can read every file in `$HOME`, write anywhere, open any network port. The actual surface it needs is much narrower: read `~/.claude/projects/` (token-monitor JSONLs), read+write `<repo>/` (git operations), execute `claude` / `node` / `git` / `pnpm` / `gh` (and nothing else), bind a localhost port for the dashboard. A regression that causes the supervisor to read `~/.ssh/` or `~/Documents/` should fail loudly, not silently exfiltrate. macOS sandbox-exec (deprecated but still functional) + Linux systemd `ProtectHome=`, `ProtectSystem=`, `ReadWritePaths=`, `RestrictAddressFamilies=`, `SystemCallFilter=` are the levers. **Pre-registration**: the sandboxed supervisor passes every existing dogfood iteration smoke (the same lints / tests / iterations work) AND `sandbox-exec` (or systemd) blocks reads to `~/.ssh/` (verified via a chaos test that intentionally reads it from inside the supervisor — should fail with EPERM). Pivot if the constraint set is too tight to allow normal operation (>3 iterations per week fail with EPERM on legitimate paths the operator uses) — relax that specific path with a TASKS-id-justified entry, don't disable the sandbox entirely.
  - **Details**: (a) macOS: write a sandbox profile in `distribution/launchd/com.minsky.tick-loop.sb` (Apple TrustedBSD MAC profile — `(version 1) (deny default) (allow ...)` syntax). The launchd plist's `ProgramArguments` becomes `/usr/bin/sandbox-exec -f <profile> <run-tick-loop.sh>`. (b) Linux: extend `distribution/systemd/minsky-tick-loop.service` with `ProtectHome=read-only` (with `ReadWritePaths=<repo>` for the writable subset), `ProtectSystem=strict`, `PrivateTmp=true`, `RestrictAddressFamilies=AF_UNIX AF_INET AF_INET6`, `SystemCallFilter=@system-service`, `NoNewPrivileges=true`. (c) Both: chaos test in `scripts/chaos/sandbox-attempts-disallowed-read.mjs` — spawned inside the supervisor via the dry-run path; tries to read `~/.ssh/known_hosts`; expects EPERM. (d) Operator escape hatch: `MINSKY_SANDBOX=off` for emergencies (rule #2 + Beyer SRE Ch. 17). (e) Documentation: `docs/security/supervisor-sandbox.md` explains the threat model + the allow-list + how to extend it.
  - **Files**: `distribution/launchd/com.minsky.tick-loop.sb` (new — pending), `distribution/systemd/minsky-tick-loop.service` (extended — stage 0 safe directives shipped this PR), `distribution/systemd/minsky-budget-guard.service` (extended — stage 0 safe directives shipped this PR), `distribution/systemd/minsky-watchdog.service` (extended — stage 0 safe directives shipped this PR), `scripts/check-supervisor-sandbox-hardening.mjs` (new — stage 0 lint pinning the safe directive set across all three units; paired test shipped this PR), `scripts/chaos/sandbox-attempts-disallowed-read.mjs` (new — pending; paired test), `docs/security/supervisor-sandbox.md` (new — shipped #342), README mentions of the sandbox + escape hatch.
  - **Verification**: `pnpm dogfood` works post-sandbox (regression suite); chaos test asserts EPERM on `~/.ssh/`; manual: `cat ~/.ssh/id_rsa` from inside the supervisor's spawn fails with EPERM.
  - **Measurement**: `sandbox-exec -f distribution/launchd/com.minsky.tick-loop.sb /bin/cat ~/.ssh/known_hosts; echo $?` returns non-zero (sandbox blocks). On Linux: `systemd-run --user --uid=$(id -u) --slice=minsky-test --property=ProtectHome=read-only /bin/cat /home/$(whoami)/.ssh/known_hosts` returns non-zero. After supervisor restart with sandbox on: existing dogfood iteration smoke passes — `tail .minsky/tick-loop.out.log | grep -c '"iteration.status":"completed"'` ≥ 1 within 30 minutes.
  - **Pivot**: if the macOS sandbox-exec API is removed by Apple (it has been deprecated since macOS 14), pivot to a wrapper based on `seatbelt` (the underlying mechanism, still exposed via private API) OR to running the supervisor inside a Docker container with `--security-opt=apparmor=...`. The Linux systemd config is unaffected.
  - **Acceptance**: sandbox profile shipped; chaos test pins the EPERM-on-disallowed-path behaviour; existing dogfood still works; the override env documented.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #3, "supervisor sandbox"); McKusick & Watson's TrustedBSD MAC framework (the `sandbox-exec` substrate); systemd's hardening guide (`systemd.exec(5)` man page — every property cited above is a documented security primitive); Saltzer & Schroeder 1975 "The Protection of Information in Computer Systems" — principle of least privilege; rule #7 (graceful-degrade chaos table — every disallowed path attempt is itself a chaos test fixture).
  - **Risk**: high. Sandboxing introduces real friction with normal operation; the path-allow-list is the most likely source of false positives. Mitigation: ship in stages (pre-merge: dry-run the sandbox locally for 7 days; post-merge: ramp via `MINSKY_SANDBOX=warn-only` for 14 days, then `MINSKY_SANDBOX=enforce`). Each ramp step is a separate PR, not a single big-bang change.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything."

- [ ] `otel-no-pii-in-spans-lint` — CI lint that blocks any `record({...})` call carrying PII-shaped attributes
  - **ID**: otel-no-pii-in-spans-lint
  - **Tags**: security, p0, otel, observability, leak-prevention, rule-10
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Hypothesis**: Every `record({...})` call in `novel/**/*.ts` becomes an OTEL span. Spans flow to OpenObserve (and, in the cloud tier, to a multi-tenant aggregator). A regression that puts a Claude API key in a span (`record({apiKey: env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY})` is an easy mistake) leaks across the whole pipeline. The lint scans for: attribute names matching `(api[_-]?key|password|token|secret|credential|bearer)` or values matching `(sk-[a-zA-Z0-9]{20,}|ghp_[a-zA-Z0-9]{30,})` and rejects them. **Pre-registration**: 0 PII-shaped attributes across all current `record({...})` calls (verified via initial sweep); 0 allowed in any future PR. Pivot if the regex is too narrow (a leak-class slips through) or too noisy (≥2 false positives per month → refine rules).
  - **Details**: (a) `scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs` — regex over `record\(\{[^}]+\}\)` call sites in `novel/**/*.ts`. (b) Pure decision function `classifySpanAttribute(name, value): {ok: boolean, reason?: string}` with paired tests. (c) Allow-list: explicit annotations like `// @otel-pii-allowed: <reason>` next to a flagged line, recording why this particular attribute is intentionally PII-shaped (e.g., a hash of an opaque ID where the regex false-positives on the `_token` substring). Each allow-list usage requires a TASKS-id justifying it.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs` + paired tests, `.github/workflows/ci.yml` job + `needs:` entry.
  - **Verification**: ≥6 paired tests (token-named-attribute / sk-prefixed-value / password-named / safe-attribute-name / annotated-allowlist-honored / nested-object-traversed); CI job runs on every PR.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-rule-otel-no-pii.mjs --diff-base=origin/main` exits 0 against current main (no leaks today). Synthetic fixture: `test/fixtures/otel-pii/leaking-span.ts` containing `record({apiKey: env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY})` makes the lint exit 1.
  - **Pivot**: if the regex misses a leak class (e.g., the operator names a field `userPassphrase` instead of `password`), extend the regex with a learned pattern; the allow-list grows when refinement causes a false positive. Don't drop the lint — the alternative is "trust the operator", which is exactly what fails.
  - **Acceptance**: 0 PII-shaped attributes in current spans; lint blocks new ones; doc in `docs/security/otel-no-pii.md` explains what counts.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #2, "no PII in OTEL spans"); rule #4 (OTEL coverage; this is the security companion); rule #10 (deterministic enforcement); GDPR Art. 25 (data protection by design); CCPA equivalent in California; OWASP A04 "Insecure Design".
  - **Risk**: low. Static regex over source code; both false-positive and false-negative are tunable.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything."

- [ ] `cloud-tier-external-security-audit-gate` — block the cloud tier ship until a third-party security audit clears
  - **ID**: cloud-tier-external-security-audit-gate
  - **Tags**: security, p0, audit, cloud-tier, blocked-until-cloud-readiness
  - **Estimate**: external — 4-8w from when triggered
  - **Blocked**: needs-user-approval — engaging an external security audit firm is a human action (vendor selection, contract, payment) and out of scope for autonomous loops per `feedback_modify_only_minsky_repo.md`. Filed here so the gate exists in advance of the cloud tier shipping; user must approve in a separate session before this task starts.
  - **Hypothesis**: The local CLI's blast radius is the operator's own machine (already heavily mitigated by the other 5 P0 tasks here). The cloud tier's blast radius is **every customer's repo**, **every customer's API tokens**, and **every customer's data flowing through the multi-tenant OTEL aggregator**. Self-audit is insufficient — operators / customers correctly discount internal claims. **Pre-registration**: before any cloud tier feature ships to a non-operator user, an external firm (Trail of Bits / NCC Group / Doyensec / a comparable specialist) audits the threat model + sample implementation; their report is public (or at minimum the executive summary is); their critical findings are remediated and re-tested before the gate clears. Pivot if the audit cost exceeds the cloud tier's projected MRR for 12 months — postpone the cloud tier until the unit economics support a real audit; don't ship cloud-multi-tenant without one.
  - **Details**: (a) Block any PR that touches `novel/cloud-supervisor/`, `novel/cross-repo-benchmark/`, or `novel/shared-invariant-catalog/` (when those packages exist) until this task's `**Blocked**` line is removed. The block is enforced by a CI lint that scans for those package paths in the PR diff. (b) Scope of audit: cloud-supervisor's GH App auth flow, multi-tenant data isolation, OTEL ingestion pipeline, billing-once-paywall-lands. (c) Findings tracker: each finding is a P0 sub-task; gate clears only when all P0 sub-tasks ship.
