  - **Files**: `scripts/check-cloud-audit-gate.mjs` + tests, `.github/workflows/ci.yml` (new lint), `docs/security/audit-gate.md` (operator-facing — explains the gate + the unblock criteria).
  - **Verification**: synthetic PR touching `novel/cloud-supervisor/` is rejected by the lint; same diff after this task's `**Blocked**` line is removed → accepted.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-cloud-audit-gate.mjs --diff=test/fixtures/cloud-tier-without-audit.diff` exits 1; same with audit-cleared fixture exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if no external audit firm has bandwidth in a 4-8w window, the gate stays — the cloud tier just doesn't ship. Don't auto-clear the gate based on internal review alone (that's exactly the failure mode the audit prevents).
  - **Acceptance**: gate lint shipped + `needs:`-ed; cloud-tier sub-tasks (in the `paid-tier-features-skeleton` block) reference this gate as a prerequisite; doc explains what triggers the gate clear.
  - **Anchor**: rule #13 (security & privacy as #2 priority after performance — this task implements minimum-bar item #6, "external security audit gate before cloud tier"); CNCF Security TAG's recommendation that multi-tenant infra ships with third-party audit; the empirical reality that every cloud-SaaS breach since 2020 (Log4Shell-adjacent, MOVEit, etc.) was eventually caught by external researchers — internal review is insufficient; rule #1 (use the existing audit-firm market — don't reinvent).
  - **Risk**: low for the gate itself (small CI lint); high for the cloud tier as a whole (this gate is what makes that risk manageable).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user brief — "Add P0 tasks to make sure that minsky is extremely secure and doesn't leak anything." Pairs with `paid-tier-features-skeleton` (P3) — this gate is the security prerequisite for that task's cloud sub-tasks.

## P1

<!-- 9-hour monitoring window 2026-05-06 22:00 → 2026-05-07 ~07:30 surfaced these P1 ergonomics findings — operator-flagged but not loop-breaking. -->

<!-- task-aware-model-router (P1) — operator directive 2026-05-07 surfaced by an external "10-day routing experiment" post the operator shared: a developer logged 150 randomly-sampled coding tasks across 10 days, re-ran each on both cloud-frontier and local Qwen3.6-27B, and found a strong task-class × local-match-rate pattern: file-reads / scanning / "explain code" matched 97 % (35 % of workload), test-writing / boilerplate / single-file-edits matched 88 % (30 %), multi-file debugging dropped to 61 % (20 %), architecture / 5+ file refactors at 29 % (15 %). The operator's translation: "we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time". This task formalises Minsky's per-iteration model router — composes with the P0 local-LLM-fallback substrate (#358 / #365) but with a different decision surface: the P0 fires on budget-circuit-break (emergency); this P1 fires every iteration (routine routing). -->

- [ ] `task-aware-model-router` — daemon classifies each iteration into a routing bucket (docs / single-file slice / multi-file debug / architecture) and routes to the cheapest model that meets that bucket's quality bar, enabling 25-worker concurrent operation within Claude Max 20 budget
  - **ID**: task-aware-model-router
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, throughput, cost-optimization, model-routing, scale, pick-next-after-358-365
  - **Pick-next**: queued behind P0 local-LLM-fallback substrate (#358 merged + #365 on the way) — the substrate must be in main before this P1's slice 1 can land.
  - **Estimate**: 5d (4 code slices ratchet from a measurement preparation slice).
  - **Hypothesis**: External 10-day routing experiment (operator-shared post 2026-05-07): a developer re-ran 150 randomly-sampled coding tasks across both frontier-cloud and local Qwen3.6-27B-on-3090, finding **65 % of routine coding work runs identically on a model that costs only electricity, another 20 % is close enough to accept the occasional miss, and only 15 % genuinely justifies cloud frontier pricing**. Mapped onto Minsky's iteration kinds: brief refreshes / TASKS.md edits / docs-only PRs / metric snapshots / no-code self-diagnose runs are bucket 1 (route to local always); paired-test slices / single-file pure-function additions are bucket 2 (route to local first, fall back to cloud if CI red ≥2×); I/O-wrapper slices / CI-fix iterations / lint-fix iterations are bucket 3 (route to a cheap cloud tier — Sonnet/Haiku — with local as last-resort fallback under budget pressure); substrate slices touching ≥5 files / constitutional-rule changes / cross-package refactors are bucket 4 (route to Opus-grade cloud only; if unavailable, hold rather than burn budget on a degraded run). Pre-registration: post-router, **(a)** the rolling 7d Claude-token-spend per shipped PR drops by ≥40 % vs the pre-router baseline, **(b)** the rolling 7d PR-merge throughput is unchanged-or-up (no quality regression), **(c)** Minsky can sustain 25 concurrent workers within the Claude Max 20 plan budget envelope without triggering `circuit-break-and-notify` more than once per 24 h.
  - **Details**: (a) **Slice 0 (preparation PR — measurement substrate)**: instrument the daemon to emit `iteration.routing.bucket` (one of `docs`, `single-file`, `multi-file`, `architecture`), `iteration.routing.provider` (one of `claude-opus`, `claude-sonnet`, `claude-haiku`, `local-qwen`), and `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` OTEL span attributes for **every** iteration — even pre-router, every iteration is currently `claude-opus-4-7`. Lands `node scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs --since=$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) --json` that reports per-bucket counts, per-provider counts, total tokens, and per-PR-merge cost. This is the rule-#9 baseline; without it, slice 1+ can't measure their own effect. (b) **Slice 1 — pure classifier**: `classifyIteration({ taskBlock, expectedFiles, fileCount, recentPrFailureCount, briefSize }) → { bucket: "docs" | "single-file" | "multi-file" | "architecture", confidence: number }` in `novel/tick-loop/src/iteration-classifier.ts` + 25+ paired tests. Inputs are derived purely from the task block + the daemon's iteration plan; no network calls. (c) **Slice 2 — pure router**: `routeProvider({ bucket, budgetState, claudeProbeResult, localProbeResult, recentBucketSuccessRate }) → { provider: "claude-opus" | "claude-sonnet" | "claude-haiku" | "local-qwen", reason: string }` in `novel/tick-loop/src/provider-router.ts` + 30+ paired tests. Composes with `decideProvider` from P0 #358's substrate (the budget-paused fallback path is preserved as a strict override — circuit-break still wins). (d) **Slice 3 — wire-in + spawn-strategy adapter**: extend `ProcessSpawnStrategy` to dispatch among 4 invocation shapes (`buildClaudePrintInvocation { model: "opus" | "sonnet" | "haiku" }` + `buildAiderInvocation` for local); wire `classifyIteration` + `routeProvider` into `tick-loop.mjs` boot path. The aider invocation hard-codes `--edit-format diff-fenced` per the format gotcha recorded in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`. (e) **Slice 4 — quality gate + auto-tune**: per-bucket rolling 30-iteration success rate (PR merged within 4h CI-clean) is recorded as `routing.bucket.success_rate`; if a bucket's local-routing success rate drops ≥10 pp below its "ought-to" baseline (97 / 88 / 61 / 29 from the load-bearing post), the router auto-promotes that bucket to the next-cheapest cloud tier for 50 iterations, then re-tests local; the re-test prevents permanent degradation while preserving cost discipline. (f) **Slice 5 — 25-worker scale enablement**: memory-pressure invariant in `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (`vm_stat | grep "Pages free" < 100k → fire`); single-shared-mlx-server pool semaphore (max 12 concurrent local invocations) so 25 workers don't thundering-herd the local model; per-worker brief-size budget (cap at 20k tokens to avoid local-model context-overflow on bucket 1+2). (g) **Slice 6 — dashboard column + cost-per-PR rolling chart**.
  - **Files**: `TASKS.md` (this block — slice 0 substrate), `docs/task-aware-model-router.md` (operator-facing routing matrix + bucket definitions + the load-bearing post citation), `scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (slice 0), `novel/tick-loop/src/iteration-classifier.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 1), `novel/tick-loop/src/provider-router.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 2), `novel/tick-loop/src/spawn-strategy.ts` (slice 3 — extend dispatcher), `novel/tick-loop/src/aider-invocation.ts` (slice 3 — `--edit-format diff-fenced` hard-coded), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slice 3 — wire-in), `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.ts` (slice 3 — emit `iteration.routing.{bucket,provider}` + `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` span attrs), `novel/tick-loop/src/router-quality-gate.ts` + `.test.ts` (slice 4), `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` (slice 5 — memory-pressure invariant), `novel/dashboard-web/src/routing-column.ts` (slice 6).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for `classifyIteration` (25+ cases including the 4 canonical buckets + edge cases: empty task block, task block with only docs files, task block with `Files:` listing 8 files, brief refresh of an already-shipped task). Paired tests for `routeProvider` (30+ cases: each bucket × each budget state × each probe state × each bucket-success-rate band). Integration test: replay 50 historical iterations from `.minsky/workers/*.log`, assert the router's bucket assignment matches a hand-coded expected-bucket label (≥90 % agreement with operator labelling). Chaos test: at 25 concurrent workers, assert no worker waits >60 s on a local-LLM-server lock; assert no `vm_stat` page-free reading drops below 50 k for >2 min.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/iteration-routing-baseline.mjs --since=$(date -v-7d -u +%Y-%m-%d) --json` returns `{"buckets": {"docs": N1, "single-file": N2, "multi-file": N3, "architecture": N4}, "providers": {"claude-opus": M1, "claude-sonnet": M2, "claude-haiku": M3, "local-qwen": M4}, "tokens": {"prompt": Tp, "completion": Tc, "total": Tt}, "cost_per_merged_pr_usd": C, "merged_pr_count": P}`. Acceptance thresholds (rolling 7d, post-slice-3-merge): **(a)** `cost_per_merged_pr_usd` ≤ 0.6 × pre-router baseline (≥40 % cost reduction); **(b)** `merged_pr_count` ≥ pre-router baseline (no throughput regression); **(c)** `circuit-break-and-notify` events from `.minsky/budget-guard.out.log` ≤ 1 per 24 h sustained at 25-worker concurrency. Per-bucket success rate threshold (rolling 30 iterations per bucket): docs ≥ 92 %, single-file ≥ 80 %, multi-file ≥ 55 %, architecture ≥ 25 % (slack of ~5 pp under the load-bearing post's numbers, accounting for Minsky's stricter CI gate stack vs an unstructured benchmark).
  - **Pivot**: if the rolling 7d cost reduction is <20 % (i.e., the router doesn't actually save money), the bucket-classification accuracy is the bottleneck; pivot to a *learned* classifier (small fine-tune on Minsky's own iteration history) rather than a heuristic one. If multi-file or architecture buckets see local-success-rate drop below 40 % / 15 % respectively for 30 consecutive iterations, retire local routing for that bucket entirely — the post's 61 % / 29 % numbers were on a 3090 with Qwen3.6-27B; M1 Max on Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B may not match those for hard buckets. Don't push local into a bucket where it's not pulling its weight; the rule-#9 mandate against vanity activity applies. If the 25-worker target triggers `circuit-break-and-notify` more than 1×/24 h sustained for 7 days, the router's not the bottleneck — the budget envelope is — pivot to "20 workers, accept lower theoretical max" rather than burning Max 20 plan headroom on retries.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `iteration.routing.{bucket,provider}` + `iteration.token.{prompt,completion,total}` span attrs emitted on every iteration (slice 0). (2) `classifyIteration` pure function with 25+ paired tests, ≥90 % agreement with operator labelling on a 50-iteration historical replay (slice 1). (3) `routeProvider` pure function with 30+ paired tests, composes with the P0 `decideProvider` budget-fallback (slice 2). (4) `spawn-strategy.ts` dispatches among 4 invocation shapes, `--edit-format diff-fenced` hard-coded for local (slice 3). (5) Per-bucket auto-tune fires + reverts within 50 iterations (slice 4 — verified via 7d chaos run). (6) 25 concurrent workers sustained for 24 h without triggering `circuit-break-and-notify` more than 1× and without any `vm_stat` page-free reading dropping below 50 k for >2 min (slice 5). (7) Dashboard shows per-bucket counts + per-provider cost-per-PR rolling 24h (slice 6).
  - **Anchor**: operator-shared 10-day routing experiment post 2026-05-07 (load-bearing prior — the 97 / 88 / 61 / 29 bucket-quality numbers); operator directive 2026-05-07 — "we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time"; rule #1 (don't reinvent — the post's bucket model is industry-validated; adopt it rather than designing a novel taxonomy); rule #6 (stay alive — running 25 workers all the time means more total throughput even with per-iteration quality dispersion); rule #9 (this task's measurement is the rolling 7d `cost_per_merged_pr_usd` query, pre-registered above; success threshold ≤ 0.6 × baseline; pivot threshold <20 % reduction); rule #13 (security-privacy — local routing keeps more code on-device, reducing data-egress surface, which is a positive externality of cost-discipline routing); Forsgren et al. 2018 (DORA's deployment frequency — the router is judged by sustained throughput, not per-iteration latency); Saltzer & Schroeder 1975 (fail-safe defaults — when in doubt about a bucket, default to the more-capable cloud tier rather than the cheaper local one — quality bar holds); the load-bearing post itself: "we're just too lazy to measure it" — slice 0's measurement substrate is the explicit refusal to skip that measurement.
  - **Risk**: medium-high. (a) **Mis-classification — high impact**: a complex task routed to local burns iterations on an under-capable model. Mitigation: slice 1's confidence score; iterations below `confidence < 0.7` always route to claude-sonnet rather than local; slice 4's auto-tune catches sustained mis-routes within 30 iterations. (b) **Local model overload at 25 workers**: 25 concurrent aider clients hammering one mlx-lm.server instance creates queue depth and tail latency. Mitigation: slice 5's 12-concurrent semaphore — extra workers queue rather than spawn additional aider processes. (c) **Memory pressure on M1 Max 32GB**: 25 worktrees × ~500 MB Python aider + 17.2 GB local model + ~5 GB cloud-claude processes ≈ 27 GB resident; tight on 32 GB unified memory. Mitigation: slice 5's `vm_stat` invariant; if page-free drops below 50 k, the supervisor pauses worker spawning. (d) **Quality regression masked by routing**: a router that routes everything-hard to claude makes the local-success metric look good while shipping nothing local. Mitigation: slice 4's per-bucket-success-rate gate watches the actual local-routed rate, not the routed-to rate. (e) **Aider format-gotcha drift**: if a future Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B-Instruct point-release breaks the `diff-fenced` integration, all bucket 1+2 work fails silently. Mitigation: the existing smoke test (Run B in `docs/local-llm-fallback.md`) becomes a CI gate (`pnpm smoke:local-llm`) that runs nightly and fires a P0 task if it fails.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-07 operator directive — *"I think as P1 we should optimize minsky token usage so that it always uses various models including local one based on tasks. Ideally we want 25 workers working at the same time with claude max 20 and also no critical issues at the same time"* — citing a foodtruck-bench-post-style 10-day routing experiment where a developer logged 150 random coding tasks across local + cloud models and found 65 % of routine work runs identically on a local model that "costs only electricity". The post's load-bearing claim: *"we're just too lazy to measure it"* — slice 0's measurement substrate is Minsky's explicit refusal to skip that measurement.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — this block provides the 4-bucket classifier + provider router. The parent adds the **role-pin override** (orchestrator iterations always Opus; worker iterations always local-first) so role wins over per-iteration bucket when they conflict.

- [ ] `daemon-local-model-self-tune` — daemon evaluates rolling per-iteration metrics by local-model and auto-swaps the per-machine pin when a better-fitting model is observed; operator approves once, daemon reconciles forever
  - **ID**: daemon-local-model-self-tune
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, local-llm, self-tuning, model-router, follow-up
  - **Touches**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` (new), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (extends #worker-model-per-machine-config), `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` (new), `.minsky/local-config.json` (rewrite via Strategy seam, never directly edited).
  - **Pick-next**: queued behind P0 #worker-model-per-machine-config (PR #404 filed) and P1 #task-aware-model-router slice 0 — the resolution chain + per-iteration `iteration.routing.{provider,model}` spans are the substrate this consumes.
  - **Estimate**: 3d (1d for the leaderboard fixture + probe; 1d for the recommender + tests; 1d for the auto-rewrite + rollback gate).
  - **Hypothesis**: today the per-machine local model is pinned by the operator at file-edit time (`.minsky/local-config.json`) based on a one-shot recency check (the user's 2026-05-10 swap from Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B → Qwen3.6-27B Dense was a one-time decision keyed off a leaderboard query). Six months later that pin will be wrong: model families ship every quarter; the M1 Max 32GB tier specifically has had Qwen 2.5-Coder-32B → Qwen3-Coder-30B-A3B → Qwen3.6-27B-Dense in 12 months. Operator's 2026-05-10 directive: *"minsky should be able to figure out a better local running model for the machine based on metrics. It should be able to change setup."* Pre-registration: post-fix, the daemon reads its own rolling-30d per-iteration spans (per #task-aware-model-router slice 0) bucketed by `iteration.routing.model`, computes a per-model `merged-pr-rate` and `tokens-per-merged-pr`, compares against the periodically-refreshed leaderboard fixture (`scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --json` — pulls SWE-bench Verified + Terminal-Bench 2.0 + RAM tier from the cited sources, capped at the machine's RAM tier), and **(a)** when a candidate model has ≥10 pp higher SWE-bench Verified than the current pin AND fits the machine's RAM AND has ≥3 corroborating sources in the leaderboard fixture, the recommender writes a P0 task block `local-model-swap-candidate-<id>` that proposes the swap; **(b)** if the operator has enabled `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`, the recommender ALSO updates `.minsky/local-config.json` (gitignored, per-machine) and emits a `local-model.auto-swapped` OTEL span with before/after model IDs + rationale; **(c)** rollback gate — if the post-swap rolling-50-iteration `merged-pr-rate` is more than 5 pp below the pre-swap baseline, the recommender auto-reverts the pin and files a Blocked task with the regression details. Without (c), a bad swap could silently degrade throughput for days. Pivot: if leaderboard recency drift is too coarse (the fixture is ≥30d stale most of the time) the recommender is reading dead data; pivot to live-fetch via `WebFetch` against the same sources the operator's recency-check uses, with an offline cache for the daemon's `MINSKY_NETWORK_DENY` mode.
  - **Details** (slices ratchet):
    - **Slice 1 — leaderboard fixture + probe** (1d): `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` ships an offline JSON fixture at `scripts/fixtures/local-model-leaderboard.json` with the canonical sources (`benchlm.ai`, `kilo.ai`, `tokenmix.ai`, `huggingface.co/mlx-community`, `swebench.com`) and per-model rows: `{model_id, ram_q4_gb, swe_bench_verified, terminal_bench_2, hf_mlx_repo, source_urls, recorded_at}`. The fixture is updated quarterly via a manual operator process documented in `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md`; the script's `--refresh` flag uses `WebFetch` against the source URLs (rate-limited, opt-in) when network is available. Pure read-only on read; mutation only via `--refresh`.
    - **Slice 2 — recommender** (1d): `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` exports `recommendLocalModel({ currentModel, machineRamGb, recentSpans, leaderboard }) → { kind: "stay" | "swap-candidate" | "rollback"; toModel?: string; rationale: string; sources: string[] }`. Pure function; tested with 30+ paired cases covering: stay-no-better-model, stay-not-enough-RAM, swap-recommended-with-corroboration, rollback-after-regression, leaderboard-stale-fallback. The "rollback" kind fires only when post-swap rolling spans show ≥5 pp `merged-pr-rate` regression vs the pre-swap baseline (which the recommender persists in `.minsky/state.json` under `local-model-history` on every swap).
    - **Slice 3 — wire-in + auto-rewrite** (1d): `bin/tick-loop.mjs` runs the recommender every N=50 iterations (cheap, pure call). When `kind === "swap-candidate"`, files a P0 task block via the existing `self-diagnose.mjs` writer (composes with #self-diagnose-on-start). When `kind === "swap-candidate"` AND `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1` is set, additionally rewrites `.minsky/local-config.json` via the resolution chain's writer (a new function `setLocalConfigField` in `local-config.ts`; the existing `resolveLocalModel` is read-only). When `kind === "rollback"`, ALWAYS rewrites the config back (rollback bypasses the auto-swap opt-in — the gate exists to prevent regressions, not to require operator approval to undo them). Emits `local-model.auto-swapped` / `local-model.rollback` OTEL spans with before/after IDs.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/local-model-recommender.ts` + `.test.ts` (new, slice 2), `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs` + `.test.mjs` (new, slice 1), `scripts/fixtures/local-model-leaderboard.json` (new, slice 1 — quarterly-refreshed), `novel/tick-loop/src/local-config.ts` (slice 3 — adds `setLocalConfigField` writer alongside the existing `resolveLocalModel` reader; composes with #worker-model-per-machine-config), `novel/tick-loop/bin/tick-loop.mjs` (slice 3 — N=50 iteration recommender call), `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md` (operator-facing — quarterly-refresh process + the `--refresh` flag).
  - **Verification**: paired tests for the recommender (30+ cases). Integration test: replay 100 fake spans from a fixture into a fake `local-config.json`, assert the recommender stays/swaps/rollbacks correctly across the bucket boundaries. Live-fire (manual): with `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1` set on this M1 Max, run the daemon for 7 days and observe whether the auto-swap fires for a (then-current) better-fitting model in the same RAM tier.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --recommend --json` returns `{kind, currentModel, toModel, rationale, sources}`. Acceptance threshold (rolling 30d, post-slice-3): **(a)** when the leaderboard fixture's top-fitting candidate has ≥10 pp higher SWE-bench Verified AND ≥3 corroborating sources, the recommender returns `kind: "swap-candidate"` deterministically. **(b)** the auto-rewrite path (when `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`) successfully writes `.minsky/local-config.json` with the new pin AND the next `pnpm minsky` boot resolves to that pin (verified via `resolveLocalModel` integration test). **(c)** the rollback path triggers within 50 iterations of a deliberate regression (operator pins a known-bad model in a chaos run; daemon auto-reverts).
  - **Pivot**: if the leaderboard fixture goes ≥30d stale most of the time (operator forgets quarterly refresh), pivot to live-fetch via `WebFetch` (rate-limited; opt-in via `MINSKY_NETWORK_FETCH_LEADERBOARD=1`) with a 90-day cache. If the recommender's swap-candidate rate is ≥1/month for the same machine (chasing leaderboard noise rather than real upgrades), tighten the corroboration threshold from ≥3 sources to ≥5 OR raise the SWE-bench Verified delta threshold from ≥10 pp to ≥15 pp. If the rollback gate fires more than 1×/month sustained, the recommender's confidence is too low; pause auto-swap entirely and require operator approval per swap.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) `recommendLocalModel` ships with 30+ paired tests and the 3-kind decision API. (2) `scripts/local-model-leaderboard.mjs --json` returns a recency-checked fixture; `--refresh` updates it from the cited sources via `WebFetch`. (3) `setLocalConfigField` writer composes with the existing `resolveLocalModel` reader; both round-trip through `.minsky/local-config.json` cleanly. (4) Auto-swap is opt-in (`MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP=1`); rollback is automatic. (5) `local-model.auto-swapped` / `local-model.rollback` OTEL spans emitted with before/after model IDs. (6) `docs/local-model-leaderboard.md` documents the quarterly refresh process. (7) Live-fire on this M1 Max for 7 days: the recommender either swaps to a better-fitting model OR returns `kind: "stay"` consistently (no false positives).
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-10 directive (verbatim above); rule #2 (Strategy seam — `recommendLocalModel` is the seam between operator-intent and runtime; fed by injected leaderboard + spans); rule #7 (graceful degrade — leaderboard fetch failure falls through to "stay"); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD — Hypothesis (a)–(c) above); rule #13 (security-privacy — auto-swap is opt-in, never silent on first deploy); memory rule `feedback_verify_model_recency_at_filing_time` (this task's leaderboard fixture is the institutional form of that rule); composes with #task-aware-model-router (the per-iteration spans this consumes), #worker-model-per-machine-config (the resolution chain this writes through), #self-diagnose-on-start (the task-block writer this reuses for the swap-candidate filing).
  - **Risk**: medium. (a) **Auto-swap to a worse model**: leaderboard claims don't match this machine's actual workload mix. Mitigation: rollback gate (slice 2 — auto-revert on ≥5 pp `merged-pr-rate` regression); auto-swap is opt-in (operator must set the env var explicitly). (b) **Leaderboard fixture rot**: stale data drives bad swap recommendations. Mitigation: `recorded_at` field on every row; recommender refuses to swap when the top candidate's `recorded_at` is >90d old; quarterly-refresh process documented. (c) **Rapid-swap thrashing**: recommender swaps every 50 iterations chasing noise. Mitigation: minimum 200-iteration "settle window" between swaps; hysteresis on the 10 pp delta threshold (must hold for 100 iterations before a swap fires). (d) **Cross-machine drift**: operator runs minsky on multiple Macs; auto-swap on M1 Max picks model X; on M3 Max picks model Y; debugging "why does this machine ship slower PRs?" gets harder. Mitigation: composes with #worker-model-per-machine-config — the per-machine `.minsky/local-config.json` is the source of truth; auto-swap writes only the local file; cross-machine sync stays out of scope.
  - **Open-questions** (must be answered in slice-1 implementation iteration): (a) leaderboard refresh cadence — quarterly is the rule-#9 anchor's recommendation; does the operator want monthly? Trade-off: tighter cadence catches better models faster, fixture file churns more. (b) auto-swap opt-in default — should `MINSKY_LOCAL_MODEL_AUTO_SWAP` default to `1` (aggressive) or `0` (conservative — operator approves each swap)? Proposal: default `0` until 30d of stable rollback-gate observations on operator's own machine; then flip to `1`. (c) does the recommender consider model size as a tiebreaker (smaller = faster = better when SWE-bench Verified is within 2 pp)? Proposal: yes — `tokens-per-merged-pr` is the per-machine throughput metric the rolling spans already compute; a smaller model that ships faster is genuinely better at the daemon-throughput goal even at slightly lower benchmark scores.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-10 operator directive — *"What's more, minsky should be able to figure out a better local running model for the machine based on metrics. It should be able to change setup."* The composition with #worker-model-per-machine-config is load-bearing: that task ships the *static* resolution chain (env > config-file > repo-default); this task ships the *dynamic* leaderboard-aware recommender on top. Without #worker-model-per-machine-config's resolution chain, this task can't write its recommendation anywhere persistent.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — the per-machine model auto-tuning is what makes the worker-role default (always local-first) actually correct over time, not just at file-edit-time.

- [ ] `daemon-brief-test-pin-soft-tolerance` — relax `daemon.test.ts` brief-pin assertions to allow legitimate trims while preserving drift protection
  - **ID**: daemon-brief-test-pin-soft-tolerance
  - **Tags**: p1, daemon, brief, test-quality
  - **Estimate**: 0.5d
  - **Hypothesis**: 9h window 2026-05-07: workers identified valid optimizations (e.g., `−~110 bytes/iter`) that were blocked by exact-string `expect(brief).toContain("...")` pins in `daemon.test.ts`. The pins are good drift protection but block legitimate trims. Pre-registration: post-fix, pins use substring-of-section assertions (`expect(brief).toMatch(new RegExp("...intent keyword..."))`) so wording can be tightened while structure is preserved.
  - **Details**: refactor brief tests to assert intent (e.g., "the section names both body-only checkers") rather than exact prose. Identify which pins are load-bearing (test-pinned-string contracts) vs drift-protective (must-mention).
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/src/daemon.test.ts`.
  - **Verification**: existing brief-content tests still pass; deliberate prose mutation that drops a load-bearing section still fails.
  - **Measurement**: post-fix, the median brief-trim PR adds 0 test-update commits (currently averages 1).
  - **Pivot**: if soft pins miss real regressions, restore exact pins for the specific contracts that broke.
  - **Anchor**: 9h window 2026-05-07 — multiple workers blocked by pin strictness on otherwise-valid trims.
  - **Risk**: low-medium. Drift could slip through; mitigated by mutation-testing the new assertion shape.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 9h monitoring window — workers identified ≥3 pin-blocked optimizations.

Source code citations re-use the read-only findings PR #75 landed (now lifted into `research.md` § "OMC handoff persistence" and gated by `scripts/omc-roundtrip.mjs`) (path layout in `src/team/state-paths.ts`, task shape in `src/team/types.ts:38-58, 195-213`, write site `src/team/state/tasks.ts:90`, read/write call sites `src/team/task-file-ops.ts:157,210-243,321-376`).    
    ````markdown
    Title: Proposal: optional TASKS.md adapter for /team mode (ecosystem alignment with tasks.md spec)

    ## Summary

    Hi @Yeachan-Heo — proposing an optional adapter so `/team` mode can read its task list from a `TASKS.md` at repo root following the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md), with full backward compatibility (current behaviour is the default).

    The tasks.md spec is a minimal, plain-Markdown task-board format maintained by [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (kanban-style board renderer + linter). Multiple tools are converging on it as a portable task substrate: the upstream `tasksmd` toolchain itself, the Minsky project (constitutional rule: TASKS.md is the actor message store — Hewitt 1973), and any tool that wants its task list to be human-editable and version-controlled in the same file plain-text editors and `gh` already understand.

    OMC's `/team` mode already has a well-shaped persisted task store — this proposal is just to let users point that store at a Markdown file when they want a portable substrate.

    ## Where the integration would land (code-level)

    From a read of `Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode@main`:

    - `src/team/state-paths.ts` — `TeamPaths` declares the canonical layout (`.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`, `config.json`, `events.jsonl`, etc.). An adapter would add an alternate source resolver: when `config.json` carries `tasks_source: "tasks.md"`, the adapter reads `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` instead of the per-task JSON files. Default unchanged.
    - `src/team/types.ts` (lines ~38-58, ~195-213) — `TaskFile` / `TeamTask` shape: `id`, `subject`, `description`, `status`, `owner?`, `blocks[]`, `blocked_by?`, `created_at`, `version?`, `claim?`, etc. Maps cleanly to tasks.md fields:
      - `id` ↔ tasks.md `**ID**`
      - `subject` ↔ task title (the `- [ ]` / `- [x]` line)
      - `description` ↔ tasks.md `**Details**`
      - `status` (`pending | in_progress | completed | blocked`) ↔ `[ ]` / `[x]` checkbox + an extension `**Status**` field for the non-binary states
      - `owner` / `claim.owner` ↔ tasks.md `**Owner**`
      - `blocked_by` / `depends_on` ↔ tasks.md `**Blocked by**`
      - `created_at` ↔ provenance comment
      - `version` (optimistic concurrency) ↔ idempotency key in a hidden HTML comment, preserved on round-trip
    - `src/team/state/tasks.ts:90` — `writeAtomic(taskFilePath, JSON.stringify(updated, null, 2))` is the single canonical write site for `claimTask`. An adapter parallel to this would re-render the relevant tasks.md block (write-back is the harder direction; could ship in a v2).
    - `src/team/task-file-ops.ts:157, 210-243, 321-376` — read/write call sites; the read side is where the adapter reads tasks.md when `tasks_source: "tasks.md"` is set.

    The richer OMC v2 fields (`TeamTaskV2`'s `delegation_compliance`, `claim.token`, `claim.leased_until`) don't have natural tasks.md equivalents; the adapter would lossy-project them on read and preserve them in a hidden comment block on write so round-trips are non-destructive.

    ## Why this is ecosystem alignment, not a single-project request

    Three independent adopters of the tasks.md spec today:

    1. The spec maintainers themselves at [tasksmd/tasks.md](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md) (board renderer + linter — `npx @tasks-md/lint`).
    2. Minsky (long-running orchestration substrate; uses TASKS.md as its actor message store).
    3. Any tool that wants tasks to be `git`-diffable, plain-Markdown, editable in a plain-text editor without a runtime — a non-trivial superset given how many devs already keep a `TASKS.md` or `TODO.md` by convention.

    For OMC users specifically, this would mean: a team member without OMC installed can still read and edit the task list as plain Markdown; `gh` PR diffs show task changes in a human-readable format; the task list survives independently of `.omc/state/`.

    ## Concrete proposal

    Add an optional `tasks_source` field to `config.json`:

    ```json
    {
      "name": "my-team",
      "tasks_source": "tasks.md"
    }
    ```

    - When unset (default): current behaviour — read/write `.omc/state/team/<teamName>/tasks/task-<id>.json`.
    - When `"tasks.md"`: read `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md` per the [tasks.md spec](https://github.com/tasksmd/tasks.md); fall back to current behaviour if absent or malformed (with a warning).
    - v0 scope: read-only OMC ← TASKS.md (so OMC's optimistic-concurrency `version` field stays authoritative). Write-back can land in a v1 once the round-trip semantics are settled.

    No breaking changes to existing teams; no new required dependencies (a small Markdown parser would suffice, or `@tasks-md/lint`'s parser if you want to share the spec's reference implementation).

    ## Open question

    Does this fit `/team` mode's design intent — i.e., is the canonical task store something `/team` would want to be pluggable — or would you prefer this live as a separate plugin / adapter package (e.g., `@oh-my-claudecode/tasks-md-adapter`) so the core stays minimal? Happy to draft the PR either way; just want to follow your design preference before writing code.

    Thanks for OMC — `/team` mode's blackboard model is exactly the substrate this is trying to align with.
    ````

  - **Last-enriched**: 2026-05-04

- [ ] `spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring` — substrate for safely running N (4-10) parallel workers with a monitor that auto-unblocks stuck children + files incident tasks
  - **ID**: spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring
  - **Tags**: p2, daemon, supervisor, parallel, watchdog, follow-up
  - **Estimate**: 1w
  - **Hypothesis**: Operator question 2026-05-07: "should and can we spawn 10 workers, all monitored by this window that unblocks them & files tasks so that next time minsky unblocks itself". The 9h window demonstrated I was that monitor manually — killed the worker-1 hang, closed duplicate PRs, fixed body-fail PRs, rebased stuck PRs. Pre-registration: post-fix, a monitor process spawned by `pnpm minsky --spawn-additional-workers=N --watchdog` performs all 4 of those interventions automatically and emits incident spans + TASKS.md filings for each. Rolling-7d operator-manual-intervention count → 0 across N=4 workers; → ≤1/day across N=10.
  - **Details**: (a) New flag `--watchdog` on the root `pnpm minsky` invocation. (b) Watchdog process (separate from worker daemons): runs every 60s, queries `pgrep --parent <worker-pid>` for stuck children (CPU<5% for >15min) → SIGKILLs them. (c) Queries `gh pr list --author "@minsky-bot"` for: PRs CONFLICTING >2h → invokes the rebase watchdog (#daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog); PRs failing only on body-only checks → patches body. (d) For each intervention, files a TASKS.md entry under `## P2` with `**Auto-filed-by**: spawn-n-workers-with-watchdog-monitoring` so the daemon learns the unblock pattern over time. (e) Composes with `daemon-claude-print-hang-watchdog` (P0), `daemon-stuck-pr-rebase-watchdog` (P0), `daemon-task-rotation-on-completion` (P0), `daemon-duplicate-work-detection` (P0) — those four shipped is the precondition for safe N≥4.
  - **Files**: `novel/tick-loop/bin/watchdog.mjs` (new bin), `novel/tick-loop/src/watchdog.ts` (pure decisions for kill / rebase / body-patch), `novel/tick-loop/src/watchdog.test.ts` (paired tests for each intervention), `package.json` `bin: { minsky-watchdog: ... }`.
  - **Verification**: paired tests for each intervention class. Integration test: spawn 2 fake workers, simulate a hang, watchdog kills + files task within 60s.
  - **Measurement**: `count(operator-manual-interventions)` per worker per day → see hypothesis thresholds. Concrete log probe: `grep -c 'minsky: operator manually killed' .minsky/workers/*.log` over 7d → 0 (ideal); 1-3 is acceptable while substrate matures.
  - **Pivot**: if the watchdog itself crashes (silence-is-failure on the watchdog), the operator's manual intervention rate stays high — pivot to `launchd KeepAlive` + a separate `minsky-watchdog` plist so the watchdog has its own respawn.
  - **Anchor**: operator 2026-05-07 — "monitor + unblock + file tasks so next time minsky unblocks itself"; `daemon-parallel-worktree-launch` parent task; rule #2 (Strategy seam — pure decisions); rule #6 (let-it-crash — watchdog kills hung children); rule #9 (pre-registered HDD).
  - **Risk**: medium. The watchdog has destructive power (SIGKILL, force-push, body-patch). Mitigations: cap-3 retries before escalating to `Blocked: needs-operator`; all interventions logged + incident-task-filed; opt-out via `MINSKY_WATCHDOG_DRY_RUN=1` for first deploy.
  - **Surfaced-by**: operator 2026-05-07 directive ("file tasks for all findings and bugs… should we spawn 10 workers"); 9h monitoring window 2026-05-06/07 demonstrated all 4 intervention classes manually.
  - **Composes-into**: parent task `claude-orchestrator-local-worker-fanout` (P0, line 446) — this block provides the watchdog substrate (kill stuck child, rebase stuck PR, body-patch). The parent adds the **cross-layer** chaos slice (orchestrator-death-recovery and worker-hang-detection-from-orchestrator-side via `chaos-orchestrator-kill.mjs` and `chaos-worker-hang.mjs`).

## P3

- [ ] `demo-pr-generator` — `minsky run --target=<oss-repo> --output-mode=pr-only` produces a single high-quality demo PR per OSS repo (the funnel)
  - **ID**: demo-pr-generator
  - **Tags**: vision, business, growth, distribution, cross-repo
  - **Estimate**: 2w (compose-from-existing-primitives; no new architecture)
  - **Hypothesis**: A bot that opens a *single* meaningful PR against a target OSS repo — analytics dashboard wired up, chaos table written, rule-#9 hypothesis attached, OTEL spans on hotpaths — is *demonstrably* useful in a way most dev tools aren't. Maintainers see the work, not the marketing. The demo PR is the funnel; converted maintainers either self-host the CLI (free, runs the supervisor on their machine) or sign up for the cloud tier (Minsky-hosted supervisor running 24/7 against their repo). Conversion-rate hypothesis: the click-through from "demo PR opened" to "README badge / cloud signup" is ≥5% across 100 OSS repos in the first quarter (compare to Dependabot's ~30% adoption rate post-acquisition; we're solving a different problem than dep updates so conservative target). Composes from existing primitives: `@minsky/cross-repo-runner` v0 (host-targeting), `@minsky/handoff-spec` (the PR body shape), `@minsky/sidecar-bootstrap` (the per-repo `.minsky/` scaffold). v1 = the operator hand-picks 10 OSS repos and runs the generator manually; v2 = an autonomous discovery layer (GH search by stars + language + activity recency) feeds the queue. **Important constraint**: defaults to *one PR per repo per quarter, opt-in via README badge*, NOT bulk drive-by — Dependabot fatigue is the failure mode.
  - **Details**: (a) New CLI mode `--output-mode=pr-only` on `@minsky/cross-repo-runner` — instead of writing to the host's `.minsky/experiment-store/`, it runs one supervisor iteration in a temporary worktree, then opens a PR via `gh pr create` against the target's default branch with the changes + a templated body (analytics summary + chaos table + rule-#9 self-grade). (b) Templated PR body in `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-template.ts` (pure function — diff stats + signal counts + signup CTA). (c) Idempotency: the generator checks for an existing `[minsky-demo]` label / PR via `gh pr list --label minsky-demo` before opening; never duplicates. (d) Frequency cap: refuses to open if the last `[minsky-demo]` PR on the repo is <90d old. (e) Rate limit: refuses to open if more than N PRs in a 24h window globally (anti-spam). (f) Opt-in surface: target repo's README must contain `<!-- minsky-demo: opt-in -->` OR a maintainer must invite the bot via `@minsky-bot demo` on an issue. v1 leans toward the opt-in side; the autonomous discovery layer is v2. (g) Per the user's vision (2026-05-04): the PR body invites the maintainer to add Minsky to the repo for ongoing supervision — the CTA is the conversion event.
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-mode.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-template.ts` (new), `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/demo-pr-mode.test.ts` (new — paired tests for idempotency + rate-limit + opt-in checks), `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (mode documented), vision.md § Pattern conformance index (new row).
  - **Verification**: 6 paired tests (idempotent / opt-out-respected / rate-limit-honored / template-renders / dry-run-prints-diff / live-mode-opens-PR-against-fixture-repo); manual test run against `fyodoriv/minsky-demo-target` (operator-owned scratch repo) succeeds with one PR opened.
  - **Measurement**: `gh pr list --repo <target> --label minsky-demo --json createdAt,state,reactions --jq '. | length'` ≥ 1 after the manual run. Conversion tracking: `gh pr list ... --jq '[.[] | select(.reactions.totalCount > 0)] | length / length * 100'` ≥ 5 % across 10 manually-targeted OSS repos in 90 days post-launch.
  - **Pivot**: if maintainer reception is hostile (≥1 spam complaint per 10 PRs over the first 30 PRs, or any GH abuse-report), pivot from autonomous-PR to invitation-only. The opt-in `<!-- minsky-demo: opt-in -->` README marker becomes mandatory; we never open PRs unprompted. The discovery-driven v2 stays shelved.
  - **Acceptance**: (1) demo PR opened against an operator-controlled fixture repo with a well-formed body; (2) idempotency + rate-limit + opt-in checks covered by paired tests; (3) PR body's CTA links to the cloud-signup landing page (separate task — the landing page itself is the next thing); (4) manual run against ≥3 real OSS repos to validate maintainer reaction (operator gates between runs). NOT in v1: autonomous discovery, scheduling, billing.
  - **Anchor**: vision (user brief 2026-05-04 — "demo PR is the trojan horse for the cloud tier"); rule #1 (composes existing primitives, doesn't reinvent); rule #12 (this task IS the new scope; pre-registered above); Cialdini *Influence*, 1984 (reciprocity — a maintainer who received a useful PR is more likely to engage); Raymond *The Cathedral and the Bazaar*, 1999 (community-as-distribution — every adopted PR is a distribution surface). Anti-pattern anchor: Dependabot's drive-by PR fatigue at scale (`https://github.com/dependabot/dependabot-core` issue-tracker around 2021-2022) — the per-repo-per-quarter cap is the explicit response.
  - **Risk**: high. The blast radius extends to GitHub's abuse-detection systems and to OSS maintainer goodwill, neither of which we control. Mitigation: hard rate-limit + opt-in default + Pivot threshold tied to the first abuse signal. Stop the autonomous loop if any maintainer asks once.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user vision conversation — "what if minsky is so successful at improving itself that one day it starts choosing open source repos, analyzing them 1 by 1 and writing for each a meaningful improvement pr that demonstrates the whole functionality of minsky".

- [ ] `paid-tier-features-skeleton` — implement the cloud-supervisor + cross-repo-benchmark + invariant-catalog features (free tier for now; paywall comes later)
  - **ID**: paid-tier-features-skeleton
  - **Tags**: vision, business, revenue, cross-repo, observability
  - **Estimate**: 4-6w (three orthogonal features; each its own sub-task)
  - **Hypothesis**: The free CLI does ~95 % of the value (you self-host the supervisor on your machine; it runs the loop against your repo). The cloud tier has to deliver value the local CLI structurally cannot — specifically: **(a) cross-repo benchmarking** (your dashboard's p95 latency vs the median Minsky-managed Node service; only Minsky-cloud has the cross-cohort data), **(b) shared invariant catalog** (the 47 invariants we've collectively detected across 10k repos, available as a one-line `import` in your `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs`; only Minsky-cloud aggregates these), **(c) compliance attestation** (a Minsky-signed quarterly proof that your repo passes the constitutional rule-set; auditors / customers want a signed PDF, not a "trust me bro" README claim). Free vs paid axis is **who hosts the supervisor**, not amount of work — paid = Minsky-cloud runs the supervisor 24/7 + provides (a)/(b)/(c); free = you run the supervisor locally + see your own data only. **Importantly for now**: implement all three features but make them free until we have ≥3 paying-customer demand signals (an unscientific qualitative gate; the alternative — guess at price first — is the vanity-metric trap rule #9 forbids). Paywall task is a separate later task.
  - **Details**: Three sub-tasks, each its own task block to be added when this one ships:
    - **`cloud-supervisor-mode`** — Minsky-cloud-hosted supervisor: a containerised tick-loop that mounts a target repo via the GH App, runs the loop, files PRs through the bot account. Reuses 100 % of the existing `@minsky/tick-loop` daemon — only the I/O boundary changes (GH App auth instead of local fs; OTEL endpoint points at our cloud aggregator). Pivot if cold-start cost per repo per loop iteration exceeds Anthropic's per-call cost by >10× — at that point the cloud tier is unprofitable even free.
    - **`cross-repo-benchmark-aggregator`** — Minsky-cloud aggregates anonymised metric snapshots from every consenting repo (the 10 success metrics already shipped); per-repo dashboard adds a "you vs the cohort median" overlay. Schema: `{repoId, metricId, valueAtTimestamp[], cohortHash}`, retention 90d, opt-in only. Pivot if cohort sizes stay <100 across all metric IDs — without ≥100 repos per cohort the benchmark is statistically meaningless and we should pivot to industry-standard reference (Forsgren/DORA 2018 numbers) instead.
    - **`shared-invariant-catalog`** — `scripts/self-diagnose.mjs` accepts `--catalog=cloud` and pulls additional invariants from `cloud.minsky.dev/invariants`. Each invariant ships with its own paired test + suggestedFix (same shape as the seed invariants in PR #156). v1 = read-only catalog; v2 = community contributions via PR (rule #1: "push upstream" is the discipline). Pivot if catalog growth stalls (<5 new invariants per quarter from non-operator sources) — at that point the catalog is just our seed list and the cloud value disappears.
  - **Files** (skeleton; sub-tasks fill in): `novel/cloud-supervisor/` (new package), `novel/cross-repo-benchmark/` (new package), `novel/shared-invariant-catalog/` (new package), `cloud/` (new directory — deployment manifests for the cloud bits), vision.md § Pattern conformance index (3 new rows).
  - **Verification**: each sub-task ships its own paired tests + chaos table; the umbrella task is "all three sub-tasks shipped + integration test that the cloud bits don't break the local CLI" (a `MINSKY_CLOUD=disabled` env var disables every cloud probe — the local CLI must work identically when set).
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-cloud-disabled.mjs` (new lint) — verifies the CLI runs successfully with `MINSKY_CLOUD=disabled` and produces output identical to the no-cloud-bits baseline. Failing this lint blocks merge of any sub-task PR. Cohort-size measurement: the benchmark aggregator's tests assert ≥100 synthetic repos in the cohort fixture; production-stage measurement is `cloud.minsky.dev/admin/cohort-sizes` (lives in the cloud-deploy task).
  - **Pivot**: if after 6 weeks none of the three features show *any* user-visible value in dogfood (operator's own eyes), pivot to picking just one feature. The candidate ordering by leverage: (1) shared-invariant-catalog (compounds with each new invariant authored), (2) cross-repo-benchmark (compounds with each new repo enrolled), (3) cloud-supervisor (highest infra cost, lowest moat — anyone can run a supervisor in a container).
  - **Acceptance**: three sub-tasks shipped behind `MINSKY_CLOUD={enabled,disabled}` flag; default is `disabled` (free tier ships the local CLI with cloud probes off); `MINSKY_CLOUD=enabled` requires the cloud account (deferred — billing is `paywall-and-billing` task). All three features land as code, all are free during the demand-discovery period.
  - **Anchor**: vision (user brief 2026-05-04 — "free vs paid axis is amount of work"; revised in this conversation to "free vs paid axis is who hosts the supervisor"); rule #2 (every cloud feature behind a Strategy seam — the local CLI keeps working with cloud disabled); rule #9 (each sub-task carries its own hypothesis + measurement + pivot — entered when it's filed); Hamilton, *Foundations of Software Engineering*, 1986 (the rule "build the substrate first, charge for it later" — every paid SaaS we know followed this pattern); Christensen, *The Innovator's Dilemma*, 1997 (a free CLI that does 95 % of the value is the disruptor against tools that bundle the supervisor and the analytics together).
  - **Risk**: high. Cloud infrastructure is a step-change in operational complexity (auth, billing-once-paywall-lands, multi-tenant data isolation, OTEL ingestion at scale). Mitigation: ship one sub-task at a time, each behind its own `MINSKY_CLOUD_<feature>=disabled` flag, with the local CLI remaining the first-class default. The Pivot threshold (none of three features shows value in dogfood) is the hard gate.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 user vision conversation — "Minsky has free tier and paid tier" + my 2026-05-04 reply identifying the moat axes (cross-repo benchmarking / shared invariant catalog / compliance attestation). User's response: "let's add tasks for paid features (temporarily free for now, let's implement the features first)". This task block operationalises that.

- [ ] `omc-tasksmd-bridge-v1-watcher` — reverse-sync + filesystem watcher for the OMC ↔ tasks.md bridge
  - **ID**: omc-tasksmd-bridge-v1-watcher
  - **Tags**: novel, bridge, follow-up, dormant-until-crdt-story
  - **Estimate**: 1–2w (CRDT story + watcher + reverse-sync)
  - **Hypothesis**: Once a CRDT story is sketched for OMC's optimistic-concurrency `version` field (`src/team/state/tasks.ts:90`), a chokidar / `fs.watch`-driven reverse path (tasks.md edits → OMC `claim` / `complete` calls) can propagate a claim in either direction within 1 scheduler iteration without lost-update collisions across 100 random concurrent-edit trials. v0 (read-only) shipped as `@minsky/omc-tasksmd-bridge`; this task closes the deferred half of the original `omc-tasksmd-bridge-v0` Acceptance ("claim propagation in either direction").
  - **Details**: Add `OmcWriter.{claim,complete,update}` mirroring OMC's persisted shape; integrate `chokidar` (or `fs.watch` if portable enough) on both `<repoRoot>/.omc/state/team/**/tasks/*.json` and `<repoRoot>/TASKS.md`; resolve conflicts via OMC's `version` field (compare-and-set). Lossy fields documented in `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/README.md` § "Lossy projection" must be addressed before reverse-sync is safe — either widen the tasks.md spec or extend the bridge to a sidecar JSON.
  - **Files**: `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/{watcher,writer,conflict-resolution}.{ts,test.ts}`, `novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/README.md` (chaos-table additions for the new failure modes)
  - **Verification**: Round-trip property test (random TASKS.md ↔ OMC trials, ≥95 % pass at 100 trials); claim-propagation E2E (claim in either side observed in the other within 1 scheduler iteration).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/round-trip.property.test.ts` exits 0 with ≥95 passed property cases; `pnpm vitest run novel/bridges/omc-tasksmd/src/claim-propagation.e2e.test.ts` exits 0.
  - **Pivot**: if the CRDT story for `version` cannot reach lost-update-free convergence at 100 random concurrent-edit trials (≥1 lost update detected), the reverse path isn't viable; pivot to a *write-throttled* reverse direction (single-writer assumption, scheduler-iteration-rate-limited) and document the asymmetry, OR escalate `omc-tasksmd-issue` to push tasks.md adoption upstream so the bridge can retire entirely.
  - **Acceptance**: Round-trip property test passes ≥95 / 100 trials; claim propagates in either direction within 1 scheduler iteration; bridge published as v1.
  - **Anchor**: Shapiro et al., "Conflict-free Replicated Data Types", *SSS* 2011 (the CRDT story this task waits on); Helland, "Life beyond Distributed Transactions", *CIDR* 2007 (the bridge's eventual-consistency frame); Hewitt 1973 (TASKS.md as the message store).
  - **Risk**: OMC adopts tasks.md upstream before this task lands → the bridge retires entirely (the Goldratt TOC win); track via `omc-tasksmd-issue` in TASKS.md.

- [ ] Quarterly dependency review (Q3 2026)
  - **ID**: review-q3-2026
  - **Tags**: governance
  - **Estimate**: 1d (when due)
  - **Hypothesis**: A quarterly scan of all 14 deps + 5 novel layers surfaces ≥1 dependency whose situation changed materially since the last review (new alternative, deprecation, security advisory) — enough to justify the review's standing existence per rule #1. *Additionally*, the quarterly review reads `validated-learnings.md` and the experiment-tracker verdict log, summarising the calibration of rule #9's predictions (predicted Δ vs observed Δ by hypothesis category) — closing rule #9's quarterly automation layer for any window the MAPE-K loop has not yet covered.
  - **Details**: Per vision.md principle 1, scan all 14 deps and 5 novel layers; reconsider choices. Append to `research.md` "Quarterly review log". **Rule-#9 quarterly-layer scope:** the review's standing checklist now includes (a) total experiments tracked, (b) % `validated`/`regressed`/`inconclusive`, (c) calibration table (mean predicted Δ vs mean observed Δ, grouped by hypothesis category — feature / refactor / bugfix / docs), (d) rule-#9 amendment proposals if any category is systematically miscalibrated.
  - **Verification**: `research.md` has a 2026-Q3 entry under "Quarterly review log" with one line per dep + one line per novel layer
  - **Measurement**: `awk '/^### 2026-Q3/{flag=1; next} /^### /{flag=0} flag' research.md | grep -c '^- '` ≥ 19 (14 deps + 5 novel layers); follow-up tasks filed for any dep flagged → `gh issue list --label dep-review --search '2026-Q3'` recorded in the entry.
  - **Pivot**: if 3 consecutive quarterly reviews surface zero material changes, drop the cadence to semi-annual; if a review surfaces ≥3 material changes, raise to bi-monthly until the rate normalises.
  - **Acceptance**: research.md updated with findings; any dep changes filed as separate P1/P2 tasks
  - **Anchor**: rule #1 (don't reinvent the wheel); Fowler, *Refactoring*, 1999 (review cadence as a refactoring discipline at the architectural scale).
  - **Risk**: Skipped if no calendar reminder set. Add a calendar event before this task is due.

- [ ] `audit-spec-monitor-coverage-q3-2026` — Q3 2026 quarterly audit of spec-monitor advisory rules (due 2026-08-03)
  - **ID**: audit-spec-monitor-coverage-q3-2026
  - **Tags**: audit, conformance, rule-10
  - **Estimate**: 30m / quarter
  - **Hypothesis**: A quarterly read-through of `novel/spec-monitor/SKILL.md`'s ≤5 advisory rules, comparing each against the current `scripts/check-rule-*.mjs` lints (and any newly-shipped `ci-lint-*` linters since the Q2 2026 audit), catches scope-creep before the Skill becomes load-bearing — preserving rule #10's "deterministic checks are authoritative" invariant. Quarterly cadence is the Risk-mitigation note from the original `audit-spec-monitor-coverage` task.
  - **Details**: Re-read SKILL.md. For each advisory rule, ask: "could this be a deterministic linter today, given any new lints shipped since Q2 2026?" If yes, file a follow-up `ci-lint-*` task and (only after the linter ships) remove the advisory rule from SKILL.md per rule #10's ratchet. Confirm rule count ≤5. Compare against the previous audit at `spec-advisories/2026-05-03-quarterly-audit.md`: if the same rules promoted then are still open AND new ones promote now, fire the pivot (reduce cap to 3). After running the audit, file the next quarterly task (`audit-spec-monitor-coverage-q4-2026`).
  - **Files**: `novel/spec-monitor/SKILL.md`, `spec-advisories/2026-08-03-quarterly-audit.md` (or whatever date the audit runs)
  - **Verification**: SKILL.md has ≤5 rules (mechanically enforced by `scripts/check-skill-rule-cap.mjs`); `spec-advisories/<audit-date>.md` exists with rule count and per-rule decisions; any deterministic-candidate filed as a `ci-lint-*` task with full Hypothesis/Success/Pivot/Measurement/Anchor; the Q4 2026 audit task is filed.
  - **Measurement**: `test -f spec-advisories/2026-08-03-quarterly-audit.md && grep -q 'Rule count' spec-advisories/2026-08-03-quarterly-audit.md && grep -q 'audit-spec-monitor-coverage-q4-2026' TASKS.md`
  - **Pivot**: if this audit AND the Q2 2026 audit both promoted ≥1 rule AND the Q2 candidates are still open, the Skill is leaking scope — reduce cap from 5 to 3 in `novel/spec-monitor/SKILL.md` (and update `scripts/check-skill-rule-cap.mjs` accordingly).
  - **Acceptance**: Audit run; SKILL.md compliant; any conversions filed; Q4 task scheduled.
  - **Anchor**: rule #10 (vision.md § 10); Munafò et al., *Nature Human Behaviour* 1, 0021, 2017 (pre-registration of audit pivot before result is observed).
  - **Risk**: Audit forgotten. Mitigation: the next-task standing-loop convention reminds; the previous audit file at `spec-advisories/2026-05-03-quarterly-audit.md` records the cadence.

- [ ] `ci-lint-watch-surface-cap` — CI lint enforcing the 3-value cap on the Watch surface (story 005)
  - **ID**: ci-lint-watch-surface-cap
  - **Tags**: ci, conformance, rule-10
  - **Estimate**: 1h
  - **Hypothesis**: `vision.md` row 12 says the Watch surface is "three values, no chrome; design discipline forbids a fourth" (story 005, anchored to Card & Mackinlay 1999 + Weiser & Brown 1995). Today the cap is prose-only — a future change to the watch JSON contract or the dashboard renderer can silently grow a fourth metric. A tiny linter that counts the value-fields in the watch contract (or the watch JSON fixture) and fails if `> 3` mechanically preserves the calm-tech invariant. Surfaces during `ci-lint-skill-rule-cap`'s resilience scout (PR #ci-lint-skill-rule-cap).
  - **Details**: Locate the canonical watch contract (likely `user-stories/005-*.md` and/or the dashboard adapter when it ships). Count the declared value-fields. Fail if `> 3`. Mirror the `check-skill-rule-cap.mjs` shape: pure function + thin CLI wrapper + paired tests + CI job.
  - **Files**: `scripts/check-watch-surface-cap.mjs`, `scripts/check-watch-surface-cap.test.mjs`, `.github/workflows/ci.yml`
  - **Verification**: synthetic contract with 4 fields → exit 1; same with 3 → exit 0; missing contract → exit 0 (story not yet implemented).
  - **Measurement**: `pnpm vitest run scripts/check-watch-surface-cap.test.mjs` exits 0 with ≥4 cases.
  - **Pivot**: if story 005's ship-shape changes such that the "three numbers" become a single composite gauge (different cap shape), retire this lint and write the new one against the shipped artefact.
  - **Acceptance**: CI job runs; the 3-value cap is mechanically enforced on every PR.
  - **Anchor**: rule #10; vision.md row 12 (Card & Mackinlay 1999; Weiser & Brown 1995).
  - **Risk**: The watch contract's exact location / shape isn't fixed yet (story 005 is not shipped). Mitigation: defer until the contract lands; the linter ships in the same PR as the contract.

- [ ] `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` — Pivot escape hatch for supervisor integration tests
  - **ID**: supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner
  - **Tags**: infra, testing, ci, pivot-followup
  - **Estimate**: 4h
  - **Hypothesis**: If `linux-supervisor-integration` consistently lands as `failure` (not `success` / `skipped`) on GH-hosted Ubuntu runners — i.e. neither `loginctl enable-linger` nor `dbus-run-session` produces a usable user-bus inside the sandbox — moving the Linux job to a self-hosted runner with a real systemd-user session is the documented Pivot in `supervisor-integration-tests`'s EXPERIMENT.yaml.
  - **Details**: Document the self-hosted-runner setup needed (Ubuntu LTS host with `loginctl enable-linger` already on for the runner user; `actions-runner.service` configured to run under that user). Update `.github/workflows/ci.yml` to gate the Linux job on `runs-on: [self-hosted, linux]`. Keep macOS as GH-hosted (launchd works there). File the cost / ownership question (who hosts the runner; is the maintenance overhead worth the empirical signal). This task only fires if the v0 integration jobs prove unworkable on GH-hosted infra.
  - **Files**: `.github/workflows/ci.yml`, `distribution/README.md`, `docs/self-hosted-runner.md` (new)
  - **Verification**: 3 consecutive PRs see `linux-supervisor-integration` land as `success` (not `skipped`) on the self-hosted runner.
  - **Measurement**: `gh run list --workflow ci.yml --branch main --limit 10 --json conclusion,name --jq '[.[] | select(.name == "linux-supervisor-integration") | .conclusion] | map(select(. == "success")) | length' >= 3`.
  - **Pivot**: if self-hosted-runner maintenance burden exceeds the empirical signal value (e.g., the runner needs >1 manual intervention per quarter), retire the Linux integration job entirely and rely on `lint-units.sh` + the macOS integration job alone — document the asymmetry as a declared deviation in `distribution/README.md`.
  - **Acceptance**: This task fires only if `supervisor-integration-tests` v0's Pivot threshold is hit; otherwise it remains a dormant scout entry.
  - **Anchor**: Forsgren et al., *Accelerate*, 2018 (test reliability — a CI gate that doesn't run reliably teaches the team to ignore failure); rule #7 (failure-mode discipline).
  - **Risk**: Self-hosted runners introduce supply-chain risk (a compromised runner can leak secrets). Mitigation: scope the runner to public-repo / non-secret jobs only; standard GH guidance (Forsgren 2018 § DORA prerequisites; rule #7).

- [ ] `lighthouse-self-hosted-runner-pivot` — Next-tier pivot if Lighthouse Mobile 0.85 also proves flaky on GH-hosted runners
  - **ID**: lighthouse-self-hosted-runner-pivot
  - **Tags**: infra, testing, ci, pivot-followup, dashboard-web
  - **Estimate**: 4h
  - **Hypothesis**: Following the 2026-05-04 threshold-pivot from 0.9 → 0.85 (`.github/workflows/lighthouse.yml`, vision.md row 58), the new `≥0.85` Lighthouse Mobile gate is *expected* to be stable on GH-hosted runners — the original observations (0.83 / 0.89) sat 1–2 percentage points below 0.9, so a 5-point drop to 0.85 should swallow the noise. If 0.85 also proves flaky (≥2 false-positive failures per 10 runs at the new threshold over 30 days), the residual variance is structural to the GH-hosted runner (CPU steal, neighbour-VM contention) rather than a tunable threshold property — the only remaining lever is to move Lighthouse to a self-hosted runner with predictable CPU. Same precedent as `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner`.
  - **Details**: If the trigger fires, gate the `lighthouse-mobile` job on `runs-on: [self-hosted, linux]`. Document the runner provisioning needs (predictable CPU, no nested virtualization, Chromium-installable). Coordinate with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` to share infrastructure if both fire — one self-hosted runner can host both jobs. If self-hosted is rejected on cost / ownership grounds, retire the Lighthouse gate entirely and rely on the dashboard-web LoC-cap + chaos-table audits as the residual `dashboard-web-v0` performance proxy — document the asymmetry as a declared deviation in vision.md row 58 and `novel/dashboard-web/README.md`.
  - **Files**: `.github/workflows/lighthouse.yml`, `novel/dashboard-web/README.md`, `vision.md` (row 58 update), `docs/self-hosted-runner.md` (shared with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if it has also fired)
  - **Verification**: 3 consecutive PRs see `lighthouse-mobile` land as `success` on the self-hosted runner with a Lighthouse score reproducibly above 0.85 (variance band ≤ 0.03 across the 3 runs).
  - **Measurement**: `gh run list --workflow lighthouse.yml --branch main --limit 10 --json conclusion --jq '[.[] | .conclusion] | map(select(. == "success")) | length' >= 8` (≥80 % success rate over the last 10 runs after the move) AND a paired `gh run download` + `jq '.categories.performance.score' lighthouse.json` over the same 10 reports shows max−min ≤ 0.03.
  - **Pivot**: if self-hosted-runner maintenance burden exceeds the empirical signal value (e.g., the runner needs >1 manual intervention per quarter), or if 0.85 proves stable for 30 consecutive days *without* the move (the trigger never fires), retire this dormant task — it is a scout entry, not a commitment. If self-hosted is moved to but the variance remains >0.03 across runs, the gate is non-deterministic at root and should be retired entirely (dashboard-web's LoC-cap + chaos-table audits become the residual proxy).
  - **Acceptance**: This task fires *only* if the new 0.85 threshold sees ≥2 false-positive failures per 10 runs sustained over 30 days. Otherwise it remains a dormant scout entry.
  - **Anchor**: rule #9 (vision.md § 9 — pre-registered pivot threshold; this is the next-tier pivot pre-registered in the original `dashboard-web-lighthouse-ci` task); Forsgren, Humble, Kim, *Accelerate*, IT Revolution Press, 2018 (DORA test-reliability — a CI gate that doesn't run reliably teaches the team to ignore failure); Wilkie, "RED Method", *USENIX SREcon EMEA* 2018 (the duration component is the user-perceived metric — moving runners preserves the metric's semantic); Munafò et al., *Nature Human Behaviour* 1, 0021, 2017 (pre-registration — the next-tier pivot was committed *before* the 0.85 threshold's behaviour was observed, in the same PR that lowered the threshold).
  - **Risk**: Self-hosted runners introduce supply-chain risk (a compromised runner can leak secrets). Mitigation: scope the runner to public-repo / non-secret jobs only; share infrastructure with `supervisor-integration-self-hosted-runner` if both fire (cost amortisation); standard GH guidance (Forsgren 2018 § DORA prerequisites; rule #7).

- [ ] `next-task-scope-to-jira-ticket` — `/next-task` should accept a Jira-key argument to pin one-shot bug fixes
  - **ID**: next-task-scope-to-jira-ticket
  - **Tags**: skill, ergonomics, one-shot, surfaced-by-fresh-install
  - **Estimate**: 1h
  - **Hypothesis**: `/next-task` today picks the highest-priority unblocked task across all `~/apps/*/TASKS.md` (per README "queue mode"). For one-shot operator workflows ("ship the fix for PROJ-840 and stop"), the operator must either temp-edit TASKS.md to bump priority or run the work outside `/next-task`. Letting `/next-task <ticket-or-id>` (e.g. `/next-task PROJ-840` or `/next-task proj-840-slash-command-labels`) pin the queue to that one task — claim it, ship it, exit instead of looping — closes the "I just want this one bug shipped" path without weakening the default queue-mode loop. The match is a substring search across either the `**ID**:` field or the task title (the title contains the Jira key for tickets).
  - **Details**: Update `.claude/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` (or wherever the skill lives — confirm via `tasks install` if the auto-install flag works in 0.7.x; per setup.sh comment 295-297, 0.7.0 install is broken, so the skill is hand-committed). Add a `<args>` parser: empty → existing queue-mode; non-empty → grep TASKS.md for the literal arg (Jira-key OR kebab-case ID), claim that single task, work it, exit on completion *without* re-entering the loop. Keep the existing audit-cascade behaviour as the default.
  - **Files**: `.claude/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` (or the equivalent path post-`tasks install` shipping), a small unit test that simulates the arg-parsing path.
  - **Verification**: `/next-task PROJ-840` claims `proj-840-slash-command-labels` from `~/apps/example-capabilities-3/TASKS.md` (via the title-match path), ships the PR, exits — does NOT proceed to the next P1.
  - **Measurement**: An integration shell-script that seeds `~/apps/test-fixture/TASKS.md` with two tasks, calls the skill driver with the second task's Jira-key as arg, and asserts the first task remains unclaimed at end-of-run (`grep -c '@' TASKS.md` == 1).
  - **Pivot**: if Jira-key matching collides with kebab-id matching often enough that operators get the wrong task (≥1 mis-claim per 10 invocations), restrict matching to `**ID**:` field only and require operators to use kebab-case IDs (PROJ-840 → `proj-840-slash-command-labels`).
  - **Acceptance**: One-shot mode works from the README's documented path; queue-mode unchanged when arg is empty; collision behaviour documented.
  - **Anchor**: Cooper, *About Face: The Essentials of Interaction Design*, 4th ed., Wiley, 2014 (modal vs modeless interfaces — the same affordance carrying both queue-mode and one-shot mode is modeless, and modeless wins when the user's intent is unambiguous from the arg); rule #1 (don't reinvent — `/next-task` already exists, the change is one optional arg).
  - **Risk**: low. Default behaviour (no arg) is preserved; the new arg path is opt-in.
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 — operator wanted to one-shot PROJ-840 in example-capabilities-3 and had to reason about how `/next-task` would interact with example-capabilities-3's pre-existing P0/P1 queue (deep engagement-onboarding work that takes priority by ID order). Workaround: filed the bug as P1 above the larger refactors, but a Jira-key arg would have been cleaner.

- [ ] `cross-repo-runner-v1-live-spawn` — graduate the cross-repo runner from v0 (dry-run plan) to v1 (live `claude --print` spawn against the host)
  - **ID**: cross-repo-runner-v1-live-spawn
  - **Tags**: novel, cross-repo, runner, v1
  - **Estimate**: 2d
  - **Hypothesis**: `cross-repo-runner-v0` (#129) and the PROJ-840 integration test (#131) ship a *plan-only* runner — the spawn boundary is mocked, no Claude Code subprocess actually runs against the host. Two chaos rows in the v0 READMEs are deferred to this v1 task: (a) `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` row 7 — sandbox-leak detection requires the live-spawn path to be exercised; (b) `novel/sidecar-bootstrap/README.md` row 5 — read-only-ignore-file fallback exercises a real bootstrap retry. Wiring the v0 plan into a real `ProcessSpawnStrategy` (rule-#1 reuse — same Strategy `@minsky/tick-loop` already uses) closes both deferrals AND validates the umbrella user-story-006 metric (`cross_repo_runs_validated_pct`) against a live PR-shaped artefact, not a synthesised one.
  - **Details**: (a) Replace `cross-repo-runner`'s mocked spawn in `src/runner.ts` with `ProcessSpawnStrategy({ command: "claude" })` from `@minsky/tick-loop`; brief on stdin (synthesised EXPERIMENT.yaml + system-prompt overlay), response on stdout. (b) Add `--live` flag to the CLI (mirrors `MINSKY_TICK_DRY_RUN` shape from tick-loop); default stays dry-run for safety. (c) After spawn, `git diff` against host to detect scope-leak (chaos row 7); record `verdict: scope-leak` to the iteration-store on out-of-scope changes. (d) Sidecar-bootstrap retries the per-clone `.git/info/exclude` write when global ignore is read-only (chaos row 5). (e) Update the PROJ-840 integration test to assert `--live` produces a real PR (or skip when `CLAUDE_API_KEY` is unset; CI keeps the v0 dry-run path).
  - **Files**: `novel/cross-repo-runner/src/runner.ts` + `runner.test.ts`, `novel/cross-repo-runner/README.md` (chaos rows 5, 7 — replace deferred → wired), `novel/sidecar-bootstrap/src/install.ts` + tests + `README.md` (chaos row 5 update), `novel/cross-repo-runner/test/integration/proj-840-shape.test.ts` (extend with `--live` skip-when-no-key path).
  - **Verification**: `pnpm vitest run novel/cross-repo-runner novel/sidecar-bootstrap` exits 0 with the new `--live` test cases passing locally (dry-run-only mode in CI). Both README chaos rows lose their `(deferred — covered when X ships)` text and instead reference the actual test path.
  - **Measurement**: `node scripts/check-rule-7-chaos-coverage.mjs` exits 0 (today: 2 violations after `cross-repo-runner-proj-840-integration-test` task block was removed; this task closes both by either wiring the chaos coverage to a real test path or removing the deferral entirely).
  - **Pivot**: if the live-spawn path proves too costly to exercise in CI (Claude API rate limits, key management for self-hosted runners), retire the `--live` integration test and document the chaos rows as `host-substrate-deferred` (the host's own CI exercises the live path; minsky's CI gates only the synthesised plan). The v0 dry-run path remains the default so this pivot is operationally cheap.
  - **Acceptance**: `--live` flag exists; chaos rows 5 and 7 reference real test files instead of deferred tasks; user-story-006's `cross_repo_runs_validated_pct` metric has a real numerator > 0 from the PROJ-840 live-spawn run.
  - **Anchor**: Armstrong, *Programming Erlang*, Pragmatic Bookshelf, 2007 (let-it-crash discipline only works when the failure surfaces — the v0 dry-run path can't surface sandbox leaks because there's no real spawn); Basiri et al., "Principles of Chaos Engineering", *IEEE Software* 2016 (chaos coverage requires the failure axis to be exercised, not just declared); rule #1 (don't reinvent — reuse `ProcessSpawnStrategy`); rule #7 (failure-mode table needs real chaos tests, not deferral chains).
  - **Risk**: live-spawn against a host repo can write tracked files; mitigation is the existing `git diff` post-spawn boundary plus `--live` opt-in (default stays dry-run).
  - **Surfaced-by**: 2026-05-04 sweep PR #132 — `chore: sweep closed task blocks` removed `cross-repo-runner-proj-840-integration-test` (shipped #131) and the rule-7-chaos-coverage lint surfaced two README rows whose deferral target no longer existed. Filing this v1 follow-up converts the dangling deferrals into a real future-task reference.
